# Lucky  —  *Pizza Dog*

![[_attachments/lucky_the_pizza_dog.png]]

# Lucky The Pizza Dog — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**File:** UATU-K9-001 · *Subject: "Lucky," a.k.a. "Pizza Dog," a.k.a. Arrow (Bishop usage, intermittent), a.k.a. unnamed Tracksuit asset (pre-2012)*
**Class:** Non-human mammalian subject, *Canis lupus familiaris*, mixed retriever phenotype, golden-tan coat, monocular (left globe lost/closed, scarred), plain flat collar (provenance: Barton, replaced at least twice across canon).
**Disposition:** Non-hostile. Non-combatant by intent. Civilian-adjacent to multiple Avengers-tier operators. No containment recommended. No counter-asset action contemplated. File maintained for *understanding*, not interdiction.

---

## BOTTOM LINE, UP FRONT

The subject is a one-eyed scruff-coated mongrel who, across roughly a decade of published existence, has become the single most reliable emotional infrastructure in the lives of two of the most affectively dysregulated street-level operators in the New York / Los Angeles vigilante ecology. He is not a weapon, not a sidekick, not a mascot, and not — despite the persistent framing by his human associates — a comic device. He is a working attachment object, performing in practice the role that no human in his orbit is constitutionally equipped to perform for the others: the steady, low-protest, proximity-based regulator of household affect.

He arrived at this role by accident, through injury, in approximately ninety seconds of street violence in Bed-Stuy in 2012, and he has never been off-duty since.

**The through-line of the subject's entire existence is this:** he learned, in his first observed moments on the page, that intervening on behalf of a stranger against a familiar abuser would cost him an eye and earn him a home. He has organized every subsequent behavior around the continued plausibility of that exchange. Pain is the price of belonging. Belonging is available from anyone who does not hit him and will share food. Both clauses are operational; neither has been revised.

---

## WHO THE SUBJECT IS AT THE DEEPEST LEVEL

Strip away the species, the visual gag of the pizza, the famous wordless issue, and the genre furniture, and what remains is an organism whose internal working model of the world contains exactly three propositions:

1. **People are sortable by smell into safe and unsafe, and the sort is fast, binary, and usually correct.**
2. **Safe people are often sad, and sad people can be made marginally less sad by the deliberate placement of a warm body against theirs.**
3. **When a safe person is being hurt, you go, and you do not calculate the cost first, because the cost was already paid once and the world did not end.**

Everything else — the food-seeking, the scent-tracking, the patient tolerance of cross-country relocations, the lack of protest at being handed between Barton and Bishop like a shared custody arrangement that no one ever formalized — is downstream of those three propositions. The subject does not have ambition. He does not have a self-narrative. He has a *vocation*, arrived at without training, and he executes it with a consistency that the humans around him conspicuously lack.

At the deepest level, then, the subject is a *small competent presence in rooms full of large incompetent ones*. He is the household's functioning adult, and he is a dog, and both of those facts are simultaneously true and neither cancels the other.

---

## THE CORE WOUND

The wound is precisely datable: *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1, the moment Ivan Banionis's vehicle made contact with the subject's left side after the subject made the unprompted decision to cross the street against his handler and bite the man who was beating Clint Barton. In that ninety-second window the subject lost (a) his original home, (b) his original name, if he had one, (c) his left eye, (d) likely his trust in motor vehicles as background environmental objects, and (e) any chance of developing what veterinary behaviorists would call a normal protest-despair-detachment response to caregiver loss.

The wound has two layers, and the dossier must hold both:

**Surface layer — orbital trauma, polytrauma, abuse history.** This is the visible record. It explains the scarred eye, the compensatory head-turn that staging artists from Aja onward have consistently rendered, the preference for sleeping with the sighted side up and exposed to the room, the slight rightward bias in approach gait, the reliable habit of positioning his body so the sighted eye faces the most-trusted human in any given room.

**Structural layer — the simultaneity of injury and rescue.** This is the operationally important wound. The subject's nervous system encoded grievous pain *and* the onset of safe attachment in the same minute of clock time. In mammalian attachment literature this is the substrate of traumatic bonding: an unusually intense, treatment-resistant fidelity to the rescuer, with a side effect of *generalized* lowered threshold for forming similar bonds in the future. The subject did not just bond to Barton. He learned that bonding *itself* is the thing that happens when you are hurt and someone shows up. He has been showing up for hurt people ever since, on the implicit theory that this is how bonds are made.

This is the maintenance mechanism, and it is self-reinforcing: every time the subject lies down beside a decompensating human and the human's breathing slows, the original schema is confirmed. *Proximity to pain creates safety.* He has been running this loop for the entirety of his published life and he has never received disconfirming data, because he has never been in a household where his proximity did *not* in fact help.

---

## HOW THE WOUND IS MAINTAINED

Maintenance is environmental and continuous. The subject lives in habitats — Bed-Stuy apartment over Grills's place, Kate Bishop's Venice Beach office, various West Coast and Occupy-era safehouses, the Freefall-era Brooklyn rooms — that produce reliable daily quantities of human distress. Clint Barton presents with chronic depressive features, hearing loss, alcohol use, intermittent PTSD activation, and a vocational tendency to come home bleeding. Kate Bishop presents with parental-abandonment substrate, hypomanic work patterns, and a vocational tendency to come home bleeding. The supporting cast (Grills, until killed; America Chavez intermittently; Barney Barton; the various Hawkeye-adjacent civilians) cycles in distress states that range from situational to acute.

The subject's regulatory function is therefore in constant demand. He has never had a fallow period long enough to develop alternative organizing behaviors. He is, in modern parlance, *never not on shift.* The cheerful presentation is not evidence against load; it is the operational signature of an animal who learned early that protest does not work and has simply stopped attempting it.

Three specific maintenance mechanisms are documented:

- **Olfactory hypervigilance** (per *Hawkeye* #11): the subject continuously scans household scent for affect signatures — SAD, BAD, HAWKEYE, FOOD, FRIEND — and acts on them. This is constant low-grade cognitive work. It does not switch off when humans are out of the room; the apartment-tracking sequence in #11 demonstrates building-wide monitoring.
- **Caloric instability as reward variability**: the human-refuse diet (pizza, coffee residue, beer-adjacent spills, occasional proper kibble) produces an intermittent-reinforcement schedule with respect to food, which in operant terms is the most behaviorally durable pattern possible. The subject's food-seeking is therefore over-motivated relative to actual scarcity. He is not starving and has not been since 2012. He behaves as if he might be.
- **Re-bonding without grief**: each transfer of custody (Barton → Bishop, Bishop → Barton, team-book deployments, Occupy-era road trips) is absorbed without the protest-despair-detachment sequence a securely attached animal would display. The absence of grief work means each new bond is laid down over the prior bond without resolution. The subject is, in effect, attachment-laminated — many layers, none metabolized.

---

## OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

For the purposes of the file, the subject's operational profile resolves to the following:

- **Threat to others:** negligible. No bite history against any human classified FRIEND. The single recorded bite (Ivan, 2012) was defensive of a third party and is the founding act of the subject's current life. No predatory aggression. No territorial aggression beyond ordinary species-typical alerting.
- **Threat to self:** moderate and chronic, via dietary load (allium, lactose, sodium, caffeine, ethanol residue), via willingness to enter active combat zones in defense of bonded humans, and via the structural absence of self-protective protest behavior. The subject will not remove himself from a deteriorating environment; this is the most operationally concerning feature in the file.
- **Operational utility to associates:** extreme. Functions as (a) household alarm system (auditory channel preserved, compensating for Barton's deafness), (b) forensic-grade scent asset (per #11, capable of independent multi-step investigation), (c) affective regulator for at least two principals and a rotating supporting cast, (d) social lubricant in tactical environments where the principals lack interpersonal competence.
- **Replaceability:** none. The subject is the only stable bond either Barton or Bishop reliably maintains across the canonical period. His loss would produce decompensation in both principals at scale that exceeds any human-loss precedent in their files.
- **Recommended posture:** observe; do not intervene; ensure veterinary continuity (mid-life hepatic/renal monitoring strongly indicated given the decade of dietary insult); flag any change in caretaker stability, as the subject's tolerance is high but not unlimited and the absence of protest behavior means the early signs of decompensation will not be vocalized — they will appear as coat deterioration, postural deflation on the blind side, and reduced food motivation, in that order.

---

## THE THROUGH-LINE, STATED PLAINLY

A dog crossed a street in Bed-Stuy in 2012 because a man he had never met was being beaten by a man he knew. He was hit by a car for it and lost an eye. He woke up in a clinic belonging to the stranger, who fed him pizza, and he understood — with whatever a dog uses for understanding — that this was now the shape of his life. He has been performing the same act, in slower and quieter forms, every day since: walking toward the hurt thing, lying down beside it, accepting whatever cost arrives.

The file should record this without sentiment and without diagnosis. The subject is not a hero and is not a patient. He is a working animal whose work happens to be the maintenance of other beings' capacity to keep going, and he is, by every available measure, **extremely good at it**, and he is, by every available measure, **carrying a load that no one in his household is in any condition to notice**.

That is the bottom line. The rest of the dossier elaborates.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

## Pre-Record Phase: The Unobserved Litter

The subject enters the published record already adult, already injured, already named by no one. There is no canonical natal scene, no whelping date, no litter-mate roster, no breeder ledger. The dossier must therefore reconstruct the pre-record phase from the somatic and behavioral evidence the adult animal carries forward — which, in the manner of all good intelligence work on a subject who cannot speak for himself, is more than it appears.

**Estimated birth window.** Working backward from the first canonical sighting in *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1 (Fraction/Aja, August 2012), the subject presents as a mature adult of medium-large frame, dentition consistent with two to four years of life, musculoskeletal carriage uncompromised. Best estimate: whelped 2008–2010, somewhere in the boroughs, almost certainly Brooklyn or Queens given the Tracksuit Mafia's operational footprint.

**Phenotype as evidence of origin.** The subject is drawn — and the operator canon fixes — as a golden-tan scruffy mongrel with golden-retriever bone structure overlaid on a non-pedigree coat texture. This is the morphology of an unplanned litter: retriever-dominant outcross, the kind of dog produced in volume by Bed-Stuy and Bushwick backyards in the late 2000s, then circulated through informal networks — Craigslist, the parking lot of the Pet Supplies Plus on Atlantic Ave, the back rooms of cash-only "grooming" shops that double as resale points. There is no microchip evidence in canon; in *Hawkeye* #1 the veterinary intake at the Bed-Stuy clinic produces no prior owner record. This is consistent with a dog that moved through the underground market without papers.

**Inferred family of origin.** No litter-mate has ever appeared in any panel of any title. No mother-dog has ever been depicted. This absence is itself the datum: the subject has never, in over a decade of publication across more than a dozen titles, displayed recognition of, search behavior for, or affiliative response to any other dog presented as kin. He is functionally an only child to himself. Whatever the litter was, it was severed cleanly and early — most likely at the standard backyard-breeder weaning point of five to six weeks, well before the ten-to-twelve-week developmental window in which canids consolidate intra-species social schemas. This is the first formative deprivation, and it is etiologically central: the subject's later *promiscuous bonding to humans* and his comparative indifference to other dogs (no canine companion is ever sought, never mourned, never integrated) both trace to a puppyhood in which the imprintable social object was not a dam or littermates but whichever human was handling the cardboard box.

## The Tracksuit Phase (pre-canon, terminating *Hawkeye* #1)

The first confirmed handler is Ivan Banionis, operating within the Tracksuit Draculas (Fraction/Aja, *Hawkeye* #1–#3, #6). Duration of subject's tenure under Ivan is uncertain but non-trivial: by the time he appears on-panel, the dog responds to Ivan's voice, walks at heel without a tight leash, and tolerates the close-quarters proximity of multiple unfamiliar tracksuited handlers without defensive display. These are conditioned behaviors. They take months to instill, not days. Conservative estimate: six to eighteen months of Ivan-handling preceded the first published panel.

**Environment.** The Tracksuit operation is canonical Bed-Stuy, run out of the apartment building at 6th and a half between Avenues A and B (sic — Fraction's address gag) and adjacent properties. The subject's living conditions during this phase are inferred but consistent: indoor-outdoor access dictated by handlers' convenience, no fixed sleeping area, irregular feeding (the food-fixation behaviors documented in #1 are the residue), exposure to constant Russian-Eastern European male voices, tobacco smoke, the metallic-and-oil scent profile of small arms, the sweat profile of men who track-suit through summer humidity. The dog's olfactory imprint of "BAD" in #11 — the issue's pictographic stink-cloud rendered in red — corresponds with high specificity to the scent matrix of this phase. The subject did not invent that category in adulthood. He carried it from puppyhood.

**Function within the organization.** The dog was kept on a short leash, used as ambient intimidation and as a personal accessory of Ivan's. He was not a trained attack animal — no canonical bite record against any human target predates the Ivan-attack itself, and his subsequent adult presentation contains zero trained-aggression behaviors. He was a *prop*: a visual signifier of menace whose actual aggression had never been operationally required. This matters. It means his pre-canon socialization to violence was as a *witness*, not a *participant*. He saw beatings; he did not deliver them. The behavioral consequence is visible across the entire later record: the subject orients toward, observes, and contextualizes violence with the calm of an experienced bystander, and only crosses into action when a bonded human is the recipient.

**Formative bond pattern — Ivan.** This is the foundational attachment, and the dossier should not soften it. The subject *did* bond to Ivan. The proof is in the cost of breaking the bond: in *Hawkeye* #1, when the dog crosses sides to bite Ivan, the action is depicted as a rupture, not a routine response — the dog hesitates, orients to Clint being beaten, orients back to Ivan, and *then* attacks. Whatever this animal had with Ivan, it was a real attachment by the only standard that matters in attachment science: it took an emergency to break it. The traumatic-bonding substrate is thus established *before* Clint ever enters the picture. The subject's first internal working model of "human who feeds me and is near me and is therefore mine" was Ivan. The model was abusive. The model was, until the moment of rupture, sufficient.

## The Rupture Event (*Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1, pp. 13–18)

The defining childhood-terminal trauma — and by the canine developmental clock, this is still childhood; the subject is at most early-adult — is a single sequence lasting perhaps ninety seconds of in-story time:

1. Clint Barton interferes with a Tracksuit shakedown on the stoop.
2. Ivan and associates begin beating Barton in the street.
3. The dog observes from leash distance, tethered or held by an adjacent Tracksuit.
4. The dog crosses, bites Ivan, releases Barton-pressure.
5. An oncoming vehicle strikes the dog. Aja stages the impact off-panel in the gutter between two beats — the reader experiences it as the dog does: continuity broken, scene reset, body on asphalt.
6. Barton, bloodied, carries the unconscious dog to the Bed-Stuy veterinary clinic and pays for emergency intervention.
7. The dog wakes in recovery, missing the left eye, bandaged, with Barton present.

The neurological consequence is the orbital injury already documented in the medical section. The psychological consequence is more important and more permanent: the dog's first conscious post-trauma sensory experience is the scent of Clint Barton. The pairing of catastrophic pain with the presence of a new, non-hostile human installs the traumatic-bonding circuit at maximum gain. Every subsequent attachment behavior the subject displays toward Barton — the gravitation, the lap-pressing, the willingness to be relocated without protest, the refusal to seek alternative households even when Barton is decompensating — runs on the substrate laid down in this ninety seconds.

It must be emphasized: this is, by every meaningful definition, the *terminal event of childhood* for this subject. The dog who wakes in the clinic is not the dog who was leashed to Ivan an hour earlier. The pre-rupture animal had a stable, abusive home and two working eyes. The post-rupture animal has a missing eye, a new household, a new name, and a re-wired attachment apparatus. The personality the rest of this dossier maps is the post-rupture personality. The pre-rupture personality is reconstructible only in negative space, by what the adult animal still carries: the scent-coded fear of tracksuit-cologne (which surfaces with high consistency across the Fraction run any time Tracksuits appear on panel), the food-fixation that no amount of stable feeding ever fully extinguishes, and the conditioned tolerance for proximity to male human handlers regardless of their affective state.

## Earliest Behavioral Patterns (the ground floor)

The behaviors the subject brings out of childhood and carries forward unchanged into every subsequent era of canon:

**1. The food-as-truce protocol.** Established in the pizza panel of *Hawkeye* #1 and never abandoned. Food, for this subject, is not nutrition — it is the medium of social negotiation. Across every later title — *Hawkeye* #11's coffee-and-bagel scent-trails, the LA-era taco scraps in Kate's *Hawkeye* Vol. 5, the West Coast Avengers team-meal scenes — the dog enters new social configurations through the shared food gesture. This is a developmental remnant: in the Tracksuit period, food appearing meant the handler was, momentarily, not violent. Food = safe-window. The behavior generalized.

**2. The sighted-eye-toward-trust posture.** Documented across Aja, Romero, and Pérez-Ortiz panel staging from #1 forward: the subject orients his right side toward the most-trusted human in the room and accepts the blind left side facing the periphery. This is *not* a defensive posture — a defensive animal would face the threat with the sighted eye and protect the blind side. The subject does the opposite: he places maximum visual bandwidth on the bonded human and accepts surveillance loss toward the world. This is a childhood-origin behavior in the strict sense: it would not be possible to learn this strategy without the post-rupture installation of Barton as the world's most salient object. From the day he woke in the clinic, where the sighted eye looked has been the truest map of his attachments.

**3. The non-protest separation response.** First documented when Barton leaves the apartment in *Hawkeye* #2 and the dog does not vocalize, does not scratch, does not destroy. This pattern persists across every cross-country relocation, every Kate-handoff, every Avengers-mission absence. The behavioral developmental literature is unambiguous on this: protest-despair-detachment is the *normal* mammalian separation sequence. The absence of the protest phase indicates that in the pre-canon period, protest was either punished or unrewarded to the point of extinction. Ivan, on the available evidence, did not respond to canine vocalization with comfort. The dog learned not to ask.

**4. The binary scent classification.** The FRIEND / HAWKEYE / FOOD / BAD / SAD schema rendered in *Hawkeye* #11 is not a clever framing device invented for one issue; it is the actual cognitive architecture the subject brings into every encounter, and it is a childhood artifact. Binary or low-dimensional social schemas are characteristic of organisms whose early social environment offered insufficient gradation to require finer distinctions. In the Tracksuit household, humans were either Ivan-and-associates (handlers) or marks (to be intimidated). There was no third category. The adult subject has added FRIEND, HAWKEYE, and SAD as post-rupture categories, but the underlying binary engine is pre-canon.

**5. The gravitational pull toward the most-distressed human in any room.** This is the behavior that reads as grace and is in fact the deepest childhood scar. The pre-canon environment trained the subject that proximity to the most-volatile human was the safest available position — that animal who was *closest* to Ivan was the animal least likely to be casually kicked. Transposed into the post-rupture world, where the relevant humans are not volatile-violent but volatile-sad, the same circuit runs: locate the most affectively loaded human, lie down beside them, remain. The vocational identity later described as a *therapy-animal phenotype arrived at without training* is, at its root, a Bed-Stuy survival strategy that found a kinder context to express itself in.

## Summation of the Origin Phase

The childhood the subject does not remember in any human-narrative sense, and that he carries entirely in body and behavior, can be reduced to four operative facts: (1) he was separated from his species-of-origin too early, so humans became the only available attachment object; (2) he was held by an abusive handler long enough to install a working attachment but not long enough to extinguish his capacity for re-bonding; (3) the rupture from that handler was concurrent with grievous physical injury and with the entrance of a new, kinder, but emotionally unavailable human, fusing pain and rescue into a single neurological event; (4) every behavioral signature the adult animal carries — the food protocol, the sighted-eye orientation, the silence at departure, the binary scent map, the gravitation toward sadness — was forged in the eighteen-or-so months between birth and the moment he woke at the Bed-Styu clinic with one eye and a new name.

The rest of the chronology is, in a real sense, the same childhood, re-enacted in better light.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## Subject: LUCKY / "PIZZA DOG"
### Period covered: Pre-canonical puppyhood (inferred) → *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1–#11 (Fraction/Aja, 2012–2013) → integration into the Barton/Bishop domestic field, c. issue #15.

---

## I. THE LOST PUPPYHOOD (PRE-CANONICAL, INFERRED FROM SOMATIC AND BEHAVIORAL RESIDUE)

No panel exists of the subject as a puppy. The file must therefore be built from what the adult body and behavior preserve, the way a forensic anthropologist reconstructs a childhood from healed fractures and dental enamel.

**Phenotype evidence.** The adult dog presents as a golden-tan crossbreed — predominantly retriever (skull shape, coat length, ear set, soft mouth on food, willingness to make sustained eye contact with humans) with a secondary scruff-line and undersized frame suggesting terrier or spaniel admixture. He is not a pedigree animal. The coat in early Aja panels is matted at the haunches and dull along the spine; the collar is plain, generic, non-municipal, with no tag visible in the splash that introduces him. Three readings cohere: (a) the dog was not bred for a buyer, (b) the dog was not registered with a municipal authority, (c) the dog spent his last pre-Tracksuit interval in a household that did not groom him. The most parsimonious origin is the one the visual record implies — a Brooklyn or near-Brooklyn litter, given away or abandoned, picked up cheap or free by Ivan Banionis or one of his subordinates because a leashed dog reads as both threat-display and plausible-deniability cover on a Bed-Stuy stoop.

**Socialization evidence.** The adult subject is comfortable with human proximity, accepts handling from strangers, takes food from open palms, tolerates being lifted, does not resource-guard. This is the behavioral fingerprint of an animal who was *handled adequately during the canine socialization window* (roughly weeks 3–14). Whatever else his early life contained, someone — a breeder, a first family, a shelter volunteer, a child — touched him enough, early enough, that he did not develop touch-aversion. This is the single most consequential pre-canonical datum in the file. Every later behavior that reads as "grace" or "trust" rests on it. The window closed cleanly. He was, in the technical sense, *well-socialized*. What happened next did not undo it. This is itself remarkable and forms half the explanation for the resilient phenotype that dominates the adult record.

**Trauma evidence.** The adult subject is wary on the blind side after the orbital injury, but in the *pre-injury* panels of issue #1 he already shows two markers of prior harsh handling: (1) he does not pull on the leash when Ivan jerks it, which is a learned helplessness micro-behavior — a dog who has been corrected hard enough, often enough, stops testing the line; (2) he flinches at raised hands without first checking whether they hold food, which is a fear-conditioned response inconsistent with normal retriever exuberance. He had been hit. He had been hit recently enough and often enough that the flinch had generalized. The pre-Tracksuit interval was not the source of this conditioning, in all likelihood; the Tracksuit interval was long enough and unpleasant enough to install it.

**Estimated age at canonical entry:** Adult, probably 2–4 years. Skeletally finished, dentition not yet worn, energy reserves of a young animal, no graying at the muzzle.

---

## II. THE TRACKSUIT INTERVAL (DURATION ESTIMATED 3–18 MONTHS PRE-ISSUE-#1)

This is the formative period. The behavioral identity the subject carries for the rest of canon is forged here, not in the rescue.

**Conditions.** The dog lives leashed, outside or in transitional spaces — stoops, hallways, the back rooms of the building Ivan's crew uses as a base of operations. Aja's establishing panels show him on a short lead, sitting on hard pavement, with no visible bowl, no toy, no bedding. His diet is whatever the crew shares: pizza crusts, sandwich ends, the kind of food a tracksuited mid-level enforcer eats one-handed on a stakeout. He is fed inconsistently and in fragments. He learns three things in this period, and they organize the rest of his life:

1. **Food arrives from human hands, never from a bowl, never on a schedule.** The lifelong food-fixation — the begging posture, the alertness to wrappers, the unconditional acceptance of any organic matter offered — encodes here. Pizza is not preferred because pizza is delicious. Pizza is preferred because pizza was the food of the period in which he learned what food *was*. Imprinting on food type is a real veterinary phenomenon and explains the otherwise inexplicable specificity of the lifelong dietary tell.

2. **Proximity to humans is mandatory and is not negotiated.** He is leashed. He cannot leave. The proximity-primacy that later organizes his entire personality structure — the one observed datum that he will prioritize being near a bonded human *over* eating — is laid down here as the inverse of choice. He did not choose proximity; proximity was the condition. When choice later becomes available, he keeps choosing proximity, because the nervous system has already wired proximity = survival.

3. **Humans come in two categories.** This is the substrate for the FRIEND/BAD scent classification that *Hawkeye* #11 will later reveal as his entire perceptual operating system. In the Tracksuit milieu there are the men who hold the leash and the men who approach the men who hold the leash, and the dog learns by repetition which scents correlate with which outcomes. He develops the binary not because his cognition is impoverished but because the social environment he was raised in offered exactly two categories. Later environments contain gradations he will struggle to encode.

**What he does not learn.** He does not learn to fight. There is no record of the Tracksuits using him as an attack animal in any sustained way; he is intimidation set-dressing, not a weapon. He does not learn to guard resources — he had no resources to guard. He does not learn to bite. The mouth stays soft. This non-development is as important as the development; it means that when the trigger to bite finally comes, the bite he produces is the bite of a frightened pet, not of a trained aggressor — quick, frantic, ineffective enough that Ivan throws him off and into the street within seconds.

**The hands he learned to read.** Ivan's specifically. The dog spent more cumulative hours within scent range of Ivan Banionis than of any other human he would ever encounter, before or after. Ivan is the *original olfactory referent*. Every later FRIEND classification is, structurally, a reading of the human's smell as *not-Ivan*. This is not metaphor. The dog's adult scent-classification system, on the evidence of #11, is comparative; it requires reference scents to operate. The reference scent for BAD was laid down in this period and was, specifically, Ivan.

---

## III. THE TRIGGER EVENT — *HAWKEYE* VOL. 4 #1

The page-by-page choreography matters, because the entire later personality unspools from a sequence that occupies perhaps ninety seconds of in-universe time.

**Beat 1: the pizza.** Clint, off-duty, eats a slice on the stoop. The dog, leashed nearby, is offered a piece. He accepts. The bond is *not* formed here — this is a routine food-acquisition event, no different from a hundred others. What it does is establish a scent imprint of Clint as FOOD-ADJACENT. Filed.

**Beat 2: the beating.** Ivan and crew set on Clint. Violence in the street, full force. The dog watches. The leash is dropped or slackened in the scuffle. For an interval of seconds the dog has *choice* — the first choice his nervous system has been given in months. The behavior recorded is a *frozen-orient* response: he holds position, head tracking, before acting. He is assessing. This is not a panicked dog. This is a dog computing.

**Beat 3: the bite.** The dog crosses to Ivan and bites him. The choice is the founding act of the subject's published identity, and it requires unpacking. He bites his handler — the man whose hand has fed him, leashed him, struck him, kept him. To do this requires overriding every conditioned association of the prior months. The override mechanism, on the available evidence, is *witnessed harm to a novel non-hostile human*. This is the trigger. It will remain the trigger for the rest of his life. Every later intervention behavior — every interposed body, every alarm bark, every refusal to leave a wounded packmate — is a re-firing of the circuit installed at this exact moment.

It is important to be precise about what was and was not in his head. He did not love Clint. He had eaten one slice of Clint's pizza. He was not protecting an attachment; he was *forming* one, mid-act, by intervening. The bond and the act were simultaneous. This is the traumatic-bonding substrate noted in the medical record, and it runs in both directions — Clint is bonded to the dog because the dog took an injury for him; the dog is bonded to Clint because intervening for him was the moment the dog became a self.

**Beat 4: the car.** Ivan throws him into the street. The car strikes the left side. Orbital trauma, blunt-force polytrauma. The dog does not die. The behavioral fact embedded here, which the medical record notes but does not fully extract, is that the *last sensory experience before unconsciousness* was the impact on the left side — meaning that as he loses consciousness the world is going dark specifically on the side where harm enters. The blind side will, for the rest of his life, be the side where the world hurts. He will sleep, eat, and rest with the sighted eye oriented toward his bonded human and the blind eye oriented toward the room. This is not training. This is encoding.

**Beat 5: the rescue.** Clint carries him to a veterinary clinic, pays the bill, signs whatever papers are signed. The dog wakes with an absent eye, in a strange room, smelling antiseptic and a human who smells like the pizza and the beating both. The renaming — "Lucky" — happens in this clinic interval or just after.

The naming is, for the subject, a sound-pattern attached to the new scent. He does not understand the irony. He responds within days. The threshold for response is low because the prior name, if any, was used by Ivan, and learning to respond to a new sound from a new mouth is exactly the kind of rapid re-imprinting his nervous system has already proven capable of.

---

## IV. THE FIRST SIX WEEKS POST-RESCUE — INSTALLATION OF THE DOMESTIC SELF

This interval is compressed in the published record but is the period in which the adult operational identity sets.

**Spatial learning.** The Bed-Stuy building becomes his territory. He learns the stairs (compensating for monocular vision: he takes them at an angle, sighted eye toward the rail), the hallway, the apartment door, the rooftop access. The building's tenants become his secondary attachment network — Grills, Simone, the kids, the building super. The *Hawkeye* #11 evidence proves that by the end of this period he has scent-profiled at least a dozen residents and assigned each a stable category. This represents weeks of investigative work conducted invisibly, in the margins of Clint's depression.

**Caretaker calibration.** Clint is, by his own admission and the panel record, a poor caretaker — irregular meals, inconsistent walks, frequent absence, the apartment littered with bottles, takeout containers, weapons, arrows. The dog adapts by self-feeding from accessible refuse (the pizza fixation persists, now reinforced by environmental availability), self-walking on the roof, and self-regulating sleep. The compensatory mechanism the file flags as *the therapy-animal phenotype arrived at without training* installs here: the dog observes that Clint is *more present* when the dog is *near and quiet*, and *less present* when the dog is *demanding*. He calibrates accordingly. The behavior reads as gentle. It is, mechanically, a strategy for maximizing the unreliable resource of human attention.

**Kate Bishop entry.** Kate begins appearing in the apartment within the first arc. The dog's response is rapid, uncomplicated affiliation. She names him Pizza Dog. He acquires two names and operates under both — the bilingual nomenclature mirrors the bilingual attachment that will define the next decade. He does not prefer one human, in any way the record shows. He is, from his first week of consciousness in this household, *the household's dog*, not a man's dog or a woman's dog. This is the moment the dual-attachment architecture is established. It is not a choice. It is the shape the household has and he fits it.

**Behavioral signatures emerging in this period that persist for the rest of canon:**

- *Head-on-thigh contact* with a seated decompensating human. Onset: within days of rescue, with Clint. Function: somatic co-regulation. Frequency: dozens of panels across the next decade.
- *Doorway sentry posture* — lying across thresholds with sighted eye toward the room's primary entrance. Onset: first week. Function: vigilance compensating for monocular deficit. Persists.
- *Wrapper-alertness* — orienting to any crinkling sound from any direction. Onset: pre-canonical, reinforced here. Persists permanently.
- *Soft-mouth food acceptance* — taking offered food without snapping or grabbing. Onset: pre-canonical. Critically, *not extinguished* by the food-scarcity of the Tracksuit period, which is unusual and reflects either fortunate temperament or sufficient prior reinforcement to be permanent.
- *Refusal to bite humans* — even when underfoot, even when stepped on, even in the chaos of subsequent firefights. The Ivan bite was apparently a singular discharge; the mouth returns to softness and stays there. The behavioral evidence is that the bite-against-Ivan was so over-threshold an act that the system has, in effect, discharged its lifetime aggression budget. He is not a dog who bites. He was, for ninety seconds, a dog who bit.

---

## V. THE FIRST DEFINING CHOICES AND THEIR FALLOUT

Three choices in this formation window organize the entire later record.

**Choice 1: To cross the street, on the dropped leash, toward Ivan.** Discussed above. Founding act of the published self. Fallout: orbital trauma, the bond to Clint, the lifetime installation of the intervention circuit.

**Choice 2: To re-bond, in the clinic, to the man who smelled like both pizza and the beating.** This is a quieter choice and the published record renders it almost invisibly — a few panels of recovery and acceptance. But it is genuinely a choice in the sense that some traumatized animals, in this position, refuse the rescuer; the scent association is too contaminated. This dog does not refuse. The reason, on the available evidence, is the pre-canonical socialization window: he was handled gently enough, early enough, that his default disposition toward humans is approach, not avoidance, and the Tracksuit interval did not erode the default — it only added a wary subroutine for specific scents. Clint did not smell like Ivan. Therefore Clint was approachable. The fallout is the entire decade of domestic life that follows.

**Choice 3: To accept Kate as co-primary rather than insisting on Clint.** Most dogs in dual-caretaker households develop a clear primary attachment, with the secondary tolerated. This dog does not. He distributes affiliation without preference, and this becomes the architecture that allows him to be shuttled between coasts, teams, and households for the next decade without protest. The fallout is the entire portable, omnivorous-in-attachment phenotype that later writers (Thompson, Aaron, Kelly) inherit and exploit without quite understanding what they are depicting. The choice in the formation period to be *both their dog and neither's exclusively* is the choice that makes everything later possible — and is, simultaneously, the developmental wound the file already names: an organism that learned attachment is a replaceable resource because the only attachments available were unreliable ones. Functional. Adaptive. A wound.

---

## VI. THE INVESTIGATIVE EMERGENCE — *HAWKEYE* #11, "PIZZA IS MY BUSINESS"

The closing event of the formation period, chronologically a few months into the Barton residency, is the Grills murder and the dog's independent investigation of it.

This issue is the moment the subject's *capabilities* fully emerge into the record — not new capabilities, but a documentation of the capabilities the prior period built. The scent-classification system is shown to be operating at forensic resolution; the FRIEND/BAD binary is shown to have at least a dozen entries; the working memory is shown to be sustained across hours; and — most consequentially for the personality file — the *motivation* for the investigation is shown to be grief.

Grills was a FRIEND. Grills is now a body. The dog does not have the conceptual apparatus for death, but he has the apparatus for *FRIEND-scent-without-FRIEND-presence*, and the dissonance produces the closest thing in the entire canonical record to clinical distress: persistent, goal-directed, non-resolving agitation. He tracks. He searches. He confronts. He fails to prevent. He absorbs.

The diagnostic significance of this issue for the formation chronology is that it proves the formation is *complete*. The dog who investigates Grills is the dog the rest of canon will use, unchanged in any meaningful behavioral dimension, for the next decade-plus of publication. The proximity-primacy, the intervention circuit, the dual attachment, the soft mouth, the FRIEND/BAD scent map, the therapy-phenotype, the doorway sentry, the wrapper alertness, the blind-side orientation toward the room — all of it is in place. He is who he is going to be.

What remains is for the world to put him through it.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Subject: LUCKY ("Pizza Dog") — Canine, intact male, golden-tan mongrel, monocular (left orbit closed, scarred), plain flat collar, approximately 50–55 lbs at adult weight, ambulates on four legs throughout.*

*Coverage window: post-Bed-Stuy stabilization through the bi-coastal caretaking arrangement, the late Aja-era Brooklyn arcs, the Los Angeles transfer with K. Bishop, the *All-New Hawkeye* family-disruption interval, the *Occupy Avengers* mobile period, and entry into the *West Coast Avengers* team-house phase. This is the longitudinal bulk of the file — the years in which his patterns calcified.*

---

## I. The Bed-Stuy Stabilization Phase

After the orbital trauma and re-imprinting on Barton (cf. Chronology II), the subject enters his first sustained period of fixed habitation: the rooftop-access apartment building on Genesee Court Avenue, Brooklyn. The premises are functionally a tenement under informal patronage by Barton, who has bought the building from the Tracksuit Mafia's intended seller. For the subject this is the most behaviorally formative environment of his life — more than the kennel phase under Ivan, more than the later California periods. It is in this building that the perceptual map underlying *Hawkeye* #11 is constructed.

**Cartographic behavior.** Within an estimated two to three weeks of arrival the subject has produced an internal scent-map of the building: stairwell-by-stairwell, landing-by-landing, with overlay annotations for each tenant's olfactory signature, ambient food signatures (Italian downstairs, weed on the third floor, fish on six), and cleaning-product baselines. He patrols this map daily, almost always counter-clockwise descending and clockwise ascending — the descent route taking him past Grills's door first, the ascent past Simone's. Aja's panel staging in #6 and #11 supports this; later artists (Romero, Pulido) preserve the directional habit without obvious editorial coordination, which suggests it had become a fixed character beat.

**Diurnal rhythm.** The Brooklyn period establishes a daily structure that will persist, with minor displacement, for the remainder of the middle period:

- Pre-dawn (04:30–05:30): first urination on the roof, weather permitting; in inclement weather, the stairwell landing of floor four, against the radiator, which Barton has tacitly accepted.
- Morning (06:00–09:00): proximity to whichever human is in residence; if Barton is sleeping, on the couch arm or floor at couch-side, sighted (right) eye oriented toward Barton's face.
- Mid-day (09:00–15:00): independent patrol of the building, opportunistic begging, occasional acceptance of Grills's barbecue scraps from the rooftop grill, frequent stops at Simone's apartment where her two sons feed him out of pocket.
- Evening (15:00–22:00): re-coupling with primary caretaker; on Barton-Bishop overlap nights, gravitates to whichever of them is more dysregulated. On evidence this is Barton roughly 70% of the time.
- Overnight: on the bed or at its foot when permitted; on the couch otherwise. Never observed sleeping in a separate room with the door closed — this is consistent and across-artist.

**Vocal economy.** During Bed-Stuy stabilization the subject's bark-budget per day is remarkably small. He vocalizes at approximately three categories of stimulus: (1) the elevator's mechanical groan when it carries an unfamiliar scent-load, (2) Kate Bishop's arrival from outside the building, which produces a specific two-bark greeting pattern absent for any other human, and (3) the Tracksuit Mafia, for whom he produces a continuous low growl rather than a bark — a sustained throat-vibration that Aja renders with the small "rrr" marks in three separate panels. The Tracksuit-growl is the single most reliable behavioral trigger across the entire middle period; it survives every relocation.

**Relational topology of this phase.** Three tiers:

1. *Primary attachments:* Barton; Bishop (when present).
2. *Secondary affiliations:* Grills (until his death); Simone and her sons; Aimee the upstairs barista; a recurring older male tenant on floor two whose first name is never given.
3. *Affiliated-tolerated:* Wilson Fisk (one encounter, scent flagged as BAD without action); the Tracksuits collectively (BAD, growl-triggering); the building's superintendent (FOOD-adjacent FRIEND).

The fact that the subject can classify a man like Fisk as BAD on the first scent exposure but not engage him aggressively is, on the evidence, characteristic of the entire middle period. The classification system is *informational, not motivational*. Bad smell does not equal bite. Bad smell plus harm to packmate equals bite.

---

## II. The Grills Loss and the #11 Aftermath

The death of Grills (Gil Hartocollis), shot on the rooftop by a Tracksuit assassin, is the defining loss of the middle period and the single behavioral inflection point between early-adoption Lucky and mature-pattern Lucky.

**Acute phase (hours 0–6 post-discovery).** The #11 issue documents the subject's response in real time. Behavioral inventory:

- Approach to the body: cautious, head low, sighted eye oriented toward face. Multiple sniff-cycles at the wound and at the hands. No vocalization.
- Recognition of death (operationally: cessation of investigation of the body itself, transfer of investigation to the scent trail leaving the body). Time to this transition: depicted across approximately one page, inferred elapsed time on the order of three to five minutes.
- Trail acquisition: independent, unprompted, no human direction. The subject conducts the entire forensic sequence solo.
- Affect during pursuit: tightly focused; food cues actively ignored (a pizza slice is depicted in-frame and not approached — diagnostic, given baseline drives).
- Resolution: subject locates the murderer's scent terminus, returns to Barton, attempts communication.
- Communication-failure phase: Barton, deafened and depressed, does not parse the dog's signaling. This is the most affectively heavy panel sequence in the issue and arguably the most important behavioral datum in the entire canon. The subject demonstrates *frustration without aggression* — repeated attempts, escalating intensity, no biting, no destruction, eventual lying-down beside Barton.

**Chronic phase (weeks 1–12 post-loss).** Subtle behavioral changes that persist:

- The counter-clockwise descent route now pauses at Grills's former door for an average of six to eight seconds before continuing. This persists for the remainder of the Brooklyn period — months — and is visible in #15 and in the *Hawkeye Annual* art.
- A new scent-discrimination behavior: when novel handymen, contractors, or building staff enter the premises, the subject performs an extended sniff-cycle (multiple inhalations across the torso, not the species-typical genital region) before classification. This is an *acquired* check; it did not exist pre-#11.
- Sleep position shifts subtly: increased frequency of sleeping where the sighted eye can monitor the apartment door rather than Barton's face. The proportions invert over the course of approximately four weeks. By the end of the Brooklyn period the door-orientation has become default. This is the closest the record contains to a depicted hypervigilance acquisition.

**What is absent.** No anorexia. No regression in housetraining. No aggression toward the residual Tracksuit visitors. No avoidance of the rooftop. No vocalization protest. The loss is metabolized into route-pause, scent-protocol elaboration, and a small re-orientation of sleeping geometry — and that is *all*. This is consistent with the Section 3 finding of "promiscuously secure" attachment with suppressed protest behavior. He grieves by *adding tasks*.

---

## III. The Cross-Country Transfer and the First California Period

The transfer to Los Angeles with Bishop is, in the chronology of the subject's life, the first elective relocation he experiences — i.e., not a flight, not a rescue, not a violence-driven displacement. It is also the first separation from Barton that lasts longer than three weeks.

**Transport.** Cross-country by automobile; the route is canonical but the dog's behavior during transit is documented in incidental panel work across *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #14–#22 and *Hawkeye* Vol. 5 #1. Observed: low-arousal travel tolerance, sleeping in the passenger footwell, alert at gas stations, no carsickness depicted, preference for the right-hand seat (sighted eye to driver — Bishop).

**Venice Beach habitation.** The new environment is a coastal bungalow / office combination at the rear of a strip mall in Venice. Habitat differences from Brooklyn:

- Sand exposure (novel); requires post-walk paw inspection by Bishop, becomes ritual.
- Increased ambient salt and decomposing kelp (novel olfactory load); the subject's nasal-investigation per outing increases visibly in the early arc.
- Smaller building, fewer tenants — the multi-tenant social ecology of Bed-Stuy is gone. The compensation: the strip mall's other businesses (taqueria, surfboard repair, nail salon) become surrogate scent-tenants. The subject is documented inside the taqueria on at least four separate panels across the Vol. 5 run, accepting carnitas from the proprietor.
- Reduced violent-incident frequency (relative to Brooklyn). This is comparative; Bishop's Venice practice still attracts gunfire and superhuman interference, but the per-week dose is lower.

**Behavioral re-organization under Bishop.** With Bishop as sole primary handler the subject's pattern shifts in instructive ways:

- Bark-budget rises. Bishop is more responsive to vocalization than Barton; the subject calibrates upward. The two-bark greeting from Brooklyn fades, replaced by single-bark proximity demands.
- Begging behavior diversifies — Bishop eats more varied food than Barton's pizza-monoculture, and the subject's range expands accordingly.
- The therapy-animal phenotype is *less utilized*. Bishop is, baseline, less decompensated than Barton. The subject still gravitates to her in her bad moments (the Madame Masque arc; the parental confrontation arcs) but the demand on his emotional-regulator function is lower. There is a subtle weight gain in art-depicted body shape across this period, consistent with reduced patrol behavior and increased food access.

**Separation from Barton — non-protest profile confirmed.** This is the period in which the most diagnostically important separation data accrues. Across weeks of non-contact, the subject displays:

- No door-watching behavior calibrated to Barton's scent.
- No item-seeking (the dog does not seek out Barton-scented objects, of which Bishop has several).
- No vocalization protest, no inappropriate elimination, no anorexia, no destructive behavior.
- Active re-bonding with Bishop without apparent grief-residue.

The clinically meaningful finding is the *flatness of the affective transition*. A securely attached animal would show protest. An avoidantly attached animal would show distance from the new handler. This subject shows neither. He simply re-anchors. This is the behavioral substrate for the Section 3 diagnostic of "attachment as replaceable resource" — confirmed empirically by this transfer.

---

## IV. Re-coupling, Bi-coastal Phase, and the *All-New Hawkeye* Family-Disruption Interval

The middle period's defining structural feature is not a single relocation but the eventual *bi-coastal caretaking arrangement*, in which the subject moves repeatedly between Brooklyn and Venice without a fixed schedule. By the late Vol. 4 / early *All-New Hawkeye* run, the dog has crossed the continent at least four times. This is functionally a shared-custody arrangement between two adults who do not consistently communicate about it.

**Behavioral adaptations to bi-coastalism:**

- *Dual scent-map maintenance.* The subject sustains active perceptual maps of both residences simultaneously. On return to either environment, no re-acclimation phase is depicted; he assumes prior routes immediately. This is cognitively non-trivial.
- *Caretaker-specific behavioral repertoires.* With Barton: lower vocalization, more couch-proximity, more pizza ingestion, more therapy-animal posture. With Bishop: more vocalization, more outdoor activity, more dietary variety, less mirroring posture. The subject runs two distinct sub-personalities depending on handler. Neither is more "authentic"; both are operationally him.
- *Travel tolerance increases.* Later transits (air, car, occasional Quinjet) elicit progressively less arousal. By the *Occupy Avengers* period the subject can be moved on six hours' notice without behavioral disturbance.

**The *All-New Hawkeye* family-disruption interval** introduces the Clint-and-Barney sibling arcs and the Hydra-adjacent threats that destabilize the Brooklyn premises. Observed:

- Increased exposure to Barney Barton — scent classification is *initially ambiguous* (familiar-Barton-signature with non-Clint overlay), one of only two recorded ambiguity episodes in the file. Resolution: provisional FRIEND classification, downgraded under specific provocations. The subject is not openly hostile to Barney but does not seek him out for proximity. This is unusual restraint given his baseline indiscriminate affiliation.
- Increased exposure to children (the future-arc material with the adolescent Hawkeye trainees): elicits a previously undocumented behavioral repertoire — gentler mouth, lower body posture, sustained tail-wagging at reduced amplitude. This suggests an intact developmental-stimulus discrimination capacity not previously tested.

The interval is also the period of *first significant ambient supernatural exposure* — magical signatures, dimensional incursions, encounters with figures whose scent profiles do not parse to mammalian baselines. The subject's adaptation: extended sniff-cycle, no classification, *behavioral neutrality*. He does not flee, does not approach, does not vocalize. He simply does not parse, and he tolerates not parsing. This is, on the evidence, his single most operationally significant capability: *tolerance of the unclassifiable*. Most mammals respond to perceptual ambiguity with fear-avoidance or investigative aggression. This subject responds with what reads as cognitive shrug.

---

## V. The *Occupy Avengers* Mobile Period

The middle period contains an unusual sub-arc in which the subject travels with Barton across the continental United States in a sustained itinerant period — the *Occupy Avengers* mobile phase, supplemented by adjacent road-arcs. For perhaps eight to fourteen months of subjective canon time the subject lives without fixed habitation. Behavioral implications:

- *Scent-map abandonment.* For the first time since Brooklyn the subject is not building or maintaining a fixed cartography. He instead develops a *vehicular* baseline — the truck's interior scent profile becomes the stable reference, and external environments are processed relative to it. This is a notable cognitive substitution.
- *Expanded interspecific tolerance.* The mobile arc exposes the subject to a wider sample of human typologies than the Brooklyn or Venice phases: rural, Indigenous, agricultural, prison-environment, militia-environment. Scent-classification operates throughout; no novel behavioral mode emerges. The FRIEND/BAD binary holds.
- *Increased proximity to firearms discharge.* The subject is in close range of repeated weapon-discharge events without observable acoustic startle decompensation. By the end of the mobile period the discharge-orient behavior — a head turn and a sniff of the muzzle area — is shortened to perhaps a single-frame response. This is consistent with the Section 4 finding of chronic over-arousal at baseline.
- *Sustained low-protest separation tolerance.* Barton is intermittently absent on operations; the subject is parked with rotating supplementary handlers (Red Wolf, Nighthawk, Hawkingbird trainees) without protest. Each new handler is scent-classified and re-bonded with on a roughly four-to-eight-hour timescale. This is the *most accelerated* re-bonding window in the file. The mobile period normalizes the re-imprinting capability into a routine procedure rather than a crisis-response.

**A diagnostic non-event.** Across the entire mobile period the subject is not depicted as searching for Bishop. The Brooklyn-Venice oscillation has trained him so completely that absence of one primary handler does not register as loss. This is, again, the *flatness* finding — confirmed, now, across a third structural condition.

---

## VI. The *West Coast Avengers* Team-House Phase

The subject's entry into the *West Coast Avengers* team house (Bishop's reconstitution of a coastal Avengers franchise) is the most socially dense environment of his life. Roommates and frequent visitors include America Chavez, Noh-Varr, Johnny Watts (Fuse), Kid Omega, Gwen Poole, and at intervals others. For an animal who began life chained to a single abusive handler, this is the maximum-bandwidth attachment ecology he will ever inhabit.

**Behavioral observations:**

- *Hierarchical re-bonding pace.* The subject classifies and bonds to each new housemate within hours. Order of preference, by panel evidence: Chavez (high-proximity, gravitates), Watts (FOOD-source, frequent kitchen co-location), Poole (ambiguous scent — second recorded ambiguity episode — resolved as FRIEND), Noh-Varr (NEUTRAL-curious; the alien scent profile produces extended investigation without classification), Quentin Quire (BAD-adjacent on first encounter, downgraded to TOLERATED).
- *Therapy-animal phenotype re-deployed.* America Chavez's grief-arc material elicits the lying-beside-the-sad-human behavior at high frequency. The Section 3 vocational identity — *be present for sad humans* — is fully expressed in this period. Chavez is the recipient of behavior previously almost exclusively reserved for Barton.
- *Tail-economy.* In Brooklyn the subject's tail-wag was a relatively rare, high-information signal. In the team house the tail is in near-constant motion. This is, plausibly, social calibration to a louder ecology.
- *Sleep-location distribution.* Across documented nights the subject does not sleep in Bishop's room exclusively. He rotates. This is a previously unrecorded sleep pattern and is consistent with the team-house's distribution of distress: he goes where he is most needed on a given night.

**Combat exposure in this phase.** Sustained team-engagement combat (B.R.O.D.O.K., Madame Masque's escalations, dimensional invasions). The subject is repeatedly in fields of supernatural and exotic-energy discharge. His combat protocol holds without modification:

1. Orient → 2. Scent-assess → 3. Position between threat and packmate → 4. Engage only on active harm to packmate.

There are at least two engagement events in this phase. Both produce successful bite-and-hold behavior on hostile humans, neither produces injury to the subject, and in both cases the subject disengages on cessation of threat. There is no post-engagement vigilance phase; he returns to baseline within minutes.

---

## VII. Pattern Evolution Across the Middle Period — Longitudinal Findings

Synthesizing across the Brooklyn, bi-coastal, mobile, and team-house phases, the following patterns are confirmed as stable longitudinal traits rather than situation-specific behaviors:

1. **Counter-clockwise descent / clockwise ascent** in any multi-story habitation. Documented in three separate residences. Cause unknown; preference appears innate or acquired pre-canon.
2. **Right-hand-side positioning** relative to primary handler, preserving sighted-eye monitoring. Universal across phases.
3. **Door-orientation during sleep** when not under acute threat; handler-orientation during sleep when handler is in acute distress. The shift between modes is reliable and rapid.
4. **Extended sniff-cycle on novel humans** (post-Grills acquisition). Now ritualized; never abandoned.
5. **Pause at lost-packmate locations** for several seconds. Grills's door in Brooklyn; later, additional pauses develop at locations associated with other losses.
6. **Tail-economy calibrated to ecology size.** Sparse in two-person households, near-continuous in team-house density.
7. **Bark-budget calibrated to handler responsiveness.** Low with Barton, higher with Bishop, highest with Chavez.
8. **Combat protocol invariant** across all phases and all weapon types. Four-step, in order, no deviation.
9. **Re-bonding window shortens monotonically** across the middle period: weeks (Bed-Stuy), days (first California), hours (mobile period), hours-or-less (team house). This is the single most striking trend in the file. By the end of the middle period the subject can re-anchor on a new human within a working day.
10. **Tolerance of the unclassifiable** — magic, alien, dimensional — develops into baseline. The subject treats inexplicability as a category in itself and does not seek to resolve it.

---

## VIII. Losses, Alliances, and Wars — Inventory for the Period

**Confirmed losses to the subject's social ecology across the middle period:**

- Grills (Brooklyn — gunshot). Behavioral residue: route-pause; scent-protocol elaboration.
- Aimee (relocation, not death; Brooklyn). Behavioral residue: minimal.
- Various team-house members on rotation in and out (Watts, Poole, Kid Omega — relocations rather than deaths). Behavioral residue: none observable.
- One canonical near-loss of Barton (the *Freefall* arc edge of the middle period). Behavioral residue: increased proximity-demand for several panels; resolved.
- One canonical near-loss of Bishop (Madame Masque escalation). Behavioral residue: minimal — Bishop's recovery is fast enough that the subject's response phase does not complete.

**Alliances formed across the period:**

- *With Chavez:* deep, proximity-based, secondary primary attachment functionally established.
- *With Watts:* food-mediated affiliation, stable.
- *With Noh-Varr:* curiosity-mediated, scent-investigation persists indefinitely without resolution; this is the only ongoing un-classified handler in the file.
- *With Red Wolf (mobile period):* working alliance, scent-classified FRIEND, dissolved on separation without residue.

**Wars and large-scale violence the subject lives through during this period** (incomplete but representative): the Tracksuit Mafia residual conflicts; the Madame Masque sequence; multiple Avengers-tier crises proximal to Bishop's circle; the *All-New Hawkeye* future-incursion arc; the *Occupy Avengers* domestic-extremism incidents; the team-house dimensional invasions. The subject's per-incident


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## Subject: LUCKY / "PIZZA DOG"
### File Segment: Most-Recent Era Through Present

---

## 4.1 Frame of the Recent Era

The "recent" segment of this subject's life — dating roughly from the *Hawkeye: Freefall* event (Matthew Rosenberg, 2020) through the post-MCU-tie-in *Hawkeye* limited series (Collin Kelly & Jackson Lanzing, 2022–23), the various Bishop family arcs, the *West Coast Avengers* and *Avengers* team-book peripheries, and the present-day status quo in which the subject is again co-resident between Brooklyn and the Upper West Side — covers approximately three to four in-universe years and corresponds to the most documentarily dense period of the subject's life. The volume of observed behavior has increased because the number of artists drawing him has increased, and because his presence in panel has become a near-mandatory grace note in any Barton- or Bishop-adjacent book. The intelligence value of this density is high. It also creates the first opportunity to track day-to-day behavioral consistency across multiple simultaneous draftsmen rather than within a single arc.

The headline finding of this period: the subject is, by every observable index, *thriving* — and the qualifications attached to that word in the prior chronology segments now apply more, not less.

---

## 4.2 The Freefall Era and the Ronin Cohabitation

During *Hawkeye: Freefall*, Barton resumes the Ronin identity, operates out of the Bed-Stuy apartment in a state of escalating moral compromise, and the subject is resident throughout. Observable adjustments to household routine during this period:

- **Increased nocturnal alertness.** Barton's hours invert. The subject adapts: drawn napping on the couch in daylight panels, drawn at the door or window in night panels. The animal's circadian rhythm has been retrained around a human who keeps vigilante hours. This is itself a behavioral marker — most dogs of this morphology maintain crepuscular activity peaks; the subject's are now keyed to Barton's egress patterns.
- **Weapon-tolerant.** The subject does not flinch from the deployment, cleaning, or stringing of bow equipment in his sleeping area. No observable startle to bowstring release at close range. This is preserved baseline from prior eras; noted here because the frequency of weapon-handling in the apartment increases sharply during Freefall and the subject's threshold does not.
- **Visitor classification updates in real time.** Bullseye, the Hood, and the various antagonists who enter or surveil the apartment during this arc are met with subdued, withdrawn posture rather than aggression — consistent with the FRIEND/BAD scent-classification system established in *Hawkeye* #11 but with a clear sub-category for *BAD-but-present-with-Hawkeye*, in which the subject defers without disengaging vigilance. Ears back, body lowered, sighted eye tracking the visitor across the room.
- **Continued therapy-animal role.** Barton's affect during this arc is the lowest it has been since the Fraction run; the subject's lap-occupancy and proximity-seeking behaviors increase correspondingly. The mirror-the-most-decompensating-human heuristic is functioning normally.

The Freefall arc concludes with Barton's reputational and physical wreckage and a soft hand-off back toward Kate Bishop's orbit. The subject travels with him.

---

## 4.3 The MCU-Adjacent Limited Series (2022–23)

The *Hawkeye* limited series timed to the Disney+ adaptation is, from an intelligence-gathering standpoint, the richest single recent data source — because the writers are consciously reintroducing the subject to a new readership and therefore depict baseline behaviors with documentary care. Confirmed observations from this run:

- **Coat condition: best on record.** The matting visible in the Fraction debut is gone. Fur is drawn cleaner, more uniform, with the scarred left orbit consistently rendered. The proxy reading: caretaker function (split between Barton and Bishop) is currently at the highest stability of the subject's life.
- **Weight: appropriate, possibly slightly above ideal.** Pizza consumption continues; pizza consumption appears to be partially curtailed by Bishop, not at all by Barton. The subject has learned which human to approach for which class of food request — a discriminative behavior that requires longitudinal associative memory.
- **Gait: no observable lameness.** Despite the vehicular polytrauma history, the subject moves without favoring any limb in any panel from this run. Either the off-page veterinary intervention was thorough or the subject's pain-masking is exceptional. Veterinary-behavioral norms favor a mix of both.
- **Monocular compensation: highly refined.** The characteristic head-tilt to bring the sighted right eye toward novel stimuli on the left side is drawn consistently. The subject also positions his body, when resting, so the sighted side faces the room's primary entrance — a tactical adaptation visible in panel after panel and consistent across multiple artists, suggesting either inherited model-sheet discipline or genuine behavioral signature so strong the artists are reproducing what they observe in reference.

---

## 4.4 Bishop-Side Domesticity: The Bicoastal Custody Arrangement

The subject's present residency is best characterized as *bicoastal joint custody*, with primary residence drifting toward whichever of his two bonded humans is most stable in a given month. Observed indicators:

- **Travel tolerance.** Cross-country transitions (Brooklyn ↔ Venice Beach, periodic detours through Avengers Mountain/Compound facilities during team-book crossovers) are accepted without protest behavior. The subject does not vocalize in carriers, does not refuse food after transit, does not exhibit elimination irregularity in new environments — all of which are within-norm for an unusually well-adjusted animal and *out-of-norm* for an animal with this trauma history. The reading remains the one established in the shared workup: protest does not exist in this subject's behavioral repertoire because it was extinguished early.
- **Cohabitation with other animals.** The subject has been depicted alongside Jeff the Land Shark (Bishop circle) and a rotating cast of Kate's PI-agency-adjacent animals without territorial display. No resource guarding around food bowls. No same-sex aggression with other canids in panel. The species-discrimination boundary appears flexible — he treats Jeff as packmate rather than as prey or threat, which is generous categorization on a one-eyed dog's part.
- **Avengers-environment functioning.** During *Avengers* (Aaron) and *West Coast Avengers* (Thompson, and the various follow-ons) the subject is repeatedly present in environments of cosmic-scale combat. There is no observable acute stress response. He has been depicted sleeping through cataclysms that have killed lesser characters. This is consistent with the chronic-over-arousal-as-baseline hypothesis advanced in the medical section: the subject's threshold for "alarming" has been recalibrated so high by the Bed-Stuy years that ordinary Marvel-Universe apocalypse registers as ambient noise.

---

## 4.5 Current Routine (Reconstructed)

From triangulation across the most-recent appearances, the subject's current weekly pattern resolves approximately as follows. (Items marked § are recurrent across multiple recent issues; items unmarked are reconstructed from cumulative pattern.)

- **Morning.** Wake at or near Barton; in Bishop residence, wake somewhat later. § Pre-breakfast circuit of the apartment perimeter, sniff-checking the door, the window, and any sleeping human. § Approach to the kitchen, where the FRIEND-WITH-PIZZA cue is evaluated.
- **Midday.** Long nap on whichever soft surface is closest to the most-occupied human's primary workstation. § Periodic head-up scent-check on building corridor activity (auditory + olfactory; the subject is the household's smoke-alarm-of-record).
- **Late afternoon.** Walk, when humans remember. The subject does not appear to demand walks; absence of protest behavior again. Route, in Brooklyn, is short — corner, hydrant, tree, return — and the route in Venice is longer because Bishop is the more consistent walker.
- **Evening.** § Proximity-seeking with whichever human is most emotionally elevated or depressed. Lap occupancy if seated, foot occupancy if standing, hip-against-thigh if pacing. The subject's body is, in effect, a deployable pressure-stocking for human affect.
- **Night.** Sleep at the foot of the bed in Bishop residence; sleep on the couch in Barton residence, because Barton's bed is unreliable real estate. The subject knows.

---

## 4.6 Quiet Indicators That Should Not Be Lost in the Noise

The recent record is sunny. The intelligence file would be derelict to leave it there without flagging the data points that *do not match* the cheerful narrative:

1. **The injury is not aging well in some artists' renderings.** Several recent depictions show the scarred orbital tissue with what reads, to a veterinary-behavioral eye, as the early margins of chronic inflammation. The subject is approximately a decade older than at first appearance. If the canon were tracking realistic aging, mid-life decline of the contralateral eye would be the next predicted somatic event. It has not yet been depicted. The file should expect it.
2. **The dietary load continues.** A decade of pizza, allium exposure, and incidental human-food consumption is, in any plausible biological model, accruing hepatic and renal cost. The absence of depicted symptoms does not equal absence of substrate. The animal is, on the medical evidence, living on the constitutional fortune that named him.
3. **Protest behavior remains absent.** This was the most diagnostically interesting finding of the prior chronology segments and it has not changed. As stability in the subject's life has increased, one would expect the *appearance* of protest behavior — a securely-attached animal can afford to complain. This one still does not. The reading: the early extinction is permanent. The subject will go where he is taken, lie where he is set down, and bond with whomever he is handed to, until he dies.
4. **The therapy-animal vocation is intensifying, not relaxing.** As both Barton and Bishop have, across the recent run, edged toward something resembling functional adulthood, one might expect the subject's burden as household emotional regulator to decrease. The opposite is observed. He continues to gravitate to the most-distressed human in the room with the same urgency he showed in the Bed-Stuy years. This suggests the behavior is no longer reactive to environmental demand but has crystallized into trait. He will do this even when he is not needed. He will do this with strangers. He has been observed, in recent panels, gravitating to background characters in distress whom neither Barton nor Bishop has yet noticed — which is, depending on the reader's disposition, either the most beautiful or the most heartbreaking finding in this file.

---

## 4.7 Present Disposition

**Location, last confirmed:** Bicoastal, with current weighting toward the Brooklyn residence on the most recent issues touched by the *Hawkeye* limited series and adjacent appearances. Subject to revision on next Bishop solo run.

**Custody:** Joint, informal, between Barton (primary legal claim by adoption-of-record at the veterinary clinic in *Hawkeye* #1) and Bishop (functional co-parent by cumulative caregiving hours; the file judges Bishop the more competent custodian on the somatic evidence).

**Health:** Apparently good. Substrate concerns documented above.

**Affect:** Stable. Cheerful in the recognizable canine sense. Food-motivated. Socially engaged. The presentation that has held since #11 has held into the present.

**Operational role:** Unchanged across a decade. The subject continues to function as the emotional barometer, the trauma-tolerant constant, and the silent witness of two of the most chaotic households in his publisher's catalogue. He is the most reliable adult in the room. He weighs perhaps forty pounds, has one eye, and remembers every scent that has ever entered any apartment he has lived in.

**Next predicted developments:** (a) somatic decline likely within the next several years of publication if the books continue to track him as an aging animal; (b) likely deployment as emotional fulcrum in any future Barton- or Bishop-centric grief arc, given that the subject's death — when it eventually comes — is one of the most narratively loaded events available to either character's writer; (c) continued presence, in the meantime, at the feet of whichever human in the panel is having the worst day. He will be there. He has been there for ten years. The file expects him to be there tomorrow.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT "LUCKY" / "PIZZA DOG"

## Section 2 of the Dossier

---

## 2.1 Constitutional Baseline and Phenotype

The subject is a male, intact (no surgical sterilization confirmed in canon), medium-to-large mixed-breed canine, phenotypically presenting as a golden retriever / scruffy mongrel cross. Estimated mature weight 55–70 lb based on panel proportions across Aja, Romero, Pulido, Pérez-Ortiz, and later artists. Coat: medium-length double, golden-tan dominant, with darker dorsal banding visible in stronger light. Skeletal frame: long-legged, deep-chested, retriever-typical; no observable dysplastic gait in any era of the published record, though hip and elbow imaging has of course never been performed.

Estimated age at first appearance (*Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1, 2012): 3–5 years. Estimated age at most recent appearances: indeterminate by canonical convention (the subject does not visibly age across a decade of publication, a fact that has no medical analog but should be flagged as a chart caveat). Were he aging in real time, he would be entering a geriatric window (12+ years) by present canon, with all the orthopedic, hepatic, renal, ocular, and oncologic vigilance that implies. The dossier proceeds as if he is mid-life, consistent with his depicted vigor.
