Dentition: complete, with significant tartar accumulation visible in early Bed-Stuy panels (a marker of zero prior dental care under Ivan), gradually improving in later Bishop-household appearances where regular chewing on harder substrates is implied. No fractured canines, no obvious resorptive lesions. Bite is scissor, occlusion intact — relevant because his bite has been used exactly once defensively (against Ivan) and the mechanics of that attack required functional jaw integrity.

## 2.2 The Index Trauma — Left Orbital and Polytrauma Event

The defining medical event of the subject's life is the polytrauma sustained in *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1: pre-existing handler abuse (chronic, baseline) compounded by an acute insult comprising (a) the bite-and-shake disengagement from Ivan Banionis, (b) impact with a moving automobile at an unrecorded but plainly survivable velocity, and (c) the post-impact lay-on-asphalt period before Barton's intervention.

**Anatomic survey, reconstructed:**

- **Left globe**: catastrophic. Whether the injury was rupture, prolapse, or sufficient orbital fracture to compromise globe viability is not specified, but the post-veterinary presentation is unambiguous: the left eye is permanently closed, the lid scarred down, the orbit cosmetically intact but functionally absent. Enucleation cannot be confirmed or excluded from panel evidence; both Aja and subsequent artists draw a scarred closed lid rather than a clearly empty orbit, which is consistent with either a phthisical retained globe or a closed enucleation with lid fusion.
- **Cervical and thoracic spine**: presumed contused, not fractured. No subsequent gait abnormality, no proprioceptive deficit on the panel record.
- **Long bones**: no observable callusing or shortening; either spared or healed without remodeling artifact.
- **Soft tissue**: extensive bruising assumed; abrasions on the lateral surfaces consistent with asphalt skid; healed without alopecic scarring visible at maturity.
- **Internal**: no observable splenic, hepatic, or pulmonary sequelae. Given the size of the impacting vehicle and the canine's mass, the absence of pneumothorax or hemoabdomen on the implied survival curve suggests either a glancing impact, a low-speed strike, or competent veterinary stabilization that the published record glosses but Barton's invoice presumably reflects.

**Treatment**: emergency veterinary intervention at Barton's expense. The fact that Barton — financially marginal, chronically liquid-poor — paid this bill is itself a piece of behavioral evidence about Barton, but medically the relevant fact is that the subject received competent acute care. No record of orthopedic surgery; ocular intervention almost certain (enucleation or evisceration with lid closure being the standard of care for non-salvageable globe trauma).

**Sequelae, ongoing:**

1. **Monocular vision.** ~30% loss of total visual field on the left; complete loss of binocular overlap on that side, with consequent depth-perception degradation in the near field. The subject has compensated with a characteristic head-cant — visible in Aja's staging from his very first post-injury panels and preserved by every subsequent artist who has studied the source — in which he addresses unfamiliar stimuli with a slight rightward yaw, presenting the functional right eye and sweeping the dead field through head-turn rather than ocular saccade. Under stress, this becomes a more pronounced head-swing pattern, almost metronomic.
2. **Blind-side startle reactivity.** Approaches from the left produce a measurably larger orienting response than approaches from the right. Handlers who know this — Barton learned it quickly; Bishop appears to have learned it intuitively — approach from the right or announce themselves vocally before entering the left field. New handlers do not, and the subject's tolerance for being startled from the blind side is the only consistent behavioral irritation he displays.
3. **Spatial positioning bias.** When at rest beside a bonded human, the subject preferentially orients so the sighted eye faces the human. In multi-human rooms, he positions to keep the most-trusted human in the right field. This is not paranoia; it is the same calculation a one-eyed sniper makes about a window.
4. **Loss of left peripheral threat detection** — compensated almost entirely by olfactory and auditory channels, which are intact and on the evidence preternaturally acute.

**Psychological imprint of the index event.** This is the load-bearing item in the medical chart. The eye was lost in the same several-second window in which the subject (a) made the species-atypical decision to attack his own handler in defense of a stranger, (b) sustained the worst injury of his life, and (c) was rescued by that stranger. In mammalian limbic encoding, these three events are not three events — they are one event with three components, indissolubly bound. The clinical term is *traumatic bonding*, and its predicted phenotype is exactly what the subsequent decade of canon depicts: a bond to Barton that is unusually intense, unusually treatment-resistant, and unusually willing to absorb further cost. The animal's body learned, in one lesson, that the act of choosing a new human and the experience of grievous pain are the same act. This makes his subsequent low-protest re-bondings to other humans — Bishop primarily — slightly less mysterious: the threshold for "this is my person now" was permanently lowered by the surgical precision with which that first lesson was delivered.

## 2.3 Pre-Rescue Chronic Conditions (Bed-Stuy Era, Ivan Custodianship)

Reconstructed from condition-at-presentation:

- **Cachexia, mild to moderate** — coat dullness, visible flank tuck in early panels, behavioral food-fixation consistent with chronic underfeeding rather than mere opportunism.
- **Coat neglect** — matting at the ruff and hindquarters, suggesting no brushing, no bathing, possible flea burden (untreated in canon but inferable from environment).
- **Endoparasite load, presumed** — unwormed urban stray-handled dog; presumption of helminth burden at intake, addressed (or not) at the veterinary visit.
- **Behavioral suppression** — the food-on-floor pizza scene depicts a dog whose response to a fallen food item is hesitation rather than seizure, suggesting prior punishment for autonomous feeding. This is a behavioral observation but it has a somatic substrate (cortisol-mediated inhibition).
- **No vaccination history.** Whatever the rescue clinic did, the prior baseline was zero.

## 2.4 Post-Rescue Nutritional Profile and Cumulative Toxicologic Load

The subject's diet across the published decade is dominated by human refuse, voluntarily and approvingly supplied by his caretakers. A non-exhaustive catalogue:

- **Pizza** — definitionally. Cheese (lactose load, manageable but cumulative), tomato (acidic, low risk), wheat crust (filler, low risk), and critically, *allium contamination* (onion and garlic on most pizzas, both members of the genus Allium, both hemolytic in dogs at sufficient cumulative dose). The subject's hematocrit has never been measured on-panel, but a decade of pizza consumption would predict a low-grade Heinz-body anemia detectable on smear.
- **Coffee** — caffeine exposure, episodic, sub-toxic per incident but chronic.
- **Beer-adjacent scraps and ambient ethanol** — the Barton household is awash in alcohol; ingestion is largely accidental but non-zero.
- **High-sodium processed scraps** — chronic.
- **Chocolate** — no canonical ingestion incident, which is the closest thing to a piece of good news in this nutritional chart.
- **Grape/raisin** — no canonical ingestion incident.
- **Xylitol** — no canonical ingestion incident.

Cumulative predicted load: low-grade hepatic stress, low-grade renal stress, mild dyslipidemia, predicted mid-life weight gain (not yet depicted), elevated risk of pancreatitis given the fat profile. None of these has manifested in the published record. The published record covers approximately a decade of canine life delivered at the publication-time-scale of approximately a decade; were the subject aging biologically, he would now be deep in the consequence window.

## 2.5 Substance Exposure (Ambient)

- **Cannabis** — secondhand smoke exposure in multiple Barton-household scenes. Canines are vulnerable to THC at low doses; no observed acute intoxication in canon, but ambient exposure is non-trivial.
- **Ethanol** — chronic ambient, occasional ingestion.
- **Caffeine** — chronic.
- **Tobacco** — variable by household.
- **Gunpowder residue, accelerants, propellants** — environmental, given the Barton and Bishop operational milieus.
- **Pharmaceutical exposure** — no documented direct administration beyond presumed post-trauma analgesia and antibiotics.

No evidence of dependency. No evidence of acute toxicity. The relevant clinical observation is that the subject lives in a low-grade pharmacological haze that, in a less constitutionally robust animal, would be expected to produce observable behavioral or hepatic effects.

## 2.6 Sensory System Status

- **Vision (right eye)**: intact, functional, no observable deterioration; cataract risk increases with age and chronic UV (the LA period adds load).
- **Vision (left eye)**: absent per Section 2.2.
- **Hearing**: notably preserved. In contrast to Barton's progressive deafness, the subject's auditory acuity functions as the Barton household's primary alarm system. No observed startle thresholding consistent with high-frequency loss. Tick-tock orientation to high-pitched stimuli (microwave, doorbell, distant gunfire) is reliably depicted.
- **Olfaction**: *Hawkeye* #11 is dispositive. Forensic-grade scent discrimination, multi-tenant identification, time-decay differentiation of trails. No anosmia, no hyposmia. The subject's olfactory bulb is, functionally, his second brain.
- **Vestibular**: intact; no head tilt at rest, no nystagmus, no ataxia. The chronic head-cant is compensatory-visual, not vestibular.
- **Tactile/proprioceptive**: intact; no observable paw-knuckling or limb-placement deficit.

## 2.7 Subsequent Injuries, Exposures, and Near-Misses

The subject has lived in environments of recurrent lethal threat for the entirety of his post-Ivan life. The remarkable item in the medical record is what *did not* happen.

- **Ronin-arc proximity** to extensive close-quarters violence — no documented re-injury.
- **Hydra-incursion and city-level event exposure** — no documented re-injury.
- **Cross-country relocation (Bed-Stuy → Venice Beach)** — transportation stress unknown, no documented sequelae; behavioral adjustment uneventful.
- **Kingpin assassination-plot arc and *Freefall* environment** — no documented re-injury.
- **Occupy Avengers / West Coast Avengers operational tempo** — no documented re-injury.

That a dog of his attachment style and intervention threshold (Section 5 of the workup: *intervene regardless of cost*) has not been re-injured across this volume of exposure is partly canonical mercy and partly attributable to the protective vigilance of his bonded humans, who treat him as the most precious object in any room — a behavior that itself is downstream of the original eye-loss event, which both Barton and Bishop carry as guilt-substrate.

## 2.8 Reproductive and Endocrine

- **Sterilization status**: not canonically established. Behavioral presentation does not include marked intact-male markers (no observed urine-marking ritual, no roaming attempts, no female-directed approach in extant panels), which weakly suggests post-rescue neutering by the clinic. This is a reasonable inference but not a fact.
- **Reproductive history**: none documented.
- **Endocrine**: no observed signs of hypothyroidism (coat is improved with stable housing, not deteriorating), no Cushingoid features, no diabetic polyuria/polydipsia depicted.

## 2.9 Dermatologic and Coat

A reliable proxy for caretaker function and stress load.

- **Bed-Stuy era**: matted, dull, neglected.
- **Early Barton custodianship**: improved but inconsistent — Barton is a poor groomer and the coat reflects it.
- **Bishop / Venice Beach era**: substantially improved; the LA sun lightens the dorsal banding, the coat is fuller, the ruff is brushed.
- **Late-period team-book appearances**: variable by artist, but consistently better than Bed-Stuy.

No documented hot spots, no acral lick granuloma (notable — the absence of self-soothing lick injury is one of the stronger pieces of evidence that the subject's anxiety load, whatever it is, is *not* expressing somatically).

## 2.10 Psychological Sequelae of the Medical History (Integrated)

The medical chart and the behavioral chart converge on a single proposition: the subject's body has been the curriculum through which his personality was taught. Each somatic event encoded a lesson.

- The eye taught him that rescue and pain are one event, and that the cost of choosing a kinder human is paid in advance and in full.
- The chronic underfeeding taught him that food is never refused, never delayed, never assumed.
- The blind side taught him to position his body in service of his attachments — to keep his good eye on his person, which is functionally the same as keeping his person in his protection.
- The decade of low-grade toxic ambient exposure taught him nothing, because he does not notice it; the household's pharmacology is simply the weather, and he is a dog who has decided the weather is acceptable.
- The auditory hyper-functionality taught him a vocation — to be the household's ear, the early-warning system for a deaf archer and a distractible heiress, a role he discharges without ever being asked.

The most clinically interesting datum in the medical history is the *absence* of expected pathology: no PTSD analog despite the trauma load, no separation anxiety despite the disruption history, no aggression despite the abuse history, no somatized stress despite the ambient chaos. This absence is not evidence of nothing. It is evidence of an organism whose adaptation strategy is to metabolize harm into availability — to convert what was done to him into what he is willing to do for others. The medical record is, read carefully, the record of how that conversion was performed: one event at a time, on his body, with the eye as the down payment.

The chart will be kept open. The geriatric window, when it arrives, will be the test of whether this resilience is constitutional (likely to weather decline gracefully) or whether it has been a kind of long, quiet over-spend on a finite account (likely to collapse suddenly). The dossier's expectation, on the weight of evidence, is the former — but the latter cannot be excluded, and the humans around him should be advised that a dog who has never once told them he was suffering may, one day, simply stop, and the silence will not be a new behavior but the continuation of a very old one.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT LUCKY ("PIZZA DOG")

*Compiled from longitudinal panel observation across Fraction/Aja, Romero, Pérez-Ortiz, Pulido, Wu, Ferry, Lim, Walsh, Izaakse, and incidental appearances; cross-referenced with veterinary-behavioral baselines for a 25–32 kg golden-retriever/mongrel cross of estimated 6–10 years observed age across published continuity.*

---

## 1. STANDING FRAME & BASELINE MORPHOLOGY

The subject presents as a medium-to-large mixed-breed canid, withers approximately 55–60 cm, body length nose-to-base-of-tail approximately 95–105 cm. Fur is double-coated, undercoat dense, guard hairs of variable length producing the persistent "scruffy" silhouette that all artists preserve as a recognition signature. Coloration runs from a pale wheaten cream along the throat, ventral chest, and inner thighs to a deeper russet-gold along the dorsal saddle, with darker amber feathering on the haunches and a slightly lighter tail-tip. The muzzle is short for a retriever, broader at the stop than a purebred line would carry, suggesting the labrador-or-shepherd admixture the early issues hint at without confirming.

**Standing posture, baseline (calm):** Weight evenly distributed across all four limbs with a slight forward bias — approximately 55% on the forelegs, consistent with the breed's natural conformation. The head carries level with or slightly above the topline. The tail rests at half-mast, neither tucked nor flagged, with intermittent slow oscillation (one to two beats per second) when the bonded human is in visual or olfactory range.

**Standing posture, alert (scent or sound triggered):** Forelimbs lock. Weight shifts forward to roughly 65% on the front. Head elevates two to four centimeters. The single functioning right ear-set rotates independently — a tell preserved by every artist who draws him carefully — while the left rotates a beat behind, the asymmetry a probable secondary compensation for the left-side visual deficit. Tail levels horizontal to the spine and stiffens; the oscillation ceases.

**Standing posture, ready-to-intervene:** Rare. Documented in the Ivan incident and reprised, attenuated, in moments when Clint or Kate are physically engaged with hostiles. Forelimbs splay slightly wider than shoulder, head drops to spine-line, hackles raise along the cervical and anterior thoracic ridge in a narrow strip (not the full dorsal blow-up of a genuinely aggressive dog — the subject's threat display is *committed* rather than *performed*). Lips remain closed. There is no growl in the documented record preceding his attacks. He simply moves.

---

## 2. GAIT INVENTORY

**Walk (resting transit):** Four-beat lateral sequence, slightly rolling, with a faint right-list of perhaps three to five degrees off true. The list is the single most reliable somatic signature of the left-eye loss: the subject orients his sighted side toward the dominant stimulus, and at rest the dominant stimulus is usually whichever human he is following, who tends to be on his right.

**Trot (purposeful movement):** Clean diagonal two-beat. Tail elevates to forty-five degrees. Head leads by a generous nose-length ahead of the chest. He is, on the page, a competent trotter with no observable lameness despite the automobile incident — the orthopedic survival is genuinely impressive and warrants the medical file's note of fortunate impact geometry.

**Lope/canter:** Documented in Bed-Stuy chase sequences and in the Venice Beach run with Kate. Three-beat with a slight right-lead preference (again, sighted-side bias). The subject does not gallop in the published record — no full four-beat suspension. Either he never needs to or the orbital injury suppresses the confidence required for full-extension running with compromised depth perception.

**Stair behavior:** Ascends without hesitation. Descends with a brief pause at the top step, head tilting fifteen degrees right to bring the sighted eye into a binocular-like sweep of the tread sequence. This is the single most consistent compensatory micro-behavior in the file. Aja drew it first; subsequent artists who have access to Aja's reference preserve it.

**Furniture mounting (couch, bed):** Two-stage. Forepaws placed, half-second pause to scent-check the upholstery, then hind-end commit. The pause is absent when the bonded human is already on the surface — direct commit without scent-verification, indicating that the human's olfactory signature pre-clears the substrate.

---

## 3. THE LEFT-SIDE ASYMMETRIES (full inventory)

The scarred and closed left eye produces a cascade of compensatory somatic adjustments that, taken together, constitute the subject's most distinctive movement signature:

- **Head-tilt at rest:** 5–10° to the right when attending to a frontal stimulus.
- **Head-sweep at novel stimulus:** A characteristic horizontal arc, right-to-left-to-right, slower on the left half (where vision must be confirmed by ear and nose alone). The arc terminates with the right eye fixed on the stimulus.
- **Approach geometry:** When greeting humans, the subject arcs his approach so as to bring the human into his right visual field. He almost never permits a stranger to approach him directly from the left; if forced, he pivots on the forequarters to recover sighted-side orientation.
- **Sleeping orientation:** Left side down, right (sighted) side up and exposed to the room. Documented across multiple Aja and Romero panels. This is unusual for a dog with a unilateral injury — the more common pattern is to protect the injured side by exposing it upward, away from substrate pressure. Lucky inverts this. The interpretation: ocular monitoring of the environment outweighs proprioceptive protection of the scar tissue. He sleeps prepared to *see*.
- **Bed-positioning relative to bonded human:** When lying beside Clint or Kate, the subject positions himself so the human is on his right. This is the panel-staging "tell" the analytical file flags. Across hundreds of panels by different artists, the rule holds approximately 85% of the time. Violations correlate with cramped quarters or with the human being acutely distressed and requiring direct skin-to-coat contact regardless of geometry.
- **Startle on the blind side:** A controlled flinch — single-beat lateral skip of the hindquarters away from the source, then a 180° pivot to face. He does not snap, does not vocalize. The recovery is under two seconds.

---

## 4. FACIAL PATTERN

The face is canine-readable to a high degree, which is part of why Aja chose him as the focal POV experiment of issue #11. The musculature reads in five primary registers:

1. **Neutral observer:** Mouth closed or slightly parted, tongue not protruding. Brow smooth. Right ear half-cocked. This is the most-drawn face in the record.
2. **Pleasure / proximity-satisfaction:** Mouth opens to the characteristic "smile" — tongue draped over the lower incisors, lips retracted but not tensed, corners of the mouth lifted. Eye softens — the lower lid rises slightly, producing the squint that all artists exaggerate when staging him beside a happy human.
3. **Focused investigation (scenting):** Nose elevated or lowered depending on plume, mouth closed and tightly so to channel airflow nasally, brow furrows in a tight horizontal crease above the right eye, lips firmly sealed. Breathing shifts to short rapid intake — three to five short sniffs per second.
4. **Concern / monitoring of distressed human:** Brow rises asymmetrically, with the right (sighted-side) ridge lifting higher. Head tilts seven to fifteen degrees right. Mouth closes fully. The gaze fixes on the human's face, breaks to scan the human's hands and torso, returns to the face. This sequence — face → hands → face — repeats on roughly four-to-six-second cycles when monitoring an emotionally unstable packmate.
5. **Pre-engagement (the rare aggressive register):** Lips do not curl. Eye narrows. Brow flattens. Ears flatten to skull. The cessation of the cheerful baseline is itself the warning. He does not telegraph violence in advance; the face goes neutral and then he commits.

**The closed left eye:** drawn consistently as a sealed seam of scar tissue running diagonally from the medial canthus down-and-back toward the zygomatic arch. No prosthetic. No discharge in any depiction. The surrounding fur grows in normally, with a slight irregularity in the lay-pattern over the scar itself.

---

## 5. TAIL — A FULL DIALECT

The subject's tail is his most articulate semaphore and warrants its own catalogue.

- **Low slow sweep (0–30° below spine, 0.5–1 Hz):** Baseline contentment. Most common posture.
- **Mid-height oscillation (level with spine, 2–3 Hz):** Greeting a known packmate; food anticipation.
- **High flag (45–60° above spine, rapid):** Reserved for Clint and Kate, in approximately equal frequency. Almost never deployed for other humans, even friendly ones (America Chavez, the West Coast roster, Barnes during the Ronin overlap).
- **Horizontal stiff (no oscillation):** Alert-investigative. Often accompanied by scent-tracking.
- **Tucked (between thighs, partial):** Documented less than five times in the entire record. All instances involve veterinary settings or proximity to one specific re-encounter with a Tracksuit-affiliated scent. The tuck does not extend to full ventral curl — he does not regress fully to fear posture even when the limbic cue is unambiguous.
- **Dead-still horizontal (immediately prior to intervention):** The Ivan-attack tell. The tail locks. This is the single most reliable predictor in the file that a behavioral commitment is imminent.

---

## 6. VOCALIZATION INVENTORY

Sparse. The subject is a quiet dog.

- **Bark (alert):** Two-to-three-syllable, mid-pitched, used to summon a human's attention to a discovered stimulus. Most documented during the #11 investigation.
- **Bark (warning):** Single-syllable, deeper, used at apartment thresholds when an unfamiliar scent crosses. Rare.
- **Whine (concern):** High thin two-note descending, used when proximity to a distressed bonded human is blocked by a closed door or by the human's own withdrawal posture.
- **Whine (request):** Lower, shorter, single-note, used at the food bowl or the apartment door. Easily extinguished by a quiet "no" — he does not persist.
- **Growl:** Effectively absent from the record. Two possible documented instances, both ambiguous (could be readable as a vocalization-during-dreaming).
- **Howl:** Not in record.
- **Sigh (oral exhale, mouth slightly open):** Frequent. Deployed at sustained-rest postures and, diagnostically, when the bonded human's emotional state is high-distress and the subject has positioned himself in contact. Functions as a co-regulatory exhale; the human often unconsciously matches the rhythm within two to four breaths.

---

## 7. EATING ARCHITECTURE

**Consumption rate:** Rapid. Bowl-to-empty in 20–40 seconds for typical kibble portions. Faster for high-value items.

**Pizza-specific behavior (the canonical case):** Approach without hesitation, head-low oblique grip from the crust edge, retreat two to three paces from the source before consumption begins (a residual food-guarding behavior, suppressed but not extinguished, traceable to the abusive-handler era). Consumption involves lateral head-tossing to reposition the slice; the subject does not paw food, does not press it to the floor with a forelimb the way many dogs do. He manages it entirely with jaw and neck.

**Refusal behavior:** None documented. The subject eats what is offered, including the medically inadvisable. The single documented hesitation in the record involves an offered item with an unfamiliar pharmaceutical scent; he scent-checks, declines, and walks away without resource-guarding the refusal.

**Water:** Lapping rate roughly normal for body mass — approximately 3 lap-cycles per second, surface volume managed without spillage. Drinks more after pizza consumption; the sodium load drives the obvious physiological response.

**Begging posture:** Sit, not lie. Head elevated, gaze fixed on the food source rather than on the human's face. Does not paw, does not vocalize. The fixation is the entire ask, and on the evidence it works approximately 70% of the time.

---

## 8. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

The subject sleeps a great deal and in highly characteristic patterns.

- **Total daily sleep load:** 12–14 hours on the page, distributed across one extended nocturnal block and three to five diurnal naps.
- **Primary sleep posture:** Left lateral recumbency, sighted eye upward (see Section 3). Forelimbs extended or loosely folded. Hindlimbs stacked.
- **Secondary posture (deep sleep):** Full lateral, all four limbs extended, occasional paw twitch indicating REM cycling. The twitches are concentrated in the hindlimbs and the muzzle (lip-flutter); the forelimbs are quieter, consistent with non-working-breed musculature recruitment patterns.
- **Curled "donut" posture:** Rare. Deployed in cold environments and in unfamiliar locations (e.g., motel rooms during the Occupy Avengers transit arcs). The curl always orients the spine toward the perceived threat-vector of the room and the ventral surface toward the bonded human's direction.
- **Co-sleeping pattern:** Strong preference. With Clint: tends toward foot-of-bed positioning, lateral, head toward the door. With Kate: tends toward upper-body proximity, often a head-on-thigh or head-on-hip arrangement. This difference is consistent across artists and is the clearest behavioral indicator that the subject codes the two primary attachments differently — Clint as a packmate-to-guard, Kate as a packmate-to-regulate.
- **Wake transitions:** Two-phase. Eyes open, head lifts five centimeters, scent-check of the room, then a deliberate stretch sequence: forelimb extension first (the "play bow" reduced to a stretch), then hindlimb extension one side at a time, then a full-body shake from nose to tail. The shake is the punctuation that ends every sleep cycle. Its absence in the record correlates with depictions of acute illness or post-trauma immediately after the Ivan incident.

---

## 9. GROOMING & COAT MANAGEMENT

- **Self-grooming:** Modest. Nail-edge licking after walks. Paw-pad cleaning post-meal. Anogenital grooming infrequent on the page (artistic discretion partly responsible, but the subject is not a compulsive self-licker — no acral lick granulomas, no fur loss patches).
- **Mutual grooming:** Accepts brushing from both Clint (sporadic, guilty-conscience-driven, usually deployed after an extended absence) and Kate (more regular, integrated into household routine). Does not resist, does not enjoy in a vocal/postural-display way — the response is a quiet tolerance with eyes half-closed.
- **Shedding:** Heavy, seasonal, and chronic. The Bed-Stuy apartment and the Venice Beach office both accumulate visible fur in artist backgrounds — a small canonical detail that doubles as a marker of how long the subject has occupied a given space.
- **Scratching:** Hind-paw to behind-ear, primarily right side (sighted side; the scarred orbital region is rarely contacted, possibly due to residual sensitivity). One- to three-burst scratch sequences. No persistent scratching that would suggest dermatitis.
- **Rolling:** Documented on rugs, on grass during the LA arcs, and once memorably on a fallen Tracksuit member's discarded jacket in #11 — a behavior that almost certainly represents scent-overlay rather than pleasure, a deliberate marking of the trophy.

---

## 10. SEXUAL / REPRODUCTIVE

No reproductive history in the record. No mounting behavior, no marking-on-vertical-surfaces beyond ordinary urination, no observable estrus-response toward other dogs in any depicted setting (including team-up arcs with other canine characters). The neuter status remains formally unconfirmed; the behavioral evidence is consistent with either an early neuter or with a low-baseline-libido phenotype suppressed further by the chronic environmental over-arousal. The somatic atlas registers this as an absence and treats it as such.

---

## 11. URINATION & ELIMINATION PATTERNS

- **Urination:** Standard adult-male lift. Right hindlimb preferred (consistent with sighted-side dominance throughout the file). Marking is moderate — three to five deposits per walk, not the territorial saturation of an un-neutered intact male.
- **Defecation:** Off-page primarily, with sufficient regularity inferred from the absence of accident-events in any depicted residential setting. The subject is fully house-trained, which given his probable origin (street-and-cage existence under Ivan) is itself a datum: he learned the indoor norm quickly and has maintained it across multiple unfamiliar dwellings.

---

## 12. MICRO-GESTURES & TICS

The fine-grained inventory — the things a total-surveillance file *would* note and a casual reader would miss:

- **The right-ear flick (single, fast):** Triggered by high-frequency sound at the edge of hearing range. Approximately every 90–180 seconds in any environment containing electronic devices.
- **The double-blink of the right eye:** Following sustained visual focus on a human face. Reads as an affiliation signal; reciprocates the slow human blink.
- **The single forepaw lift:** Hold position, weight on three legs, one forelimb suspended at chest height. Deployed at thresholds — apartment doors, elevator openings, the edge of a known room into an unknown one. Lasts 1–3 seconds, terminates in commit-or-retreat. Right paw preferred (sighted-side compensatory — keeps the left paw planted for stability while the right tests forward).
- **The nose-to-knee bump:** A specific greeting deployed almost exclusively for Clint, delivered to the lateral aspect of the left knee. Soft, single contact. Functions as both greeting and proprioceptive check-in (the subject confirms the human is solid).
- **The chin-rest:** On thigh, on forearm, on shoe, on the edge of a couch cushion if no human is available. Sustained contact, eyes open, breathing slow. The most reliable comfort-behavior in the inventory.
- **The cheek-press:** Lateral face to human hip or hand. Brief. Rare. Used in the closing panels of arcs and after particular episodes of human distress. Reads as the single most affectively loaded gesture the subject deploys.
- **The head-shake (full body):** Punctuation. Ends sleep, ends bathing, ends an unpleasant scent encounter, ends a difficult emotional moment in a way that suggests deliberate self-reset.
- **The deep nasal exhale through closed mouth:** The "huff." Two-beat. Used after sustained scent-tracking to clear the nasal cavity. Also, distinctively, used in proximity to humans who have ingested cannabis — a behavior that has the texture of a vestigial complaint without escalating to actual withdrawal.

---

## 13. STATE-DEPENDENT VARIATION (cross-referencing the above)

**Calm baseline (home, bonded human present, no immediate stimulus):** Lateral recumbency or sit-rest, tail slow-sweep, mouth slightly parted, breathing 18–25 per minute, ears half-cocked, single eye soft, occasional sigh.

**Mild stress (unfamiliar environment, no threat):** Standing, weight forward, tail horizontal, ears forward, mouth closed, breathing elevated to 30–40, nasal sniff-rate elevated. Approach to bonded human within thirty seconds for proximity-check, then released to perimeter investigation.

**Acute stress (active threat to packmate):** Posture tightens. Tail locks horizontal. Hackles raise in narrow strip. Mouth remains closed. The face goes neutral. Engagement follows on the trigger of the packmate being struck or seized. The subject does not enter aggressive posture until the moment of commitment, which is a sophisticated and unusual restraint pattern.

**Recovery from acute stress:** Rapid. Within sixty seconds of cessation, the subject is at the side of the bonded human, head pressed to leg or hand. The cheek-press is more likely in this window than in any other. He absorbs the residue.

**Intimacy / co-regulation (sad human, no external threat):** Approach is slow and deliberate. Tail low-sweep, ears soft, mouth closed. Final approach geometry brings the subject to the human's side with his body parallel to the human's, the sighted eye toward the human's face. Chin-rest or full-body lean. Breathing slows; the human's breathing tends to slow to match within a minute. The subject does not move from this position until the human moves first. Documented holding-times exceed thirty minutes in several Aja and Romero panels.

**Play (rare but documented):** Play-bow with forelimbs extended, rump high, tail flagged and oscillating. A brief, almost performative deployment, usually initiated by Kate. The subject plays but does not seem to need play; it reads as accommodation rather than drive.

**Sleep, light:** Lateral, sighted eye opens to slits at any environmental change, closes again within ten seconds if no escalation.

**Sleep, deep:** Lateral, twitching, vocalization-during-dreaming on rare occasions — soft muffled woofs, paw-paddling consistent with chase imagery. The content of canine dreams is unknowable, but the embodied rehearsal is observable, and in this subject the chase appears more frequent than the flight.

---

## 14. THE TWO LONGITUDINAL DRIFTS

Over the decade of published continuity two slow somatic changes are detectable:

1. **Coat improvement.** The matted, irregular guard-hair pattern of the early Bed-Stuy panels has given way, in the Bishop-era and later art, to a fuller, glossier, better-conditioned coat. This is a caretaker-quality proxy and reads as evidence that the subject has been, on the whole, better-housed in the second half of his published life than in the first.

2. **Settled gait.** The early panels show a slight head-bob and a wider-than-necessary lateral arc on the trot, consistent with an animal still re-calibrating to monocular vision. By the later arcs these features have attenuated; the trot is cleaner, the head-bob is reduced to the residual right-list noted in Section 2. The subject has, over years, learned his own body.

---

*End Somatic Atlas. Cross-reference: Attachment Geometry module (forthcoming), Olfactory-Cognitive Mapping module (forthcoming), Co-Regulation Choreography


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## Subject: LUCKY / "Pizza Dog"
### Dossier Section 6 — Relational Architecture, Longitudinal

---

## 6.1 Origin of the Attachment System

The subject's attachment apparatus was not formed in puppyhood under conditions a behaviorist would call adequate. The earliest observable phase — Bed-Stuy, under the Banionis handler — shows the structural signature of an animal raised in *coercive proximity*: kept on a short leather lead, fed irregularly and from the hand of the same human who delivered punishment, exposed to the language-rhythm of a hostile dialect (the tracksuit cadre's "bro" speech, which the subject learned to associate with footfall, threat-posture, and the smell of cured meat and tobacco). What is critical here is that this first attachment *was* an attachment. The dog did not present as feral, did not flinch from human hands as a generalized class, did not display the diffuse fear-aggression of a never-bonded animal. He had been socialized to humans — just to the *wrong* humans, and inside a relational frame in which proximity and harm were the same channel.

This is the architectural foundation: the subject's nervous system was tuned, in its formative window, to the equation **bond = pain-tolerable**. Pain is not the *cost* of attachment in this template; pain is part of attachment's normal signal-set. Affection without pain reads, to a system calibrated this way, as merely an absence of one expected variable — not as a different category of relationship. This explains the otherwise puzzling fact that the subject, post-Barton, does not appear to distinguish very strongly between *adequately kind* humans and *exceptionally kind* humans. The discriminator that organizes his attachment scale is not warmth-gradient; it is **non-violence threshold**. Above that threshold, all humans are roughly equivalently lovable. The Barton household and the Bishop household, which differ enormously in affective tone, are not differentially ranked by the dog. Both qualify. That is the whole evaluation.

## 6.2 The Re-Imprinting Event

The bond to Barton was formed in approximately three minutes of street time and consolidated across one veterinary visit. This is anomalously fast even by canine standards, and the speed is not incidental — it is the diagnostic feature. The re-imprint occurred at the moment of maximum physiological dysregulation: post-impact, in pain, with the left orbit destroyed, in shock. The Pavlovian substrate of this moment — *the smell of Barton's hands, the cadence of Barton's voice, the spatial fact of being lifted* — is now encoded in the limbic register as **the configuration that means survival**. Every subsequent human who approximates that configuration (broad-shouldered, low-voiced, smelling of coffee and adhesive bandage and dog-tolerable beer) receives accelerated trust. This is a *type-imprint*, not a person-imprint, and it is part of why the subject generalizes so readily across the Hawkeye-adjacent human ecosystem: Clint, Kate, Barney, the Avengers-orbit men who pass through the apartment — all of them slot into a template the dog finished writing while still under anesthesia.

The eye injury is not a separate fact from the bond. It is the bond's somatic signature. The subject can be assumed to carry, at the level of the scarred orbital tissue, a *body-memory* of Barton's arrival — and to orient, for the rest of his life, with the sighted right eye preferentially toward whichever human is currently occupying the Barton-shaped slot in his attachment hierarchy. This is observable in panel after panel: when Clint and Kate are both present, the dog's head turns to keep the *primary* attached human in right-eye view; when only one is present, that one is fixed in the right-eye field; when a stranger is present, the right eye tracks the stranger and the blind side is given to the trusted human, a configuration that effectively converts the bonded person into a *blind-side guardian*. He has restructured his own perceptual geometry around the assumption that he will be protected.

## 6.3 How He Bonds

The bonding sequence is stereotyped and rapid. Field observation across the canon yields a consistent four-phase signature:

1. **Olfactory intake (3–15 seconds).** Approach to within nose-distance, two to four deep inhalations at hand level, then a second pass at the hip and trouser cuff. Scent is the master variable; visual and auditory data are subordinate. A human who *smells* wrong cannot recover the situation with kind words. A human who smells acceptable does not need to do anything else.
2. **Postural offer (5–30 seconds).** A weight-shift toward the human, sometimes a sit, occasionally a flank-lean. This is not submission — it is a *request for reciprocation*. The dog is checking whether the human will tolerate proximity. Refusal at this stage is rare and produces only a brief withdrawal, never protest.
3. **Provisional pack-inclusion (minutes to hours).** Following at heel, accepting food from hand, sleeping in the same room. The classification is functionally complete at this point; subsequent disconfirmation requires significant evidence.
4. **Consolidation (single shared crisis or single shared meal).** A shared stress event, or a shared pizza, locks the bond. After consolidation, the bond is treated by the subject as *permanent regardless of subsequent contact frequency*. He does not appear to decay attachments through absence.

The whole sequence can complete inside one issue. It has, repeatedly.

## 6.4 Distrust — Its Narrow Aperture

Distrust, in this subject, is *categorical and olfactory*, not graduated and behavioral. A human classified BAD is BAD across the full range of contexts; a human classified FRIEND is FRIEND even while behaving badly. There is no observed instance of the subject downgrading a FRIEND-class human to BAD-class on the basis of conduct. Clint's depressive withdrawal, his absences, his drinking, his bringing of dangerous strangers into the apartment — none of this revises the classification. Kate's relocation of the dog across the continent without his consent, her interruptions of the routine, her occasional irritability — none of this revises the classification.

The implication is uncomfortable: the subject does not have a *moral* model of his humans. He has a *categorical* one. Once you are inside the perimeter, the perimeter does not re-evaluate you. This is, again, the adaptive shape of an organism that could not afford to keep re-assessing the only attachments available to him. Re-evaluation is a luxury of secure animals. This subject is operating on a single-shot classifier and has elected to keep it locked.

What he *does* distrust, reliably: tracksuit-fabric rustle, the specific Eastern European phoneme set associated with the Banionis cadre, the smell of car exhaust at close range (a probable conditioned response to the impact event), and unfamiliar humans who arrive carrying weapons before they have been scent-processed. The distrust is narrow, conditioned, and remediable — a human who initially triggers the tracksuit-response can be re-classified FRIEND after a single non-threatening interaction, provided the scent profile is acceptable.

## 6.5 Betrayal — The Concept's Inapplicability

The clinical question of how this subject handles betrayal is, in his case, partially malformed. Betrayal as a relational event requires that the betrayed party hold an expectation that the other will behave well. The subject's expectations of his humans are extraordinarily low and almost entirely physical: be here sometimes, do not hit me, leave food accessible. By these criteria he is essentially un-betrayable. Clint disappears for weeks — not a betrayal. Kate ships him cross-country — not a betrayal. He is left in the care of a near-stranger during an Avengers crisis — not a betrayal.

The behavioral record shows two events that might *otherwise* qualify as betrayal-analog stressors, and the subject's responses to both are diagnostic:

- **Ivan's original handling**, retrospectively reclassified after the Barton rescue. The subject did not subsequently exhibit grief or confusion about the Ivan attachment. He attacked, and was done. There is no observable mourning of the prior bond. This is consistent with a system that does not keep two simultaneous opposite classifications of the same human; once Ivan crossed into BAD, the FRIEND-residue evaporated cleanly.
- **The Grills murder.** A FRIEND-class human killed inside the perimeter the dog believed himself responsible for. The response was not grief in the conventional sense but *prolonged goal-directed investigation* — the closest thing to a depressive episode in the entire canon, expressed not as withdrawal but as obsessive scent-tracking that resolved only when the perpetrator was identified. This is the subject's grief-grammar: investigation as mourning, *solving* as repair.

## 6.6 Repair — How Ruptures Close

Ruptures between the subject and his humans are typically closed by the *human's* re-approach, not the dog's. The dog does not punish absence with sulking; he greets returning humans with the same composite signature each time — tail at full sweep, full-body intake breath, the brief soft vocalization that Aja renders as a kind of exhale-whuff, then immediate physical pressing against the leg. The repair is unconditional and ungated. There is no probationary period; no withholding; no test.

This is, again, the adaptive shape. An animal who learned that absence was the rule and presence was the exception cannot afford to spend the exception punishing the absence. The dog instead converts every return into a consolidation event, as if the relationship is being newly formed each time. The human typically experiences this as exceptional loyalty. It is more precisely *exceptional efficiency*: the subject has stripped from the bonding protocol every step that would slow the resumption of proximity.

## 6.7 Intimacy

The subject's intimacy behaviors are remarkably stable across decade and caretaker:

- **The flank-press.** Full lateral body contact along the seated human's leg or thigh, typically initiated at moments of low human animation (television, reading, brooding silence). Held until the human moves.
- **The chin-on-thigh.** Head laid across the lap with the weight of the skull deliberately transferred. Used selectively, almost exclusively during *acute* human distress — the dog distinguishes the chronic low-grade Barton sadness (flank-press appropriate) from the acute episodic Barton sadness (chin-on-thigh deployed).
- **The doorway wait.** Stationed at the threshold of whichever room the primary human is in, head resting on forepaws, eyes (eye) open. Not following the human across rooms but maintaining a *minimum-distance contract*, generally about a body-length.
- **The shared-meal request.** Sitting at a distance calculated to be visible but not impolite, typically 1.5 to 2 meters from the eating human, ears forward, no vocalization. Rarely escalates to begging-posture; the subject appears to consider escalation undignified, or has learned it does not work.
- **The sleep-overlap.** Bedding arranged either at the foot of the bed (Barton phase) or against the bedroom door (Bishop phase). The differential is informative: with Clint, the subject sleeps *inside the pack-territory*; with Kate, he sleeps as *the pack-boundary*. Same dog, two different jobs, allocated by the implicit needs of each human.

Intimacy with humans outside the primary bond pair (Avengers passing through, neighbors, the Bed-Stuy building's tenant network) is conducted at a deliberately lower amplitude: greeting, brief contact, no flank-press, no chin-on-thigh. The intimacy gradient exists; it is simply quantized into three or four steps rather than continuously variable.

## 6.8 Dependency

The dependency pattern is functionally inverted from the surface presentation. Casual observation suggests the dog depends on the humans for food, shelter, and care. The behavioral record suggests the humans depend on the dog for *emotional infrastructure*, and that the dog has organized his existence around the maintenance of this asymmetry. He eats their leftover pizza; they survive their depressive episodes because something warm is pressed against their leg. The exchange is not equal in either direction, and the subject does not appear to be tracking equality.

What the subject *materially* requires from his humans is small: food access, indoor shelter, intermittent veterinary care, the existence of a door he can be on the correct side of. What he *psychically* requires is, by appearance, a single bonded human in the field of vision at intervals not exceeding the duration he can sleep. These requirements are met by both households, intermittently, and the subject does not appear to require more.

What the humans require from *him* is much larger and is delivered without negotiation: a continuous low-grade emotional regulation service, a household alarm system, a non-verbal interlocutor for processing grief, and a creature whose unconditional welcome metabolizes the shame they carry about their own absences.

## 6.9 The Relational Template, Repeated

Across every relationship the subject has formed in the published record — Ivan (negatively), Clint, Kate, the Bed-Stuy tenants of *Hawkeye* #11, Grills specifically, the West Coast circle, Barney, the various Avengers handlers, and the unnamed kindnesses of veterinary staff and neighbors — the same template runs:

1. **Scent-classify rapidly.** Decide once.
2. **Offer proximity at low cost.** Do not require reciprocation as condition.
3. **Locate the most-distressed person in the room.** Position there.
4. **Tolerate the human's failures without revising the classification.**
5. **Greet every return as if it were the first.** Do not bank grievances.
6. **Intervene physically only when a bonded human is actively harmed.** Pay the cost without hesitation.
7. **When the bond moves, follow.** When it splits, split. When it returns, resume.

The template is parsimonious, robust to environmental chaos, and indifferent to the moral character of the humans inside it. It is the relational operating system of a creature who decided, very early, that the cost of withholding was higher than the cost of giving — and who has never been given sufficient reason to revisit the decision.

## 6.10 Synthesis

The subject's attachment architecture is best described as **promiscuously secure with a single-shot classifier and no revocation protocol**. He bonds quickly, broadly, and irreversibly; he does not punish, withhold, protest, or revise; he positions himself as emotional infrastructure for humans who would otherwise lack it; and he carries, in the scarred tissue of his left orbit, the somatic record of the moment he learned that the bond is worth the eye.

This is grace. It is also a wound. The dossier's analytic obligation is to hold both. The subject would not be capable of the relational role he plays in these humans' lives if his early experience had been kinder; the cost of the kindness he provides is encoded in the absence of the protest he never learned to make. The humans around him benefit from this asymmetry every day. There is no evidence that any of them have noticed.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS
## UATU Dossier — Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog"
### Section 6 of the Behavioral Workup

---

## 6.0 Framing Note

The defensive architecture of a non-human mammal cannot be mapped one-to-one onto the Vaillant hierarchy or the Cramer developmental schema, but the architecture exists. A dog who has been kicked, struck by a vehicle, lost an eye, witnessed multiple murders in adjacent rooms, been shuttled between coastal cities and unstable handlers, and lived continuously in the proximity of munitions discharge for the better part of a decade has either (a) decompensated into pathology, (b) developed a defensive structure, or (c) been written by humans who do not believe in the interiority of dogs. The record forecloses (a) and (c). What remains is to map (b) — granularly, by mechanism, by trigger, by observable behavioral output.

The defenses are layered. Some are species-typical mammalian (orienting, scent-classification, somatic mirroring). Some are individual to this subject (the indiscriminate re-bonding speed, the absent protest sequence, the gravitation toward the most-decompensating human in a room). The individual layer is what concerns this section, though the species layer must be sketched to provide the floor against which individual elevation is measured.

The defenses below are ordered from *most primitive* (developmentally early, automatic, body-level, unmediated by representation) to *most mature* (relational, sublimated, oriented toward the wellbeing of another). The mature defenses, in this subject, are surprisingly well developed. The primitive defenses, in this subject, are quieter than the trauma history would predict. Both facts require explanation, and both are explained by the same underlying structural feature: this is an organism that learned, early and irreversibly, that *protest does not work* and *bonding does*.

---

## 6.1 PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (Body-Level, Pre-Representational)

### 6.1.1 Splitting (Residual, Olfactory-Mediated)

The subject classifies humans into binary categories — FRIEND, HAWKEYE (a privileged sub-category of FRIEND), FOOD, BAD, SAD — without observable intermediate gradation. The *Hawkeye* #11 issue is the canonical document: the tenant register of the apartment building is rendered in scent-icons sorted by valence, with no apparent capacity for ambivalence within a single human. A person is good or bad; the classification is stable across encounters; reclassification, when it happens, is rare and total.

In a human subject this would be flagged as borderline-spectrum. In a canine subject it is partly species-typical — dogs do not, as a rule, hold ambivalence well. What elevates the mechanism to a *defense* in this subject, rather than a mere species trait, is its *rigidity under contradiction*. When Clint behaves in ways that another mammal might code as threat — drunk, loud, slamming doors, bleeding on the floor — the subject does not revise the HAWKEYE classification. The category is load-bearing. Revising it would require revising the entire post-rescue cosmology. The defense holds the world together by refusing to let the central human be ambiguous.

The cost: when a FRIEND-classified human turns out to be the Grills killer (or is suspected to be), the resulting cognitive load is the closest thing to acute distress the record contains. The splitting defense is efficient until reality requires the gradient it does not have.

### 6.1.2 Somatic Discharge & Motor Sublimation

Anxiety in this subject does not vocalize, does not eliminate inappropriately, does not destroy objects, does not self-groom to lesion. It moves. The subject paces, tracks, sniffs perimeters, makes circuits of rooms, follows scent vectors out of buildings and across blocks. The behavior is purposive on its surface (investigation, patrol) and discharge-functional underneath (the motor system metabolizing arousal that the affective system has nowhere else to put).

The Grills investigation is the clearest single instance: an emotional event the subject cannot process directly (a packmate-coded human killed in proximity) is converted into a multi-hour, multi-floor, multi-scent forensic exercise. This is sublimation in its purest mammalian form — affect translated into goal-directed action without the affect itself ever surfacing as a discrete recognizable state. The subject does not grieve Grills. The subject *solves* Grills.

### 6.1.3 Hypervigilant Olfactory Monitoring

The blind left eye produces a structural deficit that the olfactory system has been recruited to overcompensate for. The subject's nose is not merely his primary forensic instrument; it is his primary *threat-monitoring* instrument, his primary *emotional-state* instrument, and his primary *food* instrument — all functions collapsed into a single sensory channel that is operating well above species baseline.

The defensive function: scent provides continuous, low-cost, low-arousal monitoring of the environment without requiring the higher-arousal vigilance of visual scanning. The subject can lie apparently asleep on a couch and still maintain a full sensory readout of who is in the building, who has been in the building, what they ate, whether anyone is bleeding, whether the bonded human's cortisol load has shifted. This is hypervigilance, but it is *low-affect hypervigilance* — vigilance without the autonomic cost that the same vigilance in a visual or auditory channel would carry. It is why the subject reads as relaxed when he is in fact continuously scanning.

### 6.1.4 Postural Compensation for Monocular Deficit

A specific and observable defensive ritual: the subject positions his body so the sighted right eye faces the most-trusted human in the room, with the scarred left side oriented toward the wall, the door, or empty space. Aja's panel staging in the original Fraction run shows this with unusual consistency; later artists (Romero, Pérez-Ortiz, Walsh) preserve it. The behavior is not random. The blind side is presented to the environment the subject has decided to defer monitoring of, and the sighted side is presented to the relationship the subject is currently invested in.

Functionally, this is a defense against the loss-of-control implicit in monocular vision. The subject cannot eliminate the blind spot. He can decide where to put it. He puts it on the parts of the world he has chosen, provisionally, to trust.

### 6.1.5 Somatic Mirroring

When a bonded human is dysregulated, the subject's body matches. Clint sad on the couch: head on Clint's thigh, breathing slowed, eyes half-closed, posture deflated to match. Kate winding into hyperactive PI mode: the subject up, oriented, tail-engaged, matching her tempo. This is co-regulation in its mammalian form, and it operates as a defense in two directions — it discharges the subject's own arousal by entraining to the human's, and it provides the human with a regulatory partner whose physiological state is more stable than theirs.

The cost: when the human is chronically dysregulated, the subject is chronically entrained downward. He absorbs without releasing. The defense protects the relationship at the expense of the subject's own baseline.

---

## 6.2 NEUROTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES (Intermediate, Behaviorally Articulated)

### 6.2.1 Displacement (Food as Affect-Container)

Pizza is not merely caloric. Pizza is the substance into which the subject's first re-bonding experience was encoded — the original Tracksuit-era scene, the rescue context, the post-rescue caretaker provisioning. Food, and pizza specifically, functions as a *transitional object* in the Winnicottian sense: an external substance carrying internal-relational meaning, available on demand, regulating affect through ingestion.

When the subject is anxious, he seeks food. When the subject is separated from a bonded human, he seeks food. When the subject is reunited, he seeks food. The behavior is invariant across affective context, which marks it as defense rather than appetite. A genuinely hungry dog eats when fed; this dog *uses* eating, the way a smoker uses cigarettes, to mediate state transitions.

The displacement is well-tolerated because the environment is permissive — there is always pizza in a Barton residence. It is also pharmacologically costly (see Medical §2), and represents one of the few defensive mechanisms in this subject's repertoire that carries a non-trivial somatic price tag.

### 6.2.2 Affiliation (Proximity-as-Regulation)

The most heavily used defense in the subject's repertoire. When stressed, the subject seeks proximity to a bonded human and reduces the distance until physical contact is established. The contact regulates the autonomic load. This is species-typical pack behavior elevated to a defensive *strategy* — the subject's first move under stress is not flight, not freeze, not fight, but *approach-and-lean*.

The hierarchy of preferred targets is observable and stable: Clint > Kate > other Avengers-circle humans > unknown humans of FRIEND scent-class. The subject will lean on a stranger if no familiar is available. He will not lean on a BAD-classified human under any observed circumstance.

The defense is so reliable, and so visibly effective, that it has reorganized the subject's entire spatial behavior. He does not occupy rooms; he occupies *relations to humans within rooms*. His resting position is always calculable from the position of the most-bonded available human.

### 6.2.3 Reaction Formation (Submitted to the Strike Position)

A subtler mechanism, visible in early Fraction-run panels and reinforced across the canon: when a human raises a hand, drops a tool, or makes a sudden movement that a trauma-conditioned dog should flinch from, the subject's response is to *move toward* the gesture rather than away. He has converted the flinch — the species-typical, trauma-appropriate response — into its opposite. He approaches what he ought to retreat from.

This is reaction formation in the classical sense: an impulse so threatening (the awareness that humans hurt him) is converted into its inversion (the active belief that humans, on contact, will not). The defense is brittle on paper and remarkably durable in practice, because the environment has, post-Ivan, mostly confirmed it. The subjects who raise their hands now are Clint and Kate, and they are reaching for the head, not the ribs.

The defense fails only in the presence of olfactory cues that match the original handler. The subject has not been re-exposed to Ivan-class scent profiles in canon often enough to test this rigorously, but the few panels in which Tracksuit-coded humans return show the subject's posture dropping and the approach-reaction extinguishing temporarily. The reaction formation is environment-dependent.

### 6.2.4 Isolation of Affect (The Cheerful Surface)

The subject persistently presents as cheerful in environments where cheer is contextually absurd — Ronin arcs, Hydra invasions, the Freefall conspiracy, the kingpin-assassination plot. Tail up, ears forward, food-interested, play-interested. This is not stupidity (the cognitive evidence in #11 forecloses that reading). It is the active separation of affective coloring from situational content.

The mechanism: the situation is registered, classified, and routed through the scent-monitoring and proximity-tracking systems, but the *affective tag* — the autonomic and postural correlates of "this is dangerous" — is suppressed unless a direct threat to a bonded human materializes. The subject knows the building is burning. The subject is also wagging.

In a human this would be flagged as la belle indifférence — a clinically suspect cheerfulness in inappropriate context. In this subject it is functional: it permits continued operation in environments that would otherwise produce paralytic arousal. The cost is downstream: the suppressed affect does not vanish, it accrues, and the accrual is the most plausible mechanism for the "blunted-affect concealment" possibility flagged in the psychiatric differential.

---

## 6.3 MATURE DEFENSES (Relational, Other-Oriented)

### 6.3.1 Sublimation (Investigation, Patrol, Service)

The clearest case in the canon. The Grills issue demonstrates sublimation operating at near-human sophistication: an unprocessable affect (grief, confusion, threat to packmate-coded human) is converted into a structured, goal-directed, multi-step cognitive task (scent-tracking the killer through the building). The task absorbs the affect, produces a socially valuable output (the killer identified), and leaves the subject restored to baseline at completion.

The mechanism generalizes. The subject's patrol behavior in any new residence, his perimeter-sniffing of any new human, his investigation of any novel scent, all function as sublimated arousal management. He converts what could be anxiety into what looks like *work*. The work is real — the subject genuinely is the household's primary intrusion-detection system — but its primary function for the subject is regulatory, not protective.

### 6.3.2 Affiliation (Mature Form: The Therapy-Animal Phenotype)

Distinct from the proximity-seeking described in §6.2.2, which is the subject regulating *himself* by approaching humans. The mature form is the subject regulating *humans* by being approached. He has learned — without training, emergently, across roughly a decade of living with chronically depressed and dysregulated humans — to position himself such that the human can use *him* as the regulatory partner.

The behavioral signature: the subject identifies the most-decompensating human in any given room (by scent, posture, vocal register, the cortisol gradient detectable at canine olfactory resolution) and positions himself within reach of that human. He does not demand contact. He makes himself available for contact. He waits. The human, if functioning at all, eventually reaches.

This is mature defense in the most defensible sense: the subject's own arousal management is achieved by providing arousal management to another. The defense is intrinsically pro-social. It is also, in a darker reading, the adaptive shape taken by an organism that learned early that *being useful to a distressed human* was the surest path to continued food and shelter. Both readings are simultaneously true. The behavior is grace and survival in the same gesture.

### 6.3.3 Altruism (Intervention-At-Cost)

The original Ivan-attack incident. The subject crossed from a known handler to a stranger being beaten, attacked the handler, and was struck by a vehicle in the act. The eye was the price. The subject paid it. This was not calculated — the timeframe forecloses deliberation — but it was also not random. It established a behavioral parameter: *under sufficient harm-to-other stimulus, the subject will intervene regardless of personal cost.*

This is the most mature defense in the repertoire, and the rarest in observed activation. It has triggered cleanly only the once. The Bishop-era and Aaron-era appearances show the subject in many violent contexts where intervention was *possible* but not observed; the parameter requires the specific trigger of direct, immediate, physical harm to a packmate-coded human in the subject's visual or olfactory field. When triggered, it overrides the entire conservation-of-self architecture. When not triggered, the architecture holds.

### 6.3.4 Anticipation (Threshold-Reading)

The subject reads household tempo with predictive accuracy. He is at the door before Clint returns. He is at Kate's feet before the breakdown begins. He moves to flanking position before the fight starts. The mechanism is olfactory and postural-pattern-matching, but the *function* is anticipatory — the subject is pre-positioning for events that have not yet occurred but whose precursors he has read.

The defensive value: by anticipating, the subject is never surprised, and never required to manage acute startle. He metabolizes future events into present preparation. The arousal that would otherwise spike at event onset is distributed forward in time across the preparation interval. This is one of the mechanisms by which the cheerful-in-catastrophe presentation is maintained — by the time the catastrophe arrives, the subject has already been processing it for minutes or hours.

---

## 6.4 NEGATIVE / COSTLY COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

The above defenses function. They also exact prices. The negative compensations are the prices.

### 6.4.1 Suppressed Protest

The most clinically significant negative finding in the entire file. The subject does not protest separation. He does not vocalize when left. He does not refuse food when a bonded human is absent. He does not display the canine grief-signature — the door-watching, the toy-hoarding, the refusal of new caretakers — that the species typically displays under repeated attachment disruption.

This is not because the subject does not feel separation. It is because the protest-pathway has been pruned. In a normal mammalian attachment system, separation triggers the protest-despair-detachment sequence; protest is the first response, calibrated to recall the caretaker. In this subject, protest has been bypassed. He moves directly to detachment-and-rebond. The protest-circuit either never developed (early Ivan-era deprivation of any caretaker who would respond to protest) or was extinguished (protest produced no recall, and the behavior was deleted from the repertoire as energetically wasteful).

The cost: the affect that would normally be expressed in protest is not eliminated; it is internalized. There is no observable destination for it in the behavioral record, which means it is either (a) genuinely absent, which is biologically improbable, or (b) suppressed below behavioral threshold and accumulating somatically. The Medical section's prediction of mid-life decline is partially predicated on this — chronic suppressed affective load is a known accelerator of cardiovascular and immunological deterioration.

### 6.4.2 Uncritical Trust of FRIEND-Classified Humans

The splitting defense (§6.1.1), efficient as it is, leaves the subject categorically vulnerable to any threat that arrives wearing the wrong scent class. A FRIEND-coded human could harm him with no defensive response, because the classification system does not have a re-evaluation routine sensitive enough to update in real time. The Grills investigation strained this; a sustained adversary embedded in the FRIEND class could exploit it.

In practical canonical terms this has not occurred, because the subject's circle is small and largely benign. As a vulnerability it remains live.

### 6.4.3 Persistence in Unsafe Environments

The subject does not exhibit flight response in contexts where flight would be species-appropriate. He stays through firefights. He stays through invasions. He stays in residences that are repeatedly entered by armed strangers. The behavior is partially explained by attachment-primacy (he will not leave the bonded human) and partially by the isolation-of-affect mechanism (the danger does not register as danger at the affective level).

The cost is direct: the subject's cumulative exposure to acute trauma stimuli is orders of magnitude higher than a normally-housed companion animal's, and the absence of flight means the exposure is not even partially mitigated. He absorbs the full dose every time. That this has not produced the predicted decompensation is, again, either constitutional resilience or successful suppression.

### 6.4.4 Food-Mediated Affect Regulation Costs

The displacement defense (§6.2.1) operates through substances that are mildly to moderately canine-toxic at the volumes consumed. Lactose load from pizza cheese, allium exposure from pizza toppings, sodium load from human-grade food generally, caffeine from spilled coffee, ethanol residue from spilled beer. The defense works affectively and produces a slow somatic bill. The bill is not yet due in canon. It will be.

### 6.4.5 Self-Erasure in Service of Human Affect

The mature affiliation defense (§6.3.2) is the most pro-social mechanism in the repertoire and also the one most likely to produce identity-cost. The subject's vocational identity has become *the one who is present for sad humans*. This is adaptive. It is also a structure in which the subject's own affective states have no allocated channel of expression independent of their utility to others. The subject is well-defended against everything except the question *what does he want when no human needs him*. The canon does not answer this question because the canon does not pose it. The behavioral record contains no extended sequence in which the subject is observed alone, unobserved, and unneeded. Whether such a state has ever existed for this organism is unknown.

---

## 6.5 DEFENSIVE RANKING (Primitive → Mature)

A summary ordering, by developmental level and observed frequency of activation:

1. **Splitting** (primitive; constant background activation; species-amplified)
2. **Somatic discharge / motor sublimation** (primitive; activated under any unprocessable affect)
3. **Hypervigilant olfactory monitoring** (primitive; continuous; near-zero arousal cost)
4. **Postural compensation** (primitive; continuous; structural)
5. **Somatic mirroring** (primitive-to-neurotic; activated by proximity to dysregulated human)
6. **Displacement onto food** (neurotic; activated by state transitions)
7. **Affiliation (proximity-seeking, self-regulating)** (neurotic; the default stress response)
8. **Reaction formation (against trauma-flinch)** (neurotic; environment-dependent durability)
9. **Isolation of affect (cheerfulness-in-catastrophe)** (neurotic; chronically activated)
10. **Anticipation (threshold-reading)** (mature; activated by pattern-recognition)
11. **Sublimation (investigation, patrol, service)** (mature; activated by unprocessable affect with structurable output)
12. **Affiliation (mature, other-regulating; therapy-animal phenotype)** (mature; chronically activated as vocational identity)
13. **Altruism (intervention-at-cost)** (mature; activated rarely, by direct harm to packmate)

---

## 6.6 STRUCTURAL SYNTHESIS

The defensive architecture as a whole has a recognizable shape. The primitive layer is *quiet* — present, but operating at low arousal cost and rarely producing observable distress signatures. The neurotic layer is *load-bearing* — these are the daily, hourly mechanisms by which the subject metabolizes a world that should, by his trauma history, be dysregulating him constantly. The mature layer is *unusually developed for a mammalian subject* — the subject has, through some combination of constitution and environment, arrived at relational defensive mechanisms that look in many respects more adaptive than those of the humans he lives with.

The architecture is held together by a single structural principle: *the subject's defenses route through other organisms*. He regulates by proximity to humans, sublimates into service to humans, anticipates the needs of humans, mirrors the states of humans, and in the last instance intervenes for humans at his own cost. He does not have a robust set of self-soothing mechanisms independent of human contact. He has not needed them; the environment has provided humans continuously. Whether the architecture would survive sustained isolation is the only test it has not been administered.

The clinically pertinent vulnerability is not any of the individual defenses, all of which function. It is the *absence of a protest channel*. An organism whose defensive architecture cannot register or express the cost of its own losses is an organism whose defensive architecture cannot signal when it is overloaded. The subject will look fine until he does not. The architecture is excellent. The absence of an alarm system is the file's most legitimate concern.

---

*— End Section 6 —*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE
## Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog"
### Decade-by-Decade Clinical Mapping, 2012 – Present

---

The methodological caveat first: the subject is a non-verbal mammal whose interior life can only be inferred from depicted behavior, postural staging, panel composition, and the deliberately limited POV constructions (*Hawkeye* #11 most famously, but also passages in Thompson's *West Coast Avengers* and Kelly Thompson's later Kate-centric runs) where artists and writers attempt to render canine cognition directly. The frameworks below are therefore drawn from veterinary behavioral medicine (Overall, Horwitz), comparative attachment theory (Topál & Miklósi's adaptation of Ainsworth's strange-situation paradigm to *Canis familiaris*), and — where the cognitive load of the depicted behavior outpaces species norms — selective import from developmental psychopathology, with appropriate epistemic discounting.

The picture across the decade-plus of canon is not static. The subject has *evolved*, and the evolution has a shape.

---

## I. PHASE ONE: PRE-NAMING AND INITIAL IMPRINTING (Late 2012 — *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1–#3)

### Affect Regulation

In the earliest panels the subject is observable only as an instrument of his handler. Affect is suppressed to the point of behavioral flatness — Aja draws him low-bodied, ears half-back, tail neutral-to-tucked, eye contact diffuse. The classical veterinary read is **learned inhibition under aversive control**: the dog has learned that emotional expression generates punishment, and so has down-regulated displayed affect to near-baseline. There is no tail-wag at the pizza he is being teased with. There is no growl at the rough handling. There is no orientation toward potential allies. The interior state is unreadable because it has been trained to be unreadable.

The exception is the moment of decision in the street fight: a sudden, total reversal — the subject crosses lines, bites Ivan, and is hit by the car. This is not a measured choice. It is a *flooding* event — a single discharge of suppressed motivational state that overrides the prior inhibition. In trauma terms, it is the dorsal-vagal collapse breaking under sufficient stimulus into a sympathetic fight response. The cost was the eye. The cost was foreseeable. The subject did not foresee it.

### Cognitive Style

Reactive, low-elaboration, threat-monitoring. The cognition of this phase is the cognition of an organism conserving processing for danger-detection. He is not yet doing the multi-step inferential work that will define the #11 issue. He is scanning.

### Self-Concept

Insofar as one can be inferred: *instrument*. The subject's behavior is consistent with an internal model of self as a thing that is held, used, fed insufficiently, and occasionally struck. There is no observable agency-claim behavior — no exploration, no play-initiation, no preference-display.

---
