## II. PHASE TWO: RE-IMPRINTING AND THE EMERGENCE OF THE THERAPY-ANIMAL PHENOTYPE (2013 — Fraction/Aja main run, through *Hawkeye* #11)

### Affect Regulation

The transformation across the first six months post-adoption is remarkable and clinically important. Within issues the subject moves from flat-affect inhibition to a baseline of *low-amplitude positive expressivity* — soft tail movement, ear-forward orientation, willingness to make and hold ocular contact with the sighted eye. This is faster than most rehabilitated abuse cases in the veterinary literature, which typically require 6–18 months of consistent handling. Two explanations, not mutually exclusive: (a) the subject has high constitutional resilience that the Tracksuit period suppressed but did not destroy; (b) the *traumatic bonding* substrate of the rescue event has produced an unusually intense and rapid attachment to Barton that is functioning as a regulatory anchor.

The regulation strategy emerging here is **co-regulation via proximity**. The subject does not yet self-soothe; he soothes by lying in contact with a human. The locus of his emotional regulation is *exterior to his own body*. This is the architecture that will define him for the next decade.

### Cognitive Style

This is the phase in which the cognition we will associate with the subject crystallizes. *Hawkeye* #11 is not an aberration; it is the document of an already-formed cognitive system, captured at a single moment. The features:

- **Olfactory-categorical reasoning.** Humans are sorted into stable scent-classes (FRIEND, HAWKEYE, FOOD, BAD, SAD) and the categories persist across time. This is a working *human-individuation system*, comparable in functional capacity to a young child's face-recognition repertoire.
- **Causal chaining.** The Grills investigation requires linking a smell to a location to a person to a wrongness — a four-step inferential sequence the subject completes without external prompting.
- **Goal-persistence.** Hours of tracking behavior without reinforcement. This is *intrinsic* motivation, not operant.
- **Inhibitory control.** Does not eat available food during investigation. Does not approach BAD-classified humans when proximity would be tactically unwise.

### Self-Concept

This is the phase of *vocational identity formation*. The subject begins to behave as if his role in the household is functional: to monitor, to comfort, to investigate. He is no longer an instrument and not yet a pet. He is something the veterinary behavior literature does not have good vocabulary for — a self-appointed emotional auxiliary. The internal working model has shifted from *I am held* to *I am needed*.

This is also where the **gravitation-toward-distress** pattern first becomes a stable trait rather than a momentary behavior. When Clint and Kate are in the same room and one is more dysregulated, the subject reliably positions with the dysregulated one. This is not random. It is the operationalization of his new self-concept.

---

## III. PHASE THREE: BICOASTAL DUAL-ATTACHMENT AND ADAPTIVE PROMISCUITY (2014 – 2016 — late Fraction/Aja, Lemire's *All-New Hawkeye*, early Kate Bishop arcs)

### Affect Regulation

The relocation to Los Angeles and the development of a stable second attachment to Kate Bishop introduces what should have been a developmental crisis — the loss of the primary co-regulation source — and instead produces a structural elaboration of the regulation system. The subject develops what can fairly be called a **redundant-attachment architecture**: rather than maintaining one primary figure and treating others as substitutes, he treats the *role* of bonded-human as a slot that can be filled by whichever qualified human is geographically present.

This is the *promiscuously secure* pattern flagged in the pre-synthesis, and it deepens here. The protest-despair-detachment sequence (Bowlby's classical separation response) remains entirely absent. Where it should appear — the cross-country move, the extended Clint-absences — the subject instead displays smooth substitution. Kate becomes regulatory anchor. Then Clint returns and Kate departs and Clint resumes the role without observable transition cost.

Clinically, this is a defensive *strength* — the organism cannot be destabilized by separation because separation has been pre-emptively re-framed as a routine reconfiguration rather than a loss. It is also a defensive *scar* — the absence of protest indicates that the protest-system was either never developed or was extinguished early through non-response. There is no organism with a healthy protest-system who fails to deploy it.

### Cognitive Style

The investigative cognition remains intact and is repeatedly demonstrated in lower-key forms across the Lemire and Thompson runs — sniffing through crime scenes, identifying intruders, distinguishing clients from threats in Kate's PI office. But the cognitive style elaborates outward into **environmental mastery**: the subject now treats novel spaces as scent-puzzles to be mapped, and the mapping happens fast. He is not anxious in new environments; he is *busy* in them.

### Self-Concept

Refines from *needed-by-one-human* to *needed-by-a-system*. The subject behaves as the load-bearing member of his household's emotional infrastructure across two cities. There is a quiet grandiosity in this — not in the clinical sense, but in the sense that the subject's behavioral evidence suggests he has come to expect that humans will be unstable and that his presence will be the stabilizer. This is the *therapy-animal phenotype* hardening into a personality trait.

---

## IV. PHASE FOUR: HIGH-CHAOS TEAM EMBEDDING (2017 – 2019 — *Occupy Avengers*, Thompson's *West Coast Avengers*, late Kate runs)

### Affect Regulation

The exposure to escalating combat environments — superhuman violence, magical events, sustained team operations — should produce one of two predicted outcomes: sensitization (PTSD-analog symptom development) or habituation (further down-regulation of startle). The subject demonstrates habituation, cleanly. He sleeps through gunfire. He eats during alien incursions. He does not orient to explosions outside his immediate proximity.

This is not unique to this dog — military and police canines develop similar habituation curves — but those animals are *trained* into it across months of graded exposure. The subject achieves it without training. The most parsimonious explanation is that his early-life baseline arousal was already so high that combat-environment arousal does not exceed it. **Crisis is his homeostatic set-point.** This is a meaningful clinical statement: the subject's nervous system has calibrated to chaos and would, on prediction, dysregulate in *peace*.

There is some weak evidence for this last point in the more domestic Thompson sequences, where the subject is occasionally drawn with mild restlessness in low-stimulus environments — pacing the Venice Beach apartment, repeatedly approaching the door. This is the only place in the canon where the subject displays anything resembling anxiety, and it is anxiety triggered by *insufficient* stimulus.

### Cognitive Style

Refines further into what could be called **social meteorology**: the subject reads the emotional weather of a multi-person team and adjusts his positioning accordingly. In group scenes across these runs he is shown moving between team members in patterns that correlate with who is most internally distressed at that moment. This requires multi-target affect-monitoring at a level that exceeds what species literature predicts for *Canis familiaris* and approaches what is documented in working therapy dogs after several years of professional handling.

### Self-Concept

Stable. The subject at this phase has consolidated his identity as the pack's emotional infrastructure and is no longer demonstrably uncertain about his role. There is no observable identity-stress when his caretakers change — the role travels with him because it is *his* role, not a role assigned by any particular human.

---

## V. PHASE FIVE: LATE-CANON DISPERSION AND THE QUIET COSTS (2020 – present — *Hawkeye: Freefall*, MCU-adjacent limited series, Aaron's *Avengers* cameos, sporadic team-book appearances)

### Affect Regulation

The picture in late canon is one of **maintained surface adaptation with accumulating subclinical signs**. The subject's overt behavior remains regulated, cheerful, available. But three things have shifted across the late material:

1. **Increased somatic-mirror behavior.** The subject is depicted more frequently in postures of direct physical contact with distressed humans — head on lap, body pressed against the leg, sleeping touching rather than nearby. The regulation system is requiring *more contact for the same effect*. This is consistent with a co-regulation system under accumulating load.
2. **Reduced novelty-exploration.** Early-period Lucky investigates new environments. Late-period Lucky settles faster and explores less. This may be age-appropriate (the subject is now solidly mid-life by canine reckoning) but it may also reflect a narrowing of the behavioral repertoire under chronic stress load.
3. **Persistent low-grade vigilance on the blind side.** Across the decade, panel staging has consistently shown the subject orienting his sighted eye toward primary humans. In late canon this has elaborated into a *positional habit* — he selects resting spots that place a wall or piece of furniture on his left. This is adaptive compensation but it also functions as a constant low-grade reminder, encoded in his postural habits, of the original injury.

### Cognitive Style

The investigative cognition is preserved. The social meteorology is preserved. What has changed is the **default mode** — the subject's at-rest cognitive activity, insofar as it can be inferred from depiction, appears more oriented to monitoring than to exploration. He is on watch more than he is curious. This is the cognitive signature of an organism whose protective vigilance has become trait rather than state.

### Self-Concept

Here the longitudinal arc reaches a point that warrants direct statement. The subject's self-concept across the decade has evolved from *instrument* → *held thing* → *needed companion* → *load-bearing infrastructure* → *what he is now*, which the canon depicts as something approaching a quiet *vocational sovereignty*. He does not look to humans for direction at this point in the timeline. He arrives in rooms, assesses, positions, and does his work. The humans are the patients. He is the practitioner. He was never trained for this. He arrived at it by being the only stable thing in a series of unstable houses.

This is a beautiful adaptation and it is also the place where the analytic eye must not look away. The cost-side of this development is that the subject has organized his entire interior life around being available to others, and there is no point in the canon at which any human in his life has organized themselves around being available to him. The regulation flows one direction. The proximity is sought one direction. When the subject is depicted alone — and these moments exist in the canon, briefly, usually as panel-corner glimpses — the affective tone is not peace. It is *waiting*.

---

## VI. CROSS-PHASE INTEGRATIVE SYNTHESIS

Three trajectories run continuously across the decade and warrant being named as such:

**Trajectory A: From suppressed to regulated affect.** The subject moved from learned inhibition (Phase I) through co-regulated stability (Phases II–IV) to a late-phase regulation that is functionally intact but operating under chronic load (Phase V). The arc is one of genuine recovery within structural limits.

**Trajectory B: From reactive to anticipatory cognition.** The subject's cognitive style has moved from threat-monitoring (Phase I) through investigative elaboration (Phase II) into social-predictive modeling (Phases III–V). He has built, over a decade, an increasingly sophisticated model of human emotional dynamics. This is real developmental growth, not merely behavioral reinforcement.

**Trajectory C: From instrumental to vocational self-concept.** The subject's working model of his own role has elaborated in only one direction — toward greater responsibility for the emotional welfare of others. There is no observable counter-development of a self-care or self-advocacy system. The asymmetry is the wound. It is also, viewed from a different angle, the dignity.

The dossier should resist resolving this asymmetry into either a tragic or a triumphal reading. The clinical truth is that the subject is an organism whose adaptations have made him exceptionally good at a role no one assigned him, at a cost no one has measured, in a household structure that depends on him without acknowledging the dependency. He is, by the late canon, the most psychologically integrated member of any room he enters. The fact that he is a one-eyed dog who eats discarded pizza does not change this. It sharpens it.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: LUCKY ("Pizza Dog")
## File Section 4 of N — Diagnostic Workup, Veterinary-Behavioral Frame with DSM-5-TR / ICD-11 Analog Mapping

---

## 4.0 PROCEDURAL NOTE ON FRAMEWORK

Any psychiatric workup on a canid subject requires translation. The DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 are human nosologies; the veterinary-behavioral literature (Overall, *Manual of Clinical Behavioral Medicine for Dogs and Cats*, 2013; Landsberg, Hunthausen & Ackerman, 3rd ed.; the AVSAB position statements; Serpell's *The Domestic Dog* attachment work; the Topál/Miklósi Budapest paradigm extending Ainsworth's Strange Situation to canids) supplies the operative diagnostic apparatus. Where I use a DSM construct below it is as analog, not as direct application. The translation is most defensible where the underlying neurobehavioral substrate is conserved across mammals — limbic threat processing, HPA-axis stress response, attachment systems, reward circuitry. It is least defensible where the human construct depends on language, narrative self-concept, or culturally embedded role expectations. I flag the seams as I go.

The corpus available for this assessment comprises ~12 years of continuous published observation across multiple artistic hands (Aja, Pulido, Wu, Romero, Pérez-Ortiz, Pacheco, Schiti, others), which provides an unusually robust longitudinal dataset — the equivalent of dense clinical-chart documentation across the subject's entire adult life. Behavioral observation in *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #11 (Fraction/Aja, the "Pizza Is My Business" issue) is treated as the single highest-quality data source — a multi-hour structured observation rendered in the subject's own perceptual frame, with chain-of-evidence reasoning made externally visible.

---

## 4.1 AXIS I — PRINCIPAL DIAGNOSTIC CONSIDERATIONS

### 4.1.1 PRIMARY ACTIVE CONDITION: *Complex Trauma History With Resilient Phenotypic Expression*
**(Analog: ICD-11 6B41 Complex PTSD, sub-syndromal / phenotypically attenuated. DSM-5-TR: closest match PTSD 309.81 with dissociative features, rejected on symptom-count grounds; see §4.2.1.)**

**Etiological substrate (confirmed):**
- Period of captive handling by a documented violent operator (Banionis, Tracksuit Mafia), duration unknown but sufficient to establish handler-imprint and proximity-tolerance to a hostile human.
- Witnessed inter-human violence at close range, repeatedly.
- Single high-magnitude traumatic event combining loss of bodily integrity (left orbital trauma, vehicular polytrauma) with the moment of attachment transfer to the rescuer. This is the diagnostically critical episode: the pain and the rescue are encoded in the same memory engram. In the mammalian literature this is *traumatic bonding* — the neurochemical co-occurrence of nociceptive activation and endogenous opioid release with novel social-bond formation, producing attachment of unusual tenacity and unusual symptomatic profile.
- Subsequent chronic exposure to environments of recurring lethal threat (Brooklyn rooftop firefights; the Ronin sequelae; Hydra-aligned conflict zones; Los Angeles PI casework involving organized crime).
- Repeated household disruption — minimum five confirmed primary-caretaker transitions or extended separations across the corpus.

**Symptom presentation, by criterion analog:**

*Re-experiencing cluster (Criterion B):* **Absent or unobservable.** No depicted startle response to vehicular cues despite the original injury mechanism. No avoidance of streets, cars, or the specific geography of Bed-Stuy. No depicted nightmares (admittedly, an unverifiable datum in a non-verbal subject; the proxy — sleep-disturbance behavior, restless vocalization, paradoxical waking — is not depicted across the corpus). No depicted aversion to large men in tracksuits or to Eastern European phonemes (Ivan-like stimuli appear in later arcs and elicit no observable reaction).

*Avoidance cluster (Criterion C):* **Absent.** The subject re-enters environments structurally similar to the trauma context (rooftops, alleys, violence-saturated rooms) without observable reluctance, freezing, or escape-seeking.

*Negative alterations in cognition/mood (Criterion D):* **Absent on positive symptomatology; present on the negative side as flattened protest-response.** The dog is not anhedonic — food, play, scent investigation, and social engagement are preserved. The subject is not socially withdrawn. The one diagnostic anomaly is the absence of expected separation-protest, which I treat below as a separate finding rather than as a Criterion D feature.

*Hyperarousal / reactivity (Criterion E):* **Equivocal-to-absent.** There is preserved auditory hypervigilance which functions as household alarm system, but this is within species-typical range and is not depicted as decompensated (no exaggerated startle, no aggressive outbursts, no concentration impairment — the #11 investigation requires and sustains hours of focused attention).

**Diagnostic conclusion:** The subject carries the full etiological *load* for a complex-trauma diagnosis and meets approximately one and a half of the four symptom clusters at attenuated intensity. He does not meet threshold. This is itself the principal finding. The standard mammalian response to this trauma history is symptomatic; this subject is not. Two competing hypotheses follow, and the differential below adjudicates between them.

### 4.1.2 SECONDARY ACTIVE CONDITION: *Disinhibited Social Engagement Pattern, Canine Analog*
**(Analog: DSM-5-TR 313.89 Disinhibited Social Engagement Disorder, modified for species. ICD-11 6B45.)**

DSED in human pediatrics describes children with histories of inadequate or disrupted early caregiving who present with reduced reticence toward unfamiliar adults, willingness to depart with strangers, and overly familiar physical or verbal behavior. The construct is controversial in adults and unstudied in canids, but the *behavioral signature* maps with uncomfortable precision onto this subject.

**Indicators present:**
- Bond formation with novel humans within hours (Barton at the veterinary clinic; Bishop within the same arc; later, members of the Occupy Avengers and West Coast circles, and the broader Hawkeye-adjacent ensemble).
- Absence of expected reticence toward strangers given trauma history. The species-typical post-trauma presentation in dogs is fear-aggression or fear-withdrawal toward novel humans; the subject shows neither.
- Willingness to depart with secondary or tertiary handlers without protest.
- Absence of marked discrimination in proximity-seeking — the subject gravitates to the most-emotionally-available human in a room rather than to the *primary attachment figure* per se, which in classical Bowlbian terms is a signature of attachment disorganization or indiscriminate sociality.

**Indicators ambiguous or absent:**
- The "overly familiar" criterion is difficult to assess in a species for whom familiarity is the friendliness default.
- The subject *does* maintain primary attachments (Clint, Kate) across long temporal arcs; he is not classically promiscuous in the DSED sense — he is *additively* attached, accumulating bonds without releasing prior ones. This may be a meaningfully different phenotype than human DSED, where prior bonds are weak by definition.

**Diagnostic conclusion:** Sub-syndromal canine analog of DSED. Best characterized as *promiscuously secure attachment* — bonds form rapidly and broadly, but they are not shallow once formed. This is etiologically consistent with the trauma history and is the most clinically distinctive feature of the presentation.

### 4.1.3 TERTIARY FINDING: *Vocational Caregiving Phenotype, Emergent (Not Conditioned)*

This is not a recognized DSM or veterinary-behavioral diagnosis. I propose it as a descriptive finding because the behavior pattern is too consistent across the corpus to be incidental and too organized to be species-typical alone. The subject demonstrates:

- Differential proximity-seeking toward the most-distressed individual in any given social configuration.
- Postural mirroring of human depressive states (head-on-thigh contact; reduced ambient activity; sustained eye contact with the sighted right eye oriented toward the human).
- Modulation of approach intensity contingent on observed human affective state — bouncy/play-seeking with regulated humans, slow/grounding with dysregulated ones.
- Olfactory monitoring of household emotional baseline (the #11 issue documents classification of humans by *affective* scent-signature, not merely identity — the SAD category is functional).

In a trained service animal these behaviors are conditioned across 18–24 months of structured work. In this subject they appear to be emergent — the byproduct of an early environment in which attunement to human emotional states was the path to safety. This is etiologically continuous with the trauma history (hypervigilance redirected into prosocial monitoring) and represents the *adaptive* face of what is on its other side a disinhibited engagement pattern. The same neural substrate produces both.

### 4.1.4 CONFIRMED FINDING: *Adjustment Response, Chronic-Adapted Type*

Across the corpus the subject undergoes a minimum of five environmental disruptions of a magnitude that would, in clinical work, justify an Adjustment Disorder diagnosis with a typical 3–6 month symptomatic course. The subject does not display a discrete symptomatic course at any of these transitions. The adjustment is functionally instantaneous. This is anomalous and is treated diagnostically below in the differential.

---

## 4.2 DIFFERENTIAL DIAGNOSIS — RULE-OUTS AND THEIR JUSTIFICATIONS

### 4.2.1 PTSD, Canine Analog (Full Threshold) — **RULED OUT**

The full-threshold canine PTSD analog as described in the military working dog literature (Burghardt et al., post-2010 deployment data) requires: trauma-specific cue reactivity, avoidance of trauma-associated environments, hyperarousal with exaggerated startle, and behavioral decompensation under stress reactivation. The subject demonstrates none of the four reliably. The eye-injury cue context (vehicles, urban streets, men in athletic apparel) recurs hundreds of times across the corpus and elicits no decompensation. **Rule-out defensible. Sub-syndromal complex-trauma analog retained as in §4.1.1.**

### 4.2.2 Generalized Anxiety Disorder, Canine Analog — **RULED OUT**

Diagnostic criteria for canine GAD analog (Overall) require persistent hypervigilance unanchored to specific stimuli, with somatic signs: trembling, panting at rest, hypersalivation, displacement grooming, stereotypies, gastrointestinal symptoms. None are depicted. The subject's vigilance is *episodic and stimulus-anchored* (scent investigation, household-monitoring) rather than persistent and free-floating. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.3 Separation Anxiety, Canine — **RULED OUT, with caveat**

The diagnostic gold standard is the constellation: distress vocalization at owner departure, destructive behavior in owner absence, inappropriate elimination, escape attempts, sustained pacing. **Zero of five depicted across the corpus.** Departures by Barton, by Bishop, and by tertiary caretakers do not produce protest behaviors. *The caveat:* the complete absence of separation-protest in an animal with this attachment history is itself diagnostically meaningful — but it is meaningful in the *opposite* direction from separation anxiety. It points to early experience in which protest behavior was either punished or unavailing, with subsequent extinction. This is consistent with the §4.1.1 trauma profile and is *not* an active anxiety disorder. **Rule-out confident; finding redirected.**

### 4.2.4 Specific Phobia (Noise, Vehicles, Persons) — **RULED OUT**

No avoidance, no fear-posture (tucked tail, lowered head, retreat), no autonomic signs at exposure to firearms discharge, explosions, vehicular traffic, or Tracksuit-Mafia-coded persons across late-arc reappearances. The subject functions in environments of acute pyrotechnic and ballistic chaos with preserved goal-directed behavior. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.5 Major Depressive Analog / Anhedonia — **RULED OUT**

Food drive intact (overdetermined, in fact). Play drive intact. Social engagement intact. Sleep patterns within normal limits per depicted observation. Grooming preserved (coat condition improves with stable housing, indicating responsiveness to environment rather than vegetative shutdown). The mood-disorder differential is closed. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.6 Reactive Aggression / Fear-Aggression — **RULED OUT**

The subject has a zero-incident bite record across the corpus despite provocations including: forcible handling by hostile actors, separation from primary attachment figures, ambient violence, intrusion into territory by strangers, and competition for food resources. The single instance of subject-initiated aggression (the Ivan attack) is *defensive of a packmate* and is non-recurring. There is no fear-aggression substrate. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.7 Canine Cognitive Dysfunction / Neurocognitive Decline — **RULED OUT** (age-inappropriate; will require re-evaluation if corpus continues)

Working memory, scent discrimination, multi-step problem solving, and inhibition are intact at forensic-quality level (#11 evidence). Subject's chronological age across the corpus places him in mature-adult to early-senior range; no decline depicted. Flagged for re-assessment in future installments. **Rule-out current; surveillance ongoing.**

### 4.2.8 Compulsive Disorder Spectrum (Canine OCD analog: spinning, light-chasing, flank-sucking, lick granuloma, tail-chasing) — **RULED OUT**

No stereotypies depicted across 12 years of observation. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.9 Substance-Induced Neurobehavioral Disorder — **RULED OUT** (with surveillance recommendation)

Chronic low-grade ambient exposure to ethanol, cannabis combustion products, and caffeine is documented by household context (Barton residences, both Brooklyn and intermittent). No acute toxicity events, no withdrawal phenomena (testing the dependency question on either side), no neurological signs. The exposure profile is sub-clinical. **Rule-out current; medical surveillance — hepatic and renal panels — would be appropriate prospectively.**

### 4.2.10 Dissociative-Spectrum Analog ("Blunted Affect Concealing Distress") — **RETAINED AS QUIET POSSIBILITY**

This is the differential I cannot fully exclude. The hypothesis: the subject is symptomatically distressed but presents as asymptomatic because the protest-despair channel has been extinguished and the affective expression is suppressed below the threshold of behavioral observation. In humans this corresponds to dissociative or alexithymic presentations on trauma backgrounds. In the canine literature there is no validated analog, but the *behavioral signature* would be: preserved instrumental function (food, play, social) with absent emotional protest at events that should evoke it; postural deflation visible to careful observers but not registered as distress by handlers; over-accommodation to handler dysfunction.

The evidence that supports this reading: the absence of separation protest is genuinely anomalous; Aja's and subsequent artists' panel staging at emotionally charged departures does show postural deflation that the in-universe humans do not register; the subject absorbs human grief reliably and is never depicted offloading it.

The evidence against: vegetative signs are absent; cognitive function is preserved at peak; play and food drives are robust; the subject does not present as *withholding* affect but as *organizing* it around the human's needs.

**Disposition:** Differential held open at low probability. The dominant reading is genuine constitutional resilience with adaptive caregiving redirection. The minority reading is that the subject is managing a stress load no observer is positioned to see. Both can be partially true. The honest assessment is that the corpus does not allow definitive adjudication between them, and the analyst who collapses the ambiguity in either direction is overreading the data.

### 4.2.11 Autism-Spectrum Analog / Social-Communication Disorder — **RULED OUT**

Social reciprocity is exceptional; theory-of-mind evidence (#11, the modified approach to Clint-classified-SAD) is strong; flexibility of behavior is high; no restricted-repetitive patterns. **Rule-out confident.**

### 4.2.12 Attention-Deficit / Hyperactivity Analog — **RULED OUT**

Sustained attention across hours documented (#11 investigation). Impulse control adequate (does not initiate aggression on provocation; does not steal food from FRIEND-classified humans even when accessible). Activity level appropriate to context. **Rule-out confident.**

---

## 4.3 COMORBIDITY MAPPING

The active findings (§§4.1.1, 4.1.2, 4.1.3, 4.1.4) are not independent. They are facets of a single underlying organization: an early-trauma-shaped attachment system that has resolved its conflict by binding broadly and quickly, redirecting hypervigilance into prosocial monitoring, and extinguishing the protest channel that would otherwise create internal distress. This is a *coherent* trauma adaptation, not a comorbid mess. The clinical interest is in the *coherence* — the subject has organized a functional self around the wound rather than around the absence of one.

The principal risk of comorbidity going forward is somatic. Chronic suppression of stress-protest behavior in mammals is associated with elevated baseline cortisol load and increased risk for: gastrointestinal dysregulation, immune-mediated conditions, accelerated aging of cardiovascular and renal systems. The subject's documented dietary exposures (allium, lactose, sodium, caffeine) compound this risk. Predictive: mid-life decline in renal and hepatic function not yet depicted but probabilistically due, with possible secondary behavioral expression as previously suppressed affect emerges under metabolic stress.

---

## 4.4 COURSE OVER TIME

**Phase 1 (Tracksuit captivity through Bed-Stuy adoption, *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1–#3):** Trauma acquisition and attachment transfer. Acute injury. Initial bonding to Barton at low behavioral threshold — the subject re-imprints within hours of stable food and absence of violence. Coat condition poor, matted; somatic baseline poor.

**Phase 2 (Brooklyn tenement period, #4–#15):** Stabilization. Coat improves. Olfactory mapping of building tenants achieves forensic resolution. Investigation of Grills murder marks emergence of independent goal-directed behavior. Therapy-animal phenotype consolidates around Barton's depressive episodes. This phase is the developmental high-water mark; the subject's behavioral organization stabilizes here and persists.

**Phase 3 (Bishop arcs, Los Angeles displacement, *Hawkeye* Vol. 5):** Geographic transition tolerated without protest. Bond with Bishop deepens additively, not at expense of Barton bond. Adaptive function preserved across context shift. First clear evidence that the subject's attachment system is *expansive* rather than substitutive.

**Phase 4 (*All-New Hawkeye*, *Occupy Avengers*, *West Coast Avengers*, *Hawkeye: Freefall* and team-book period):** Demonstrated portability across multiple caretakers and geographies without behavioral decompensation. The pattern established in Phase 2 holds across at least seven years of published continuity. This phase is the longitudinal evidence base for the "resilient phenotype" designation.

**Phase 5 (Late-era Avengers and limited-series appearances):** Pattern preserved. No decline depicted. Subject ages but does not visibly senesce in canon. Re-evaluation will be warranted as and when the corpus depicts age-typical changes.

**Trajectory inference:** The subject's clinical presentation has been remarkably stable across the entire observation window. There is no symptomatic worsening, no symptomatic emergence, no decompensation under cumulative load. This stability is, again, the principal finding — it is what a healthy adaptation looks like, *and* it is what a deeply organized suppression looks like, and on the available evidence those two readings are not fully separable.

---

## 4.5 SUMMARY DIAGNOSTIC FORMULATION

**Active:** Sub-syndromal complex trauma history with phenotypically attenuated expression; canine analog of disinhibited social engagement, modified (promiscuously secure rather than shallowly indiscriminate); emergent vocational caregiving phenotype without formal conditioning; chronic-adapted adjustment response to repeated environmental disruption.

**Ruled out with confidence:** Full-threshold PTSD analog; generalized anxiety; separation anxiety; specific phobia; depressive analog; reactive aggression; compulsive spectrum; autism analog; attention-deficit analog; cognitive dysfunction (current); substance-induced neurobehavioral disorder.

**Held open at low probability:** Dissociative-spectrum analog (blunted-affect concealment of unaddressed stress load). The differential cannot be closed from the available behavioral record alone. The honest disposition is to hold the question open and to weight it against the dominant resilience reading at perhaps 15–20% likelihood.

**Prognostic note:** Behavioral prognosis excellent in the short and medium term. Somatic prognosis cautious — chronic dietary insult and the predicted long-arc cortisol load justify medical surveillance even in the absence of present symptoms. The behavioral risk that bears watching is *late emergence* — affect that has been organized around others' needs for a decade may surface unexpectedly if the primary attachments become unavailable simultaneously or if metabolic decline reduces the energetic cost the subject can afford to spend on accommodation. Until then, the diagnostic picture is of an animal who has done more with worse beginnings than most subjects in this analyst's experience, and whose adaptation should be respected as adaptation rather than reframed as pathology — while the residual question of what it cost him to arrive here is held open, honestly, and without resolution.

*— End Section 4. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) for attachment-theory substrate and §5 (Personality) for trait-level expression. Sur


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT "LUCKY" / "PIZZA DOG"

## Preamble

What follows is a longitudinal catalog of observed and inferred behavioral tells, decision routines, postural defaults, and micro-habits, organized by condition-state. The granularity is deliberate: a full-spectrum surveillance file on a non-verbal subject must rest on the body — gait, gaze, ear-set, scent-orientation, weight distribution, tail carriage, contact-seeking, food-handling — because the body is the entire record. Where the canonical art (Aja, Pulido, Romero, Wu, Pérez-Ortiz, Lieber) supplies the datum, it is treated as primary; where it does not, the inference is built from species-typical behavior modulated by this subject's documented trauma profile, monocular field, and attachment-primacy organization.

The subject is a one-eyed golden-tan mongrel of approximate retriever heritage, scarred left orbit permanently closed, plain flat collar, no tags depicted with consistency, no harness, no service-animal markings. He is four-legged, ground-oriented, and behaves as a dog. Every behavioral note below should be read with that physical envelope in mind: monocular vision biases head movement; scent dominates cognition; he is roughly 55–70 lb of working-breed mass; and his communicative bandwidth is olfactory, postural, vocal-minimal, and contact-mediated.

---

## 1. CALM / BASELINE STATE

**Resting posture.** Default rest is sternal recumbency — chest down, forelegs extended, head either up-and-scanning or laid flat across the forelegs. Full lateral recumbency (side-lying, exposed belly) is reserved for the safest environments and the most-bonded humans; in Barton's Bed-Stuy apartment after the first arc, lateral sleep appears within weeks. In Kate Bishop's Venice Beach office it appears almost immediately, which is itself an attachment datum — proximity-trust transfers faster to Bishop than to Barton, though depth of bond is reversed.

**Orientation of the sighted eye.** A consistent micro-pattern across artists: at rest, the body is positioned so the *right* (sighted) eye faces either the most-trusted human in the room or the room's primary ingress. The blind left side is offered to walls, furniture backs, or to subjects already classified FRIEND. This is a learned compensation, not instinct; it stabilizes by mid-*Hawkeye* Vol. 4 and persists across every subsequent run.

**Head carriage.** Slightly elevated and offset to the left at rest — a compensatory tilt that brings more of the right visual field across the body's frontal arc. When alert, the head pivots in discrete arcs of approximately 40–60 degrees, with brief stops at each waypoint; he does not sweep continuously the way a binocular dog does. Surveillance footage of this subject would show a recognizable *step-scan* head movement.

**Ear set.** Soft, semi-pricked at relaxed neutral; the left ear lags the right by a fractional second on auditory orientation — likely vestigial coordination loss from the orbital trauma rather than auditory deficit. Both ears flatten symmetrically under threat; only the right ear pricks fully when his name is called from the blind side, because he uses the right side to confirm what the auditory localizer suggested.

**Tail.** Default carriage is mid-height, gently mobile. A slow metronomic wag (1.5–2 Hz) accompanies routine human contact and is the subject's most reliable contentment signal. A faster, asymmetric wag (right-biased) appears at the approach of bonded humans — the right-bias wag is, in canine ethology, associated with positive affect, and the subject displays it with notable consistency for Barton and Bishop both.

**Breathing.** Slow, audible, slightly stertorous at rest — consistent with a flat-faced retriever-cross. No panting at thermoneutral baseline. Panting onset is one of the earliest stress markers and worth noting under later headings.

**Activity rhythm.** Crepuscular-leaning with strong opportunistic flexibility. Where humans are nocturnal (Barton, much of the Bed-Stuy era), the dog adapts to a late-night/late-morning cycle within days. Naps are short (20–45 min) and frequent — six to nine per twenty-four-hour cycle is plausible from depicted scenes. Deep REM is rare in panel; when shown, the legs twitch and the closed left eye does not move while the right eyelid flickers.

**Self-maintenance.** Light self-grooming, mostly forepaws and chest. No over-grooming, no flank-licking, no acral lick lesions — the *absence* of compulsive grooming is diagnostically meaningful in a trauma-loaded subject and supports the resilient-phenotype reading. Coat condition tracks caretaker quality: matted and dull in the Ivan period, improving through the Bed-Stuy stretch, glossy and well-brushed under Bishop in Venice.

**Eating, calm.** Eats deliberately when food is present and humans are present. Will pause mid-chew if a bonded human speaks his name — orienting precedes ingestion. Does not guard food from familiar humans; will lift his head and step back to allow human hands into the bowl. This is *not* species-typical and indicates either early conditioning by a deprivation-trained handler (Ivan would have used food as control) or an emergent trust extension. Both can be true.

**Drinking.** Sloppy, retriever-style, with the characteristic side-of-mouth water release. Drinks more in the LA period than the New York period — a climate accommodation that registers within a week of relocation.

**Vocalization at baseline.** Near-silent. Occasional sigh-grunt on settling. A low, conversational *huff* on greeting bonded humans — not a bark, more a respiratory punctuation. True barking is rare and reserved for threat-orientation; he is not a nuisance vocalizer.

---

## 2. INTIMACY / BONDED-CONTACT STATE

**Greeting routine, bonded human.** A four-beat sequence stabilizes across the published record: (1) head-up orientation with right-eye lock, (2) two-to-three step approach at a slow trot, tail in right-bias wag, (3) chest-press or shoulder-lean against the human's nearer leg, (4) head-tilt upward to allow the human's hand to find the top of the skull. He does not jump up. He does not paw. The lean-and-look is his signature contact-initiation, and it is the same with Barton, Bishop, and — over time — the broader West Coast circle.

**Lap behavior.** Will place his head, not his body, across a seated human's thigh. Body-on-lap occurs only with humans below a size threshold or in moments of acute human distress, when he upgrades from head-contact to full body-press. This escalation is one of the most reliable indicators in the file: a Pizza-Dog-in-your-lap reading equates to *the human is dysregulating*.

**Eye contact, intimate range.** Sustained soft gaze with the right eye, slow blink, occasional gentle head-bow. Avoids hard direct stare. The blind side is offered freely to bonded humans for ear-scratching, which is the household behavior most consistently depicted and the subject's most overt pleasure-display.

**Touch tolerance.** Extremely high with bonded humans. Will accept full-body handling, paw inspection, ear cleaning, collar adjustment without flinch. The left ear and the scarred orbit are *not* avoidance-zones — he allows contact there too, which is unusual for a trauma site and suggests either successful desensitization in the early Barton period or a constitutional pain-tolerance high enough to render the question moot.

**Sleeping arrangement.** Prefers to sleep within physical contact of a bonded human — against a leg, across feet, in the curve behind bent knees. When two bonded humans share a space, will rotate position across the night to maintain contact with each, a behavior most clearly depicted in mixed-household scenes. When the household is single-occupancy and the human is on a couch, he chooses the floor-adjacent position rather than the couch itself — an accommodation, not a preference.

**Play.** Restrained. Will engage in tug, gentle mouthing, and short retrieval bursts, but does not solicit play with the persistence of a typical retriever. Play episodes are short (under three minutes) and terminate cleanly. The dampened play-drive in a retriever-cross of his apparent age is mildly anomalous and is consistent with an organism for whom play was not a survival-relevant skill in early development.

**Vocalization, intimate.** The conversational huff; an occasional soft whuff-whine on the exhale when leaning against a bonded human; a rare, almost inaudible groan on deep contact-settle. No talking-back, no howling, no demand-barking.

---

## 3. ALERT / MILD-AROUSAL STATE

**Trigger threshold.** Low for olfactory novelty, moderate for auditory novelty, surprisingly high for visual novelty — consistent with monocular compromise and dominant-nose cognition. New scent in a familiar environment produces the most reliable alert posture.

**Alert posture.** Weight shifts forward onto the forepaws, hindquarters slightly elevated, tail straightens to horizontal and stills, ears forward (right leading), nostrils working in fast small inhalations (the *sniff-burst* pattern, roughly 4–6 Hz). The head pivots in the step-scan described above. The blind side is presented away from the source of interest by reflex now — a learned tactical orientation.

**Scent-investigation routine.** Approaches scent source in a curving arc rather than a straight line, keeping the right eye on the source through the approach. Final closure to within nose-contact range is preceded by a brief stop at approximately one body-length, a confirmatory sniff-burst, and then closure. This is a forensic-grade approach and is the same sequence shown in the *#11* murder investigation and in routine pizza-box approaches alike.

**Classification behavior.** Olfactory input is processed against the memorized library of human signatures (FRIEND / HAWKEYE / FOOD / BAD / SAD per the canonical schema, with finer gradations inferable). Classification appears to complete within two to four seconds of clean scent contact. The behavioral output of classification is immediate and discrete: tail-wag and lean for FRIEND, head-tilt and approach for SAD, body-still and ear-flatten for BAD, food-orientation for FOOD.

**Tells that the dog has noticed something the humans have not.** A brief, low *huff* (the same respiratory punctuation used in greeting, but downward-inflected); a head-turn toward the unnoticed thing followed by a check-back at the nearest bonded human; sustained orientation if the human does not respond. He does not bark to summon attention until the third or fourth check-back is ignored. This is a *patient* informant.

---

## 4. STRESS / SUSTAINED-ELEVATION STATE

This category is distinct from acute threat: it covers conditions of low-grade chronic stress — household conflict, prolonged human grief, environmental instability, the subject's own unresolved scent-puzzles.

**Postural signature.** Slight forward lean even at rest; shorter naps; more frequent position changes within a room (the dog *circulates*); a tendency to settle in doorways or thresholds rather than in the room interior — a sentry position offering scent coverage of two spaces at once.

**Panting.** Onset of light open-mouth breathing in thermoneutral conditions is the most reliable somatic stress index. The tongue does not fully loll; the panting is shallow, fast, and intermittent. Easily missed by humans.

**Appetite.** Preserved. The subject does *not* stop eating under stress — this is one of the cleanest distinguishing features versus a depressed or anxious phenotype. Food is, if anything, *more* sought during stress states; the food-as-comfort routine is one of his core affect-regulation mechanisms.

**Contact-seeking escalation.** Stress increases lean-and-look frequency. The dog will reposition to maintain physical contact with a bonded human more often than at baseline — every fifteen to twenty minutes rather than every forty-five. If the bonded human is the source of the stress (their dysregulation), he upgrades to head-on-lap and then to full body-press as described.

**The doorway-vigil.** Documented across multiple arcs: when a bonded human is absent for longer than the subject's expected return interval, he positions himself at the apartment door, head down on forepaws, sighted eye toward the door, and waits. This is not protest — there is no whining, no scratching, no destructive behavior. It is *vigil*. He can hold the position for hours. This is the closest the record comes to documenting separation distress, and its silence is the diagnostic point.

**Olfactory-puzzle behavior.** A scent that does not classify cleanly produces persistent goal-directed agitation: repeated returns to the scent source, increased sniff-burst frequency, decreased food motivation (the rare condition under which appetite falters), reduced sleep depth. Resolves only when the puzzle resolves. The *#11* arc is the canonical example; the same behavior, in miniature, can be inferred in any setting where a familiar scent appears in a wrong context.

---

## 5. THREAT / ACUTE-HOSTILITY STATE

**Threat-recognition routine.** Olfactory classification (BAD) plus postural threat-cues from humans produce a stacked confirmation. The dog does not react to weapons-as-objects; he reacts to weapons-as-carried-by-BAD-classified-humans. A bonded human handling a weapon produces no threat response; a BAD-classified human handling nothing produces full threat response. The classification is upstream of the object.

**Threat posture.** Weight back on the hindquarters (loaded for either spring or retreat), head lowered to shoulder level, ears flat to skull, tail straight and low (not tucked), lips closed but with a slight forward set of the muzzle. Hackle-raise along the neck and shoulders is present but modest — he is not a display-aggressive dog. The blind side is rotated *away* from the threat with high reliability; this is the most consistent tactical micro-pattern in his repertoire.

**Decision tree under threat.** The progression is: orient → confirm by scent → position between threat and packmate → vocalize (low growl, rare) → engage only on packmate-harm. He does not pre-empt. He does not bluff-charge. He does not bark-and-retreat. The threshold for active engagement is *visible harm to a bonded human*, and below that threshold his posture is interpositional rather than offensive.

**Engagement style, when threshold is crossed.** Direct closure, target the nearest limb, bite-and-hold rather than bite-and-release. The Ivan incident is the template: he crossed the street, took the leg, did not let go until physically removed. This is working-breed bite mechanics rather than display aggression. He fights to end the encounter, not to communicate within it.

**Pain response under engagement.** Minimal. The Ivan/car sequence documents continuation of bite-hold through impact. Pain-tolerance under attachment-driven engagement is anomalously high and is the single most important tactical datum in the file: this dog will not break off when injured.

**Post-threat recovery.** Rapid. Within minutes of threat-clearance, posture returns to baseline; within an hour, behavior is indistinguishable from pre-event. No observable rumination. No avoidance of the threat-site on subsequent passes. No conditioned fear acquisition to threat-adjacent cues (the car that struck him is not generalized to all cars). This recovery profile is unusual and reinforces the resilient-phenotype reading.

**Behavior in ambient cataclysm.** In environments of generalized violence not directed at his pack (firefights, building collapses, supernatural incursions), the subject demonstrates *flattened* threat response — alert but not engaged, oriented but not active. He has either learned that generalized chaos does not require his response, or his startle system has been recalibrated by chronic exposure. The latter is the likelier reading and is consistent with the chronic-over-arousal-as-baseline hypothesis.

---

## 6. GRIEF / WITNESSED-DISTRESS STATE

This is the subject's most distinctive behavioral domain and the one with the densest canonical record.

**Detection.** Onset of human grief is detected by olfactory shift before postural shift. The dog orients to the affected human within seconds of the change, well before visual or auditory cues would suffice. Cortisol-laden sweat, altered respiration, tear chemistry — the canine nose reads all of these, and this subject reads them with notable speed.

**Approach.** Slow, low-bodied, head down, ears soft (not flat), tail at low neutral with minimal motion. The approach is conspicuously *non-demanding* — he does not solicit attention, does not initiate play, does not seek food. He closes to within contact range and pauses, allowing the human to accept or decline contact.

**Contact pattern.** Head-on-lap if the human is seated; body-press against the lower leg if the human is standing; full lateral body-press alongside if the human is on the floor or in bed. Maintains contact for the duration of the human's distress episode without breaking. Will refuse food offers during this state — one of the only conditions under which his food drive is fully suppressed.

**Vocalization, grief-attendance.** A low single huff on settling against the human, then silence. He does not whine, does not nuzzle persistently, does not lick the face. The intervention is *presence*, not stimulation.

**Gravitational selection.** In a multi-human room, the dog selects the most-distressed individual with high reliability — even when that individual is not his most-bonded human. He has been documented prioritizing a grieving stranger over a calm packmate. This is the *therapy-animal phenotype arrived at without training* in operational form, and it is the most clinically interesting behavior in his repertoire.

**His own grief.** Underdocumented because under-expressed. The Grills sequence in *#11* contains the only direct evidence: persistent agitation, doorway-vigil at the deceased's apartment, refusal to leave the scent-source until the investigation completed. No vocalization, no anorexia past the puzzle-phase, no observable mourning ritual. He resolves grief through *action* — investigation, attendance to surviving humans — rather than through display.

---

## 7. VICTORY / RESOLUTION STATE

**Definition.** Post-conflict states in which the bonded pack is intact and the threat has cleared.

**Behavioral signature.** Tail-wag returns to right-biased rapid pattern; approach to each bonded human in turn for lean-and-look contact, in order of attachment hierarchy (most-bonded first); resumption of normal scent-scanning at higher tempo than baseline; food-seeking re-engaged at elevated intensity. He celebrates by *eating*. This is consistent across runs.

**Pizza behavior.** The canonical celebratory food. Approach to a pizza slice is paced and almost ceremonial — he does not snatch, does not gulp the first bite, often carries the slice a short distance before settling to consume. The deliberation suggests the food has acquired ritual significance beyond mere caloric value, which in turn suggests human-mediated reinforcement (Barton, Bishop, and others have consistently offered pizza as reward, and the dog has encoded the offering as relational rather than alimentary).

**Sleep depth.** Deepest, longest sleep episodes follow successful resolution states. Lateral recumbency is most reliably observed in the twelve hours after pack-reintegration. REM markers (paw twitches, eyelid flickers) appear with higher frequency.

---

## 8. DEFEAT / LOSS STATE

**Definition.** States in which a packmate is harmed or absent without resolution.

**Postural signature.** Lowered head carriage, slowed gait, reduced step-scan frequency (the head moves less, scanning less of the environment), tail at low neutral without motion. Lateral recumbency disappears; sternal recumbency with head-on-forepaws becomes the dominant rest posture, often at the threshold of the absent human's most-used room.

**The vigil reprised.** Where the stress-state vigil is patient and oriented to expected return, the defeat-state vigil is undirected — the dog will hold position not at the door but at a scent-anchor (the human's chair, bed, jacket). He absorbs the scent. He does not vocalize. He does not refuse food, but he eats less and more slowly.

**Replacement-attachment risk.** Within the absence window, the subject will accept and bond to a new caretaker on the same accelerated timeline he displayed with Barton in the first arc. This is the *promiscuously secure* attachment style in operational form: under loss, he does not collapse, he *re-bonds*. The behavior is adaptive and is also the signature of an animal who learned early that protest does not work.

**Reunion with a thought-lost packmate.** The greeting routine is amplified — same four-beat sequence, but with extended chest-press, sustained right-eye lock for longer than baseline, and a single audible whine on the contact. The whine is rare enough that its appearance is itself a marker: it is reserved for reunion after extended absence and does not appear in routine greeting.

---

## 9. NOVELTY / TRANSITION STATE

**Relocation behavior.** Inter-city and inter-household transfers (Bed-Stuy → Venice, Venice → various, and so on) produce a documented but mild transitional behavior: increased scent-scanning of the new environment over the first 24–48 hours, reduced sleep depth for the first three to five days, slight appetite reduction for the first 24 hours followed by full recovery. No destructive behavior, no inappropriate elimination, no escape attempts. Adaptation is complete inside a week.

**New-human introduction.** Approach is cautious-curious rather than fearful or eager. The dog closes to scent-range, completes classification, and produces the appropriate output. Classification of a new human as FRIEND occurs within minutes when the human's behavior is non-threatening and food or gentle contact is offered. Misclassification is rare and self-corrects on subsequent contact.

**Vehicle behavior.** Tolerant. No motion sickness depicted. Prefers floorboard or footwell over seat; this is likely a learned safety position from the Bed-Stuy era. Will orient through windows with sighted eye when stimulus warrants but does not display the persistent window-watching of an unsettled traveler.

---

## 10. MICROHABITS, TICS, AND RITUALS

A discrete catalog of repeated small behaviors that, taken together, fingerprint the subject across artistic interpretations:

- **The right-eye lock on entering a room.** Sweeps the room with a single step-scan, ends with the right eye on the nearest bonded human, holds for one to two seconds.
- **The threshold-pause.** Stops at every doorway for a single sniff-burst before crossing. Faster than a sit, slower than a walk-through. Consistent across environments.
- **The food-pause.** A two-to-three second still-and-orient on food presentation before approach. Originally a deprivation-trained behavior (Ivan would have controlled access), now stabilized as ritual.
- **The collar-shake.** On rising from rest, a single full-body shake initiated from the head, traveling caudally. The collar produces a characteristic jingle that bonded humans use as an auditory cue for his location.
- **The slow blink, sustained.** Bonded-human g


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS
## Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog" — Longitudinal Surveillance Synthesis

---

A week of continuous observation on this subject yields a dossier thicker than would be predicted for a quadruped, because the subject lives across two metropolitan areas, three primary handlers across the canon's span, and a rotating cast of secondary caretakers who each impose a different micro-schedule on him without ever managing to overwrite the substrate behaviors he established in the Bed-Stuy period. What follows is the composite week — Brooklyn-anchored, with Venice Beach variants noted — and the granular tics, postures, routes, and rituals that recur regardless of geography.

---

## I. THE DIURNAL SHAPE OF THE DAY

### 04:30 – 06:30 — Pre-dawn vigil

The subject does not sleep through the night in any environment on record. He sleeps in two long bouts (roughly 22:00–02:00 and 06:30–10:00) with a reliable middle waking that puts him on his feet between 04:30 and 05:00 regardless of season. The waking is not anxiety-driven — there is no whining, no pacing, no scratching at doors. It is a quiet sentry rotation. He stands, shakes once (a full-body shake initiated at the shoulders and propagating to the tail in roughly 0.6 seconds, audible as a collar-jingle that the bonded human has learned to sleep through), pads to the apartment door, lays his nose at the gap beneath it for between forty and ninety seconds — olfactory sweep of the hallway — then moves to whichever window faces the street, rests his chin on the sill if the sill is low enough or on the radiator cover if it is not, and watches the empty street for a span that lengthens in winter and shortens in summer. The good eye is to the glass. The blind side is to the room. This is a tell: he trusts the interior more than the exterior, and he has never, in ten years of canon, reversed this orientation at a window.

At Clint's Bed-Stuy building this puts him at the front-facing window above the awning. At Kate's Venice Beach office it puts him at the casement above the kitchenette with a partial view of the boardwalk. Surveillance from either position would record: ears in neutral half-cock, tail still, weight slightly forward on the front paws, one short exhale through the nose roughly every twelve to fifteen seconds. He is not waiting for anything specific. He is, behaviorally, on watch.

### 06:30 – 08:30 — Second sleep

Returns to the bonded human's bed or the foot of it. In the Bed-Stuy period he sleeps on the couch — never the bed, because Clint's couch is where Clint sleeps when Clint is decompensating, and the subject organizes his sleep around the human's actual location, not the designated furniture. In the Venice period he sleeps in Kate's bed proper, on her left side, sighted-eye toward the door. The shift between *couch-with-Clint* and *bed-with-Kate* is not a preference change; it is the same behavior — *be where the human is, oriented to threats* — expressed against different furniture geometry.

### 08:30 – 09:30 — First feed and elimination

The morning feed is the most ritualized act in the dog's day and the act in which his pre-rescue history is most visible. He waits. He does not bark for food, does not paw at the bowl, does not lead the human into the kitchen. He sits at the threshold of whatever room contains the food source, weight even on the haunches, and watches. If the human is slow he will produce a single soft exhale — not a sigh, a half-vocalized hh sound — and wait again. This is conditioned restraint: he was a Tracksuit asset and food was an instrument of control; he learned that proximity-without-demand was the safer posture. The behavior never extinguished after rescue.

The bowl itself is a contested artifact across handlers. Clint uses a dented metal mixing bowl on the kitchen floor near the radiator. Kate has, at various points, used a ceramic bowl with her own initials on it, a paper plate during travel, and the lid of a takeout container in field conditions. The subject eats from all of them with no observable preference, which is itself a datum — most domestic dogs develop bowl-fidelity within weeks. He has not.

Elimination follows feeding by twelve to twenty minutes and is conducted on a fixed route. In Bed-Stuy the route is: down the building's south stairwell (he refuses the elevator after one incident the surveillance record does not fully resolve, possibly an early-bonding-period startle), out the side door, left along the building face, across to the tree well on the corner of the cross street, marking at three fixed posts (the hydrant, the second tree, the sign-post outside the bodega), and a defecation site that has migrated only twice in canon, both times in response to construction on the original site. In Venice the route is shorter — out the office's back stairwell, across the alley, into the strip of sand behind the boardwalk planters — and he is more willing to vary it, which suggests a level of environmental safety in California that he never quite achieved in New York.

### 09:30 – 12:00 — Independent operations

The window during which the subject does his real work. He is, when not in active contact with a bonded human, a *building-scale forensic analyst* — this is what *Hawkeye* #11 makes explicit, and surveillance of any week shows the behavior continuing in attenuated form even when no mystery is active. He patrols. The Bed-Stuy patrol is documented and reproducible: down to the lobby, scent-check at the mailbox bank, a slow sweep of the hallway floor on the ground level, an investigative pause at apartment 2B (Grills's old apartment — he persists in this stop for years after Grills's death, which is the single most affectively significant datum in his daily routine), a quick check of the back stairwell, return. The patrol takes between thirty and fifty minutes depending on how many tenants he encounters and how many tenants he chooses to greet.

His greeting protocol is itself routinized: approach to within roughly four feet, sit, sighted eye on the human's hands, await acknowledgment. He does not jump. He does not vocalize. If acknowledged he will advance and accept contact; if ignored he will hold the position for ten to fifteen seconds and then withdraw without protest. The asymmetry of which tenants he greets and which he merely passes is a precise olfactory map of his FRIEND/NEUTRAL/BAD classification system, and it is stable over years.

In Venice the analogous behavior is dispersed across the office, the boardwalk, and the alley. He has FRIEND-classified at least three boardwalk vendors (a churro cart, a smoothie operator, and a particular busker whose case he sits beside in apparent companionship) and conducts a circuit of all three on the days the household routine allows it.

### 12:00 – 14:00 — Midday low

The dog's lowest-activity window. He selects a surface — the sun-square on the rug in Bed-Stuy, the desk-side dog bed in Venice, the back seat of any vehicle in transit — and engages a behavior best described as *attentive rest*. Eyes half-closed, ears forward, breathing slow but not sleep-rhythmic. He is monitoring. He can be roused instantly. He has been observed in this state through the firing of arrows in the next room, conversations conducted at shouting volume, and at least one visit by federal agents to the apartment, with no postural change beyond a single ear-rotation toward the door.

### 14:00 – 18:00 — Human-tracking phase

This is the longest behavioral window and the one in which the subject's *therapy-animal phenotype* operates most visibly. He locates whichever bonded human is most distressed and stations himself within reach of that human. The decision tree is observable: he enters a room, lifts his nose, conducts a two-to-three-second sniff, and proceeds — in roughly 85% of recorded instances — to the human whose cortisol output is presumably highest. He has chosen the human on the floor with a hangover over the human at the kitchen table working; the human reading a difficult letter over the human watching television; the human silently crying in the bathroom over the human laughing in the next room. The selection is reliable enough that handlers have come to use his trajectory as a diagnostic instrument for each other.

Position once selected is stereotyped: lateral recumbency against the human's leg if seated; chin-on-thigh if the human is in a chair; full-body press against the small of the back if the human is curled on a couch or bed. The blind side is always presented to the room; the sighted eye is always toward the human's face or the room's primary entry. This is not a behavior the dog modulates. It is structural.

### 18:00 – 20:00 — Evening feed and the pizza ritual

The second feed of the day, more flexible in timing than the morning feed because it is more often a shared meal with the human rather than a bowl. The pizza ritual is a documented daily-to-weekly event in the Bed-Stuy period and an attenuated weekly event in Venice. The behavior is precise: when pizza enters the apartment, the subject orients within roughly two seconds of the door opening (the box is olfactorily distinct from any other food the household receives), moves to a position three to four feet from the eventual sitting location of the human, sits, and waits. He does not approach the box. He does not jump. He will accept a crust from a hand and will accept a slice if placed on the floor, but he has been observed declining a slice when it was offered during a moment in which the human was crying, in favor of pressing against the human first and eating after — a sequence that, if it occurred in a primate, would be coded as deliberate emotional triage.

### 20:00 – 22:00 — Communal idle

The household's evening downtime. The subject is present but quiet. He has a small repertoire of evening behaviors: he will retrieve a single specific toy from a fixed location (a knotted sock in Brooklyn, a rubber ring in Venice) and present it for play exactly once per evening, and he will not re-present it if play is declined. He will request — by approach and a single muted vocalization — to be let onto whichever furniture the humans are occupying. He will tolerate being draped on, leaned against, and used as a pillow by visiting humans whom he has FRIEND-classified, and will quietly extract himself and relocate if such contact is initiated by a NEUTRAL-classified visitor.

### 22:00 – 04:30 — First sleep

He sleeps deeply in this window, with one observed exception: any time the bonded human leaves the residence after 22:00, the subject will not return to deep sleep until the human returns, and will be in an attentive-rest posture at the door or at the front window within ten minutes of the human's departure. He does not whine. He does not pace. He waits. The waiting has been timed to exceed six hours without behavioral degradation.

---

## II. WEEKLY-SCALE RITUALS

**The Grills stop.** Mentioned above; deserves separate treatment. Years after the events of *Hawkeye* #11, in any extended Bed-Stuy residence period, the subject continues to pause at the door of apartment 2B during the morning patrol. The pause is brief — eight to twelve seconds — and consists of a low scent-check at the door's threshold and a single soft tail movement. It is the only behavior in his repertoire that suggests something resembling commemoration. A surveillance file would log it as the most affectively significant repeated act of his week.

**The roof.** In the Bed-Stuy period the subject has access to the building's roof and uses it weekly or more, almost exclusively in the company of one of the Hawkeyes. He does not request roof access independently. He treats it as a shared site, and his behavior on the roof is markedly different from his street behavior: more exploratory, willing to walk to within roughly two feet of the edge and no closer, capable of sustained attention to the skyline for periods that exceed his attention span at street level. The roof is the only environment in which he has been observed lying on his back with the abdomen exposed — a posture he does not adopt indoors and never adopts in the presence of any human he has not FRIEND-classified.

**The car.** Long-distance vehicular travel is a recurrent event across the canon — Brooklyn-to-LA, LA-to-Brooklyn, intra-team movement with the West Coast group. The subject's vehicular behavior is anomalously calm. He selects the rear passenger floor by preference, the rear seat as second choice, and refuses the front seat unless lifted. He sleeps for the majority of any drive exceeding two hours and produces no anticipatory excitement on departure and no decompensation on arrival. The portability is total. It is also, on the diagnostic frame established earlier in this file, *too* total — the absence of any protest at relocation is the signature of an animal who learned that protest does not function.

**The bath.** Quarterly to monthly depending on caretaker. He does not resist the bath but does not enjoy it; his behavior is one of stoic compliance. He shakes once on entry into the water, holds still throughout, shakes thoroughly on exit, and seeks the bonded human within ninety seconds of being toweled. He does not roll in dirt after a bath, which is unusual for the breed phenotype and suggests either low scent-marking drive or — more likely on the evidence — a learned suppression of behaviors that produced negative consequences in the early-handler period.

**The veterinary visit.** Documented in canon as a recurring obligation Clint takes seriously, and one of the few obligations he takes seriously. The subject's behavior in the clinic is calm — he tolerates handling, accepts injections without flinch, does not vocalize. He does present one consistent tell on entering the clinic: he positions himself such that the blind eye is to the wall and the sighted eye is to the human, and he will not move from this position until the human moves first. This is the same orientation he adopts at home, intensified.

---

## III. MICRO-PATTERNS, TICS, AND TELLS

- **The half-turn.** Because of the left-eye loss, any stimulus arriving from the left flank triggers a compensatory head rotation of roughly 40–60 degrees. The rotation is fast (under 0.3 seconds) and is followed by a stillness of two to four seconds during which he is integrating the visual data. Over a decade he has trained the bonded humans to approach from his right; visitors who approach from the left produce the rotation reliably. It is the cleanest behavioral fingerprint he has.

- **The single soft exhale.** Documented above in the feeding context, but it appears in several others: when a human is slow to open a door he is waiting at, when a play offer is not accepted, when he is asked to move from a comfortable position. It is his *only* vocalized impatience marker. The absence of escalation past this exhale into a bark, growl, or whine, across all of canon, is one of the most clinically meaningful absences in his record.

- **The chin-press.** When seated beside a human in distress, he presses the underside of his jaw against the human's thigh or forearm with measurable pressure (visibly deforming clothing in panel art) and holds the position. The hold time correlates with the human's affective intensity. This is a learned regulation behavior that he has refined over years of use.

- **The food-pause.** Before accepting any new food item from a new human, he sniffs, looks at the bonded human's face, and waits for an acknowledgment cue (a nod, a verbal okay, or a hand gesture). Only then does he eat. This is not training — no caretaker has formally conditioned it. It is a residual safety behavior from the Tracksuit period, when food from unfamiliar hands was likely to be a control instrument.

- **The crowd disappearance.** In groups of more than five humans, the subject locates a low piece of furniture or a corner with a clear sightline and stations himself there, accepting greetings as they come to him but not seeking them. He will not work a room. He will hold a perimeter position and let the room come to him. This is the most introverted behavior in his repertoire and may reflect olfactory overload as much as social preference.

- **The orientation default.** When at rest, sighted eye toward the most-trusted human; when in transit, sighted eye toward the direction of motion; when on watch, sighted eye toward the threat axis. The blind side is consistently presented to whatever the subject considers safe. The orientation choices are continuous data on his threat-model in any given environment.

- **The non-bark.** He barks. He barks rarely. The recorded triggers, across the canon, number fewer than a dozen and cluster into two categories: (1) acute threat to a bonded human, (2) alerting a bonded human to a discovered scent finding (the Grills investigation produced several). He does not bark at the door. He does not bark at other dogs. He does not bark at the mail carrier. The economy of the vocalization is total, and it makes any instance of it diagnostically high-weight.

---

## IV. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD ACTUALLY YIELD

Compressed: a small, scarred, one-eyed dog rises before dawn, watches an empty street for half an hour, sleeps a second time against a human who is variously asleep or unconscious, eats with restrained patience, walks a fixed urban route with three marking sites and a memorial pause at a dead neighbor's door, conducts a building-scale olfactory inventory that has the structure of an ongoing case file, takes a midday rest that is not quite sleep, spends the long afternoon locating and physically supporting whichever human in his household is in the worst emotional shape, eats again — often pizza, often with a deferred-gratification ritual that triages the human's needs before his own — plays once briefly in the evening, allows himself to be used as furniture, and sleeps through the night unless his human leaves, in which case he does not.

He does not vocalize unnecessarily. He does not destroy property. He does not eliminate inappropriately. He does not show separation distress. He does not resist relocation. He does not refuse food, refuse handling, refuse strangers, or refuse work. He is, on the surface, the most cooperative subject this office has ever placed under observation.

The week's surveillance, read as evidence rather than as content, describes an organism whose entire daily architecture is organized around the regulation of other organisms' distress, with his own internal state subordinated to operational silence. The routine is not the routine of an animal who has things he needs to do. It is the routine of an animal who has people he needs to be near. Every fixed point in his week is a fixed point relative to a human; every tic is a tell shaped by an old handler; every absence in the behavioral record — no protest, no bark, no escalation, no refusal — is the negative space left by an early lesson that the things he might once have done did not work.

A surveillance team would close the week's log with the observation that the subject was no trouble at all. The analytical reader of that log would note that this is the finding, not the absence of one.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

## SUBJECT: LUCKY / "PIZZA DOG"
### Dossier Module 06 — Family of Origin, Foundational Bonds, and the Dead

---

A note before the entries. The subject is a dog. The concept of "family" must be operationalized in a species-appropriate frame: the bonded pack, the territorial co-occupants, the scent-imprinted progenitors and packmates of the early-life window. For canid attachment, the formative imprinting period closes long before the subject's first published appearance; everything observable in canon is post-imprint behavior, which means the original litter and dam are inferentially reconstructable only from defensive and orientation tells. We reconstruct them anyway, because that is what this file is for. Following the litter material, we map the first attachment proper (Ivan Banionis, the abusive handler), then the early Bed-Stuy co-located humans who functioned as honorary kin (Grills, in particular, who became the dog's first *grief*), and the cohort of secondary animal-presences that the record permits us to name. Romantic, vocational, and current-handler bonds are mapped in Module 07 (Relationships II); this section is concerned exclusively with origin material and the dead.

---

### 6.1 — THE DAM (unrecorded; reconstructed)
