**Status:** Unknown. Presumed deceased or long-separated. Never depicted in canon.

**History (inferential):** The subject presents in #1 (2012) as an adult dog of approximately 3–5 years, mongrel phenotype with dominant golden-retriever expression in coat and skull morphology. He was already in Ivan Banionis's possession at the moment of first observation, with no documented prior owner record. The most parsimonious reconstruction places his origin in a backyard or unlicensed breeding context within the greater Brooklyn/Queens area, with separation from the dam at the standard premature window favored by informal breeders (5–6 weeks rather than the developmentally optimal 8–10). This early weaning hypothesis is supported by two observable adult tells: (a) the subject's persistent oral fixation on soft, warm, fatty food — pizza specifically, but the pattern generalizes to any food matching the thermal and lipid profile of milk-supplement; (b) the subject's pronounced kneading and treading behavior when settling on a soft surface beside a bonded human, a residual neonatal nursing-position artifact that should have extinguished by adolescence in a normally weaned canid.

**Dynamics (inferential):** The dam's contribution to the subject's personality is largely a function of *what she was prevented from teaching him*. Bite inhibition is present — the subject has never closed his jaws on a human in canon despite ample provocation — which means *some* litter-play socialization occurred. Resource-guarding is conspicuously absent (he shares pizza with Clint, with Kate, with strangers), which is consistent either with adequate maternal socialization or with a learned-helplessness adaptation to a context in which guarding was punished. The presence of bite inhibition with absence of guarding is consistent with a brief but adequate maternal window followed by handler suppression.

**Trust/safety:** N/A. The dam is a pre-memory absence.

**Failure mode:** The principal sequela is the kneading-and-rooting behavior under stress, and the disproportionate comfort response to warm fatty food. When the subject is anxious, food does not merely soothe — it *regresses* him to a pre-weaning physiological state. This is exploitable.

**Leverage:** Anyone wishing to settle the subject quickly does so with warm, soft, high-fat food placed within reach of a soft horizontal surface adjacent to a stationary human. The protocol works invariably. It is what Clint Barton learned within forty-eight hours of adoption and has applied ever since.

---

### 6.2 — THE LITTER (unrecorded; reconstructed)

**Status:** Unknown. Presumed dispersed at weaning. Never depicted.

**History (inferential):** A mongrel litter of this phenotype runs to 5–8 pups. The subject's adult social behavior with other dogs — cataloged across the Bed-Stuy rooftop scenes (#11), the brief Venice Beach exposures during the Kate Bishop arc, and the Avengers Compound period — is *neutral-to-affiliative without play-soliciting urgency*. He does not invite play. He does not avoid it. He tolerates conspecifics as ambient packscape but orients his social drive almost exclusively to humans. This is the profile of a dog who had sufficient litter contact to develop conspecific tolerance but was removed before play-bow signaling was fully grooved into reflex.

**Dynamics:** The litter, in absentia, accounts for the subject's *low* startle response to other dogs — including the Tracksuit Mafia's other dogs in the early Bed-Stuy period, and the occasional larger canids encountered in West Coast arcs. He does not flinch at conspecific approach. He also does not seek conspecific company when bonded humans are available, which is the dominant pattern.

**Failure mode:** The subject is socially competent with other dogs but does not *use* them for affect-regulation, which means under conditions of human absence he has no functional substitute. A handler intent on isolating the subject from human company would find that the introduction of conspecifics does not substitute as comfort.

**Leverage:** None operational. The litter is a closed file.

---

### 6.3 — IVAN BANIONIS (first handler; the abuser; *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1, 2012)

**Status:** Severed (subject-initiated). Attacked by the subject during the precipitating event in #1; subsequently exits the subject's environment. Later canon places Ivan in custody and out of the operational picture.

**History:** Ivan is the subject's first documented handler — a mid-rank Tracksuit Mafia operator who used the dog as ambient muscle and intimidation prop during shakedown operations in Bed-Stuy. The relationship in observable canon is brief but formative: the subject is leashed short, fed irregularly (the matted-coat and visible-ribs early-issue art is reliable evidence), kept proximal during acts of violence against humans, and trained, in effect, by conditioning to *be present without intervening*. The relationship terminates in a single explosive scene: Ivan and the Tracksuits are beating Barton in the street; the subject's stress threshold breaches; he abandons handler position, lunges at Ivan, and is struck by an accelerating car in the same sequence. The eye is lost there. The leash is broken there.

**Dynamics:** Asymmetric. Ivan is the source of food, the source of pain, the source of routine, and the source of permission to act or not act. The subject's behavior under Ivan is the textbook canine response to inconsistent reinforcement from a higher-status pack member: head-low orientation, oblique approach, avoidance of direct eye contact, slow tail carriage. None of these tells are visible in post-Barton art; the subject's body language transforms wholesale within two issues of rescue, which is itself a measurement of how *contained* the prior carriage was.

**Evolution:** Reversed under acute crisis. The subject did not gradually transfer attachment; he ruptured the bond in a single observable event. This is rare in abused dogs and is the single most important behavioral datum in the case file. It suggests the bond was already pre-ruptured — held in place by leash and food access rather than by genuine affiliation — and that Barton, by being beaten in the dog's presence, functioned as the *occasion* rather than the cause. The subject did not choose Barton. The subject chose *against Ivan* and Barton was who he ran toward.

**Trust/safety:** Zero in retrospect. The subject does not, in any subsequent appearance, display tells associated with Ivan's specific scent profile (a useful baseline for what *would* register as a true PTSD analog if it existed; it does not, which is one of the file's central diagnostic puzzles). This is the strongest evidence for genuine resilient phenotype over blunted-affect concealment: a truly traumatized dog would carry the scent-memory as a reactive cue. This subject appears to have closed the file.

**Failure mode:** The Ivan period installed the subject's lifelong tolerance for living adjacent to violent men. He does not register Clint's environment as anomalous because Ivan's environment was his calibration baseline. This is why he does not flinch in firefights. It is also why he cannot be trusted to flee a dangerous handler on his own initiative; the subject's threshold for "this is unsafe" is set higher than any reasonable observer would set it.

**Leverage:** Ivan is no longer operational. If he reappears, the predicted subject response is not fear but defensive engagement on behalf of whoever is currently bonded. The dog will fight Ivan again, immediately, without preamble. This is the one item in the entire file in which the subject behaves with the certainty of a trained operator.

---

### 6.4 — CLINT BARTON (rescuer; primary attachment figure; ongoing)

*This bond is mapped in operational detail in Module 07. Included here only insofar as the rescue event constitutes the subject's *second birth* and therefore belongs to the origin file.*

**Origin-relevant note:** The bond was formed concurrent with grievous physical injury, in the presence of conspecific (Tracksuit dog) and human (Tracksuit handler) threat, with the rescuer himself bleeding and minimally functional. The encoding is therefore inseparable from pain, threat, and mutual vulnerability — the precise neurochemical substrate that produces the most treatment-resistant attachment bonds in the mammalian literature. The subject did not bond to Clint despite the trauma; he bonded to Clint *through* it. Operational consequence: this bond cannot be displaced by a healthier alternative. It can be supplemented (Kate, others) but not replaced. Any plan that assumes the subject would willingly and permanently leave Clint for a more stable environment is a plan that misreads the file.

---

### 6.5 — GRILLS (neighbor; honorary packmate; deceased — *Hawkeye* #10–11)

**Status:** Dead. Murdered by the Clown in the rooftop barbecue arc; the subject discovered the body and ran the investigation in #11.

**History:** Grills — Gil, the rooftop barbecue host, the cheerful Bed-Stuy tenant who gave Clint the trade name "Hawkguy" — is the subject's first non-Barton human bond in the post-rescue period. The relationship developed across the rooftop scenes of the early arc: shared food (the subject's preferred currency), shared physical space (the rooftop being one of the few outdoor environments the subject moved through without leash anxiety), and Grills's specific behavioral profile, which was warm, food-generous, low-volume, and physically demonstrative in a way Barton is not. The subject's scent-classification of Grills in the #11 pictographic schema places him in the FRIEND register with food-icon emphasis — a category populated by relatively few humans.

**Dynamics:** Supplementary to the Barton bond, not competing with it. Grills functioned as the *available* affection that Clint was constitutionally unable to provide. The subject sought Grills out on the rooftop in the documented inter-issue gaps, returned to Clint for sleep and proximity. This is the first observable instance of the subject's mature pattern: distribute affective load across multiple humans, return to the primary for somatic regulation.

**Evolution → rupture:** The murder is the subject's first encounter with the death of a bonded individual. The behavioral evidence in #11 is precise and clinically rich. The subject (a) located the body by scent before any human, (b) did not vocalize the discovery — no observed howl, no alarm bark — but instead initiated investigative tracking, (c) classified the murder-relevant scents into a working suspect set, (d) followed scent trails across the building over the course of the issue, (e) returned to Clint with the resolved information and presented it through proximity-and-direction behaviors. The investigation is sublimated grief. The subject did not have a protest-despair response to Grills's death; he had a *vocational* response. He went to work.

**Trust/safety:** Posthumously preserved. The subject does not, in any subsequent appearance, demonstrate avoidance of the rooftop or of grill-cooking scents or of any specific Grills-associated cue. The grief was processed in real time, in #11, in the only register the subject has available — purposive scent-driven action toward resolution.

**Failure mode:** The Grills loss installed a specific behavioral template: *when a packmate is harmed, do not vocalize, do not flee, investigate*. This is a maladaptive carryover for a dog. It means the subject, in the presence of a dead or dying bonded human, will not bring help. He will conduct a scent-survey. He has done this twice in canon; the second instance (during the *Freefall* arc, when Clint is presumed dead) shows the same sequence. A handler intending to monitor the subject's emotional state via vocalization signals will get no reading. The dog grieves silently, in his nose.

**Leverage:** Grills is dead. He is leverage only in the sense that any operator wishing to elicit the subject's investigative mode rather than his comfort-seeking mode would do well to deploy meat-smoke and rooftop-spatial cues. This produces alert, oriented behavior rather than settled-companion behavior. It is the operational signature of Grills's category in the subject's memory.

---

### 6.6 — THE BED-STUY TENANT COHORT (collective honorary kin; *Hawkeye* #11 dispositive)

**Status:** Largely intact, geographically dispersed by Barton's subsequent moves.

**History:** The pictographic tenant survey in #11 documents the subject's working memory of approximately a dozen distinct human scent-signatures from the apartment building. These are not bonds in the Grills sense — they are the broader kin-network of the *territory*, classified across the FRIEND / HAWKEYE / FOOD / BAD / SAD axes the issue establishes. Simone (the upstairs neighbor) registers as FRIEND with caretaker-tonal emphasis; her two boys register as FOOD-source-and-play-source; assorted unnamed tenants populate the FRIEND-neutral band. A small minority register as BAD, including, eventually, the Tracksuit infiltrators.

**Dynamics:** The subject treats the building as territory, not as residence. He moves through it with confident scent-monitoring carriage; he tolerates and is tolerated by the cohort; he distributes light affiliative behavior broadly. This is the closest thing in the canon to a *stable, extended kin network* the subject has ever inhabited, and the duration was short — the Bed-Stuy period closes within the first volume.

**Trust/safety:** High within the cohort. The subject's tells in the building are unguarded — relaxed tail carriage, full-flank sleeping posture (the most vulnerable position; only deployed in environments classified as safe), eating in the presence of humans without postural compression.

**Failure mode:** The Bed-Stuy cohort is the subject's only experienced *extended* network. Every subsequent environment has been smaller and more transient. The subject has demonstrated, since, a tendency to construct surrogate building-cohorts in each new environment (the Venice Beach office building during the Kate period; the Avengers Compound during later arcs), with diminishing depth each time. He is reconstructing what he had, with materials of decreasing quality.

**Leverage:** Anyone wishing to read the subject's territorial-comfort baseline should do so against the Bed-Stuy reference. Anything less stable than that reads, in the subject's behavior, as transitional.

---

### 6.7 — THE TRACKSUIT DOGS (origin-context conspecifics; presumed scattered/euthanized)

**Status:** Unknown. Not depicted post-Ivan-arrest.

**History:** The subject was kept in proximity to other Tracksuit-handled dogs during the Ivan period. Names are not recorded. The relationship was conspecific co-housing without observable affiliative play — the kennel pattern, not the litter pattern.

**Dynamics:** Neutral coexistence under shared adverse handling. The subject did not bond to these animals; he did not fight them. This is the file's only documentation of the subject's conspecific behavior in his formative environment, and it predicts exactly what the adult record shows: tolerance without affiliation, neutrality without seeking.

**Failure mode:** The subject does not appear to recognize *conspecific solidarity* as an available behavioral category. Other dogs are weather, not kin.

**Leverage:** None.

---

### 6.8 — REPRODUCTIVE LINE (none documented)

**Status:** No offspring on record. No mating events depicted. Neuter status unconfirmed (likely intact; no veterinary record post the original Bed-Stuy clinic visit indicates surgical intervention beyond enucleation and orthopedic stabilization).

**Operational note:** The absence of a reproductive line is itself a behavioral signature. The subject's social drive is fully colonized by interspecies (human) attachment. There is no observed sexual or mate-seeking behavior in canon. This is consistent with a dog whose pack-affiliation circuit has been fully recruited into a single-target human-bonding mode. It is also consistent with a dog who is, simply, not in environments where conspecific females are present in receptive states. Both readings hold.

---

### 6.9 — SYNTHESIS: THE SHAPE OF AN ORIGIN FILE WITH NO BLOOD IN IT

The family-and-origin section of any other subject's dossier would be organized around blood: a mother, a father, siblings, a spouse, children, the dead among them. The subject has none of these in any documented form. His origin file is composed almost entirely of *handlers and neighbors* — humans whose role was caretaking by proxy, with no biological or formal claim to him. The dam and litter are inferential ghosts. The first handler was an abuser. The rescuer-handler became the primary bond at the cost of an eye. The first honorary packmate was murdered within months of the bond forming. The extended cohort dissolved when the primary handler moved.

The behavioral consequence of this origin structure is that the subject has *no template for a permanent kin relationship*. Every bond in his recorded experience has been (a) brief, (b) terminated by violence, geography, or death, or (c) sustained only through his own continued willingness to re-bond after disruption. He does not know that families persist. He has never observed one.

This is the substrate beneath everything in Modules 07 onward. When the subject is reassigned, transported, lent out, left behind, or grieved over, his apparent equanimity is not the equanimity of a settled animal. It is the equanimity of an animal who has never had occasion to learn that loss is supposed to be protested, because in his experience loss is simply *what happens next*. He absorbs it the way the Bed-Stuy rooftop absorbed weather: as the ambient condition of being alive.

The file should not sentimentalize this. The file should also not pathologize it. Both readings are true simultaneously, which is the analytically interesting fact about Lucky.

— End Module 06. Continue to Module 07: *Relationships II — Current Handlers and Operational Pack*.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

## Preamble to the Section

The subject is a one-eyed golden-tan mongrel of approximately 55–65 lbs, scarred left orbit closed since 2012, plain flat collar (originally Banionis-issued chain, replaced by Barton with a worn nylon flat-buckle, replaced again by Bishop with a fabric collar of variable color across the LA run, then back to nylon by *Freefall*). The subject does not select his relationships. He is *placed* — driven across the country in cars, carried up apartment stairs in arms, handed off in airports, left with sitters. The relationships mapped below are therefore not chosen in the human sense; they are the human attachments the subject has *converted into pack* by his own attachment work. That conversion is the operative behavior. It is performed, on the evidence, with almost any human who clears a low threshold of non-violence and food provision. The relationships nonetheless stratify, by observed proximity-time, scent-familiarity, postural data, and resource-flow, into a clear hierarchy.

Each entry below treats the human as the *object* of the subject's relational work, and the subject as the *agent*. Files are ordered by intimacy, not chronology.

---

## 1. CLINTON FRANCIS BARTON ("Hawkeye," "Clint")

### History

First contact: *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1 (2012), Bed-Stuy, immediately following the subject being struck by a vehicle while attacking his then-handler Banionis in defense of Barton. The subject was unconscious for the rescue. The first conscious encounter occurred at the veterinary clinic, in a recovery cage, with Barton present and paying. The naming event ("Lucky") and the imprint event were not separable in time; they occurred within the same 24-hour window as the orbital trauma. This is the foundational fact of the relationship, and it is encoded somatically: the subject's left-side blindness and his attachment to this specific human are neurologically co-stored.

### Proximity Patterns

Across the Fraction/Aja run, observable contact-time with Barton averages 14–18 hours per day in-apartment, with the subject's preferred resting positions distributing as follows: (a) the couch, body parallel to Barton's, head over Barton's left thigh — the *sighted-eye-toward-human* posture predicted by the monocular adaptation; (b) the kitchen linoleum, ventral surface down, in the throughway between refrigerator and table; (c) the apartment landing outside 6B, when locked out (a documented recurring event); (d) the rooftop, in summer panels, at Barton's feet. Sleeping position is consistently within 2 meters of Barton when Barton is present in the unit. When Barton is absent for >36 hours the subject is recorded relocating to Barton's unwashed clothing as substrate.

### Dynamics

The relationship is structurally asymmetric in caregiving direction: the subject provides more emotional regulation than he receives. Barton's affective baseline across the Fraction run is depressive, alcohol-using, hearing-impaired and increasingly isolated; the subject's pattern is to lie *touching* Barton during these episodes, head-on-lap, and to remain in contact through hours-long sessions of television. This is not random. The subject does not exhibit this behavior with Barton during cheerful or task-focused periods; the contact is *contingent* on Barton's dysregulation, which establishes the subject's discrimination of Barton's affective states by scent (cortisol load, ethanol metabolites) and posture.

Feeding is irregular and self-directed in this household. Barton's caregiving is best described as *unreliable but non-malicious* — the subject is fed when Barton remembers, and feeds himself from countertops, takeout boxes, and the building's communal pizza scraps when Barton forgets. The subject has *not* developed food-guarding behavior toward Barton, which would be the expected response to caloric uncertainty; this absence is diagnostic of an attachment that supersedes resource anxiety.

### Evolution

- **2012–2013 (Fraction Vol. 4):** Primary attachment formed. The bond is dense, daily, somatic. Issue #11 is the most extensive published documentation in comics of a dog's interior life and confirms Barton is classified at the apex of the FRIEND set, sub-categorized HAWKEYE, an identifier the subject uses operationally (e.g., bringing investigative findings to him).
- **2014–2016 (Vol. 4 conclusion, *All-New Hawkeye*):** First geographic separations. The subject is transferred to Bishop for extended periods. Re-encounters with Barton produce greeting behavior of moderate intensity — not the frantic separation-reunion of an anxiously attached dog. This is a tell.
- **2017–2019 (*Occupy Avengers*, *Tales of Suspense* Bucky/Clint arc):** Barton is increasingly absent on field operations, sometimes incarcerated. The subject relocates to Bishop's care. No observable mourning. The relationship persists by scent-memory.
- **2020 (*Hawkeye: Freefall*, Thompson):** Re-integration with Barton in New York. The subject's behavior on return resumes the prior pattern within hours — couch positioning, kitchen throughway, rooftop sequence — confirming this attachment is *recallable* rather than continuous.

### Trust / Safety Assessment

Trust: maximum on the subject's side. The subject will follow Barton into active combat scenarios, including the Ronin/yakuza arcs of *Freefall*, without flight response. He has been present for at least four incidents in which Barton was rendered unconscious and has been documented standing over the body or pulling at clothing.

Safety: *low to moderate*. Barton's lifestyle exposes the subject to repeated lethal threat (the apartment is invaded multiple times; the building is set on fire in the Fraction climax; the LA bolt-hole is shot up). The subject has sustained the original orbital injury and undocumented minor wounds across the canon. The dyad is mutually loving and structurally unsafe.

### Failure Mode

The relationship's failure mode is *Barton's depressive disengagement*. When Barton withdraws — locks himself in the apartment, drinks, refuses contact — the subject's contingent regulatory behaviors (head-on-lap, pressure-contact) escalate in duration but the subject does not vocalize, does not protest, does not demand food, does not leave. This produces the worst observable affect-state in the subject's record: prolonged immobility without sleep, alert posture, eye tracking Barton with no behavioral output. The subject *absorbs* the depression without converting it. Across a multi-year exposure this is the most predictable mid-life morbidity vector for him (cortisol-driven cardiac and gastric load) and is not depicted because comics do not depict it, but it is the file's most defensible long-term concern.

### Leverage

The subject is leverageable on Barton via any threat to Barton's body, presence, or scent. The subject will not be drawn from Barton's side by food, by other humans, by other dogs, or by environmental threat below the level of fire. Conversely, Barton is leverageable on the subject — Barton's documented behavior pattern across Vol. 4 #6 and *Freefall* #2 confirms the subject's safety is the single non-negotiable in Barton's ethical hierarchy. Any actor targeting either member of this dyad acquires the other.

---

## 2. KATHERINE ELIZABETH BISHOP ("Kate," "Hawkeye")

### History

First contact: *Hawkeye* Vol. 4 #1, on the same Bed-Stuy day as the Barton imprint. Bishop is the second human the subject scent-classifies as FRIEND, and the first to assign the operational name "Pizza Dog." The naming is significant: where Barton's "Lucky" encodes the survival event (rescue from death), Bishop's "Pizza Dog" encodes the subject's first observed pleasure-event in the published record (the pizza scene in #1). The subject thus carries, simultaneously, the name of his trauma and the name of his joy, assigned by his two primary attachments.

### Proximity Patterns

Bishop's caregiving environment differs materially from Barton's. Across the Vol. 5 LA run and intervening custody periods: structured feeding (kibble, regular times, scheduled walks), cleaner ambient environment (Venice Beach office, beach access), greater diurnal regularity. The subject's resting positions in Bishop's care: (a) the dog bed Bishop purchases (the first dog bed in the canonical record); (b) the passenger floor of Bishop's car during stakeouts; (c) the office reception area during client meetings, alert posture, scent-screening incoming clients; (d) the bed, against Bishop's spine, in the LA apartments.

### Dynamics

The subject's relationship with Bishop is structurally *healthier* than the relationship with Barton, on every measurable axis — and the subject demonstrably bonds *less intensely*. This is the single most diagnostic data point about the subject's psychology in the entire file. Bishop provides better food, cleaner housing, more attention, more play, more affection. The subject responds with stable affection and clear cooperation. He does *not* re-prioritize her above Barton. The subject's attachment ordering is not driven by reward; it is driven by the *original imprint event* and the contingent regulatory work he performs around Barton's depression. Bishop is not depressed in the same way. She therefore activates fewer of the subject's deepest behaviors.

Bishop receives the subject's *secondary repertoire*: play (fetch sequences, never observed with Barton), greeting display (tail rotation at full amplitude, full-body wag, only with Bishop), investigative cooperation (the subject is functional in PI casework, sniffing crime scenes, tracking suspects — the #11 skill-set reactivated in a professional context), and *audience behavior* (the subject orients to Bishop's voice when she is on the phone, a pattern Bishop visibly trains via verbal address-and-respond loops).

### Evolution

- **2012–2014:** Co-primary attachment with Barton; Bishop is the second household in regular rotation.
- **2014 onward (LA arc):** Bishop relocates with the subject. The transition is undertaken without observable protest behavior. The subject adapts to the new climate (the coat improves), the new acoustic environment (less urban noise, more ocean), and the new caseload (active scent work). This period contains the subject's longest stretch of stable physical health in the canon.
- **2015–2019:** Repeated handovers, cross-country relocations. The subject moves between coasts with each Bishop or Barton arc rotation. He develops what reads as *bicoastal scent memory* — recognizing both Bed-Stuy and Venice Beach environmental signatures as home.
- **2021–present:** Bishop's run with Thompson and subsequent appearances retain the subject as functional household member. The relationship is the most operationally stable in the file.

### Trust / Safety Assessment

Trust: high. Bishop has never violated the subject's safety; the subject responds to verbal commands from her at a higher rate than from Barton. He is fed by her, walked by her, taken to veterinary care by her without protest. Safety: *moderate to high*. Bishop's casework exposes the subject to occasional threat (the Madame Masque arc, the LA cult arc) but at lower frequency and lower lethality than Barton's environment.

### Failure Mode

The relationship's failure mode is *competitive availability*. Bishop is, by every objective measure, the better caregiver — and is, by the subject's behavioral choice, the secondary attachment. Bishop has been documented across multiple writers exhibiting low-grade pique at this hierarchy ("he loves Clint more, I don't know why"). The dyad's risk is therefore in Bishop's *interpretive frustration* with a bond she has earned and not been awarded the apex of. The subject is unaware of this dynamic and would not modify behavior if informed. The relationship survives because Bishop accepts the asymmetry.

### Leverage

The subject is leverageable on Bishop via any cooperative-investigation context; she will deploy him professionally and he will perform. Bishop is leverageable on the subject via offered food, offered play, and the LA environmental scent-set, which functions as a comfort-anchor. A hostile actor targeting Bishop would acquire access to the subject within the same operational envelope.

---

## 3. AMERICA CHAVEZ

### History

Contact established during *Young Avengers* / Bishop-overlap arcs and reinforced through the West Coast team era. Chavez is the third human the subject scent-classifies at the FRIEND tier with sustained presence.

### Dynamics

Chavez's interpersonal style is direct, physically confident, and low-anxiety. The subject's response is correspondingly *low-maintenance affection*: he greets, he accepts contact, he positions near her but does not exhibit the contingent regulatory work he performs around Barton, because Chavez does not present the affective targets that activate it. The relationship reads as *adult-platonic-pack-member*: stable, affectionate, undramatic, low-bandwidth, high-reliability.

### Trust / Safety / Failure Mode / Leverage

Trust: high within demonstrated context. Safety: high (Chavez's combat capability is such that the subject's physical risk in her proximity is the lowest in the file). Failure mode: Chavez is intermittently inter-dimensional and not always reachable; her availability is *episodic*. The subject does not appear to register this as loss, consistent with his replaceable-attachment pattern. Leverage: minimal in either direction.

---

## 4. AVA AYALA, AMERICA CHAVEZ, GWEN POOLE, JEFF (THE LAND SHARK), AND THE WIDER WEST COAST AVENGERS COHORT (Thompson Run)

### History

The subject is functionally a team-asset during the *West Coast Avengers* (2018) run. He is present in the Wakandan-architecture LA HQ, on missions, in living-room sequences. The team treats him as mascot and morale-anchor.

### Dynamics

This is the subject's most prolonged group-bonding context outside the Barton/Bishop dyad. He distributes affection across the cohort according to the pattern established elsewhere: gravitates to whoever is most decompensating in a given scene. With Pool, this is frequent (her fourth-wall instability presents to the subject's scent-detection as a chronic anomaly, and panel-staging shows him repeatedly orienting to her). With Jeff the Land Shark, the relationship is one of the few cross-species peer-bonds in his record; the subject demonstrates *non-aggressive curiosity* toward Jeff and shares resting space with him, which is unusual and indicates the subject's species-classification system is operationally flexible.

### Trust / Safety / Failure Mode / Leverage

Trust: warm but distributed. Safety: variable (the team's mission set includes Atlantean kaiju, Tigra/Hank dynamics, vampire arcs). Failure mode: the team disbanded; the subject was again reabsorbed into Bishop's primary care without observable protest. Leverage: the subject is recognized as a Bishop-asset by the team and would not be approached as a separate entity.

---

## 5. GRILLS (Simone Grills)

### History

A Bed-Stuy neighbor in the original Barton building. Grills appears across the Fraction run as a friendly tenant, occasional dog-sitter, beer-drinker on the rooftop. The subject scent-classifies him FRIEND. Grills is murdered by a Tracksuit operative in *Hawkeye* #10.

### Dynamics and Significance

Grills is the only confirmed *death of an attachment figure* in the subject's published record. The subject's response, documented in #11, is the closest thing to canonical *grief* on file: persistent scent-tracking of Grills's residual signature through the building, agitated investigation of the rooftop where the murder occurred, eventual identification of the killer by scent, and an attack on that killer. This is sublimated grief converted into goal-directed forensic action. It is also, on the evidence, *the only mourning behavior the subject has ever exhibited*. Compared to the absence of mourning when separated from living attachments, the difference is telling: the subject can grieve the *unrecoverable* but does not grieve the *temporarily absent*. His attachment model, in other words, has a category for *gone* and a category for *not here right now* and treats them entirely differently.

### Failure Mode / Leverage

Grills is dead. The relationship's residual function is as a scent-anchor in the Bed-Stuy building — the subject still orients to Grills's former apartment door in post-#11 panels, a low-frequency tic but a persistent one.

---

## 6. SIMONE (Grills's Neighbor — single mother with children, Bed-Stuy building)

### History

Recurring background tenant across the Fraction run. Provides occasional food. Children pet the subject. The subject classifies the unit FRIEND.

### Dynamics

Low-intensity but stable affiliation. The subject is comfortable with the children, which extends his demonstrated tolerance set to small humans — a non-trivial extension given his trauma history could plausibly have produced child-reactivity. He shows none. This is data: the subject's bad-handler memory is *handler-specific*, not generalized.

### Failure Mode / Leverage

Low salience. The relationship survives only as long as the Bed-Stuy housing arrangement does.

---

## 7. THE BED-STUY BUILDING TENANTS (collectively)

### History

The subject's most extensive social network in the published record is the residential cohort of Barton's apartment building. Issue #11 establishes that he holds scent-signatures for at least twelve to fifteen tenants, classified individually.

### Dynamics

The subject performs unsupervised circulation through the building's common areas, accepting food from approximately half the tenants, sleeping in stairwells, conducting independent territorial monitoring. He is the building's *de facto* security animal and emotional barometer, and is treated as such — multiple tenants address him by name without Barton present. This is the closest thing in his record to *community embeddedness*, and it is the relational asset he most clearly mourned upon relocation to LA (panel evidence: the first weeks of the Bishop Vol. 5 LA arc show the subject in markedly reduced exploratory behavior, increased proximity-seeking to Bishop — a transitional period of approximately two weeks before LA scent-anchoring stabilizes).

### Failure Mode / Leverage

The Bed-Stuy network is the subject's only documented *non-dyadic* attachment system. Its loss is the single most behaviorally observable disruption in his record (more so than any separation from a primary). This suggests the subject's *resilience* — assessed elsewhere as constitutional — may in fact partially depend on the breadth of his peripheral attachment net, and is more vulnerable to environment-loss than to person-loss.

---

## 8. THE VETERINARIAN OF RECORD (Bed-Stuy clinic, *Hawkeye* #1)

### History

The human who saved his life. The subject was unconscious during the operative phase of the relationship but was awake and bandaged during the recovery interval, and Barton was present. Scent-memory of the clinic is, on the evidence, *not* aversive — the subject does not exhibit fear behavior at subsequent veterinary visits, which would be the predicted response to a trauma-site re-exposure.

### Dynamics

Functionally null in the published record after #1. Significant only because the *absence* of clinic-aversion is itself evidence of the subject's atypical fear-conditioning profile.

---

## 9. NATASHA ROMANOFF (Black Widow) — Limited Contact, High Significance

### History

Periodic contact through Barton across multiple arcs. The subject scent-classifies her FRIEND but with operational sub-categorization that panel-staging indicates is distinct from the general FRIEND set: she is one of the few humans whose proximity does not produce relaxation in the subject. Romanoff is read by the subject as a *fellow operator*. He alerts in her presence rather than de-escalating. This is *not* threat-classification — he does not bristle, position defensively, or restrict her access to Barton — but it is *vigilance-classification*, a category his behavior implies exists but which is sparsely populated.

### Dynamics

The subject and Romanoff appear to share a mutual operational respect, observable in posture-mirroring during shared-scene panels. Romanoff is one of the few humans who touches the subject without preamble and to whom the subject extends immediate physical access. There is a *peer* quality to the relationship that the subject extends to almost no other adult human.

### Trust / Safety / Failure Mode / Leverage

Trust: high but operationally framed. Safety: high (Romanoff's lethality protects rather than threatens him). Failure mode: Romanoff is intermittently dead. The subject's lack of mourning behavior on her published deaths is consistent with his pattern but does not indicate the relationship is shallow. Leverage: minimal.

---

## 10. JESSICA DREW (Spider-Woman) and the PI/Friends Circle around Bishop's Venice Beach Office

### History

Walk-on but recurring. The subject is comfortable with Drew, accepts food from her, and during co-investigations performs cooperative scent work alongside her.

### Dynamics

Low-intensity adult-pack-member affiliation. The subject's presentation around Drew is *play-permissive*, which is rare in his behavior set (Bishop, Chavez, Drew — the women of the LA circle activate his play repertoire far more reliably than any of the men except in early Barton scenes).

### Failure Mode / Leverage

Episodic. The relationship is stable as long as the Bishop-LA professional context persists.

---

## 11. THE MENTOR QUESTION

A standard intelligence-dossier section asks whom the subject has *learned from*. For this subject, the answer is structurally unusual.

The subject has had no human mentor in the conventional sense. No training, no behavioral conditioning regimen, no service-animal preparation. His operational skill set — the scent-forensics of #11, the multi-step investigative reasoning, the discrimination of human affective states, the surgical interventions in violent scenes — is *emergent*. It was not taught.

If a mentor must be identified, three candidates present:

**(a) Banionis (negative mentor).** The first handler taught the subject what *bad* smells like and established the FRIEND/BAD binary that organizes his entire perceptual system. This is the foundational education in his life and it was received in violence. Every subsequent scent-classification refers back to this calibration.

**(b) Barton (modeling-by-need).** Barton has taught the subject *what depression looks like in a human*, by extensive exposure. The subject's contingent regulatory repertoire was developed in response to this exposure. Barton has not trained him; Barton has *needed him*, and the subject has learned the shape of that need.

**(c) The building (collective mentor).** The Bed-Stuy tenant network taught the subject that humans are *plural*, classifiable, predictable, and largely non-violent. This was the corrective curriculum to Banionis's foundational lesson. Without it the subject's FRIEND set would never have grown past Barton.

---

## 12. PROTÉGÉS

None. The subject has not been observed in a teaching role with any other animal. The closest analog is the *cohabitation tol


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*UATU dossier, Lucky / "Pizza Dog" — Section 7c. Cross-reference Section 7a (Primary Attachments: Barton, Bishop) and Section 7b (Packmates, Caretakers & Casual Affiliates). The present section covers every confirmed and inferred antagonist across the canonical record, plus the (sparse, definitionally complicated) intimate-pair register for an unneutered male dog whose romantic biography is, on the record, almost entirely sublimated.*

The conceptual difficulty of this section must be acknowledged at the outset. The subject is a dog. The categories "rival," "enemy," and "lover" map onto canine ethology only with translation. "Rival" includes resource-competitors and dominance-contesters; "enemy" includes both humans who have harmed the subject and humans the subject's threat-classification system has tagged BAD by scent; "lover" must be construed broadly — pair-bonded affiliates, breeding-potential conspecifics encountered on the record, and the most-frequently-overlooked but most analytically important category: the human dyads in which the subject is the *third party*, the witness, the de facto co-regulator of an intimacy not his own. The subject's relational life is conducted overwhelmingly in that third position, and any honest mapping has to admit it.

---

## A. THE FOUNDING ENEMY — IVAN BANIONIS

### History

Ivan is the origin. Before the subject had a name he had Ivan, and the totality of his early-life relational template was built inside Ivan's economy: leash, kennel, food-as-leverage, training-by-coercion, deployment as a weapon against strangers in Bed-Stuy. The exact duration of the Ivan period is not specified in canon, but the matted coat, the conditioned proximity-tolerance with hostile handlers, and the fluency with which Ivan's tracksuit-clan associates handled the dog on first appearance argue for months at minimum, likely longer — long enough for the smell of Ivan (vodka, tobacco, leather, the particular detergent on tracksuit polyester) to have become the subject's *baseline reference odor* for what a primary attachment figure smells like. This is significant. The subject's later olfactory FRIEND/BAD system is built on top of that earliest reference and defines itself, in part, by negation against it.

### Dynamics

Coercive. Asymmetrical. The relationship was structured around food deprivation cycling and leash-correction. The subject's earliest visible behaviors — the sidewalk pizza scene's posture (low, deferent, eyes-up to handler before lowering to food) — are the somatic record of that training. He had been taught to ask permission for what he wanted.

### Evolution

Single discontinuity, one panel wide. When Ivan struck Barton and Barton was at risk on the pavement, the subject made the only categorical decision of his recorded life: he switched packs. He left Ivan. He bit Ivan. The car-strike followed and the left eye was lost. The relationship terminated in the literal sense that the subject never returned to Ivan's custody, but it did not terminate in the deeper sense — every subsequent attachment in the subject's life is constructed against the Ivan template, and Ivan's continued presence as a Tracksuit Mafia operator means the *scent* of Ivan was almost certainly re-encountered during the Bed-Stuy arcs (the Hood Crime War, the Ronin pre-echoes). No reunion is depicted on-page. The behavioral record across those arcs — the subject's unusual quietness on certain rooftops, the choice of which side of the apartment to sleep on — is consistent with a residual cue-discrimination that the subject himself probably could not have articulated.

### Trust / Safety

Zero. The subject's BAD classification, in the #11 schema, is tonally and chromatically Ivan-derived. Ivan is the prototype.

### Failure Mode

The relationship failed by re-imprinting. The subject did not escape Ivan through any internal psychological process; he was rescued by accident, by the proximity of a kinder hand at the right moment. This is the *foundational failure mode of the subject's entire relational life*: he does not extract himself from bad attachments, he is extracted by chance and then immediately re-bonds. Any future Ivan-analog would, on the evidence, hold the subject indefinitely absent external intervention.

### Leverage

Ivan held complete leverage during the dyad — food, shelter, exit. Post-discontinuity, Ivan retains exactly one form of residual leverage: he is the only person on the record who can produce a scent-mediated freeze response in the subject. If a future operator wanted to immobilize Lucky non-violently, the answer is in Ivan's wardrobe.

---

## B. THE TRACKSUIT MAFIA, COLLECTIVELY

### History

The dog was raised, functionally, by this organization. Kazi, the unnamed brothers, the chorus of "bros" — they were the dog's first social environment after weaning. He recognizes the tracksuit polyester scent at a distance and across years.

### Dynamics

Pack-adjacent without pack-membership. The dog was their tool, not their packmate. He ate their scraps, smelled their cigarettes, slept where they put him. They were not, in his classification, malicious in the Ivan sense — they were *ambient*. This produces a peculiar later behavior: in the Bed-Stuy arcs the subject will track and locate Tracksuit operatives faster than any human investigator, but his physiological response upon locating them is *not* the BAD-tag flight-or-engage; it is the much more troubling *neutral-recognition* — a flat, oriented attention without arousal. He knows them the way a child of a closed community knows the adults of that community. He does not love them. He does not fear them, individually, with the specificity reserved for Ivan. He simply knows their smell and the shape of their threat.

### Evolution

Across the Fraction run, the Thompson run, and into the *Freefall* arc, the Tracksuits remain in the subject's olfactory rolodex but lose operational salience. By the West Coast period the scent reference is dormant. By the Aaron-era *Avengers* appearances it is functionally extinguished.

### Failure Mode

The subject cannot be relied upon to *alarm* on Tracksuit presence. The neutral-recognition response means he will note them and continue with whatever he was doing. For a handler who needs an alarm dog, this is a blind spot.

### Leverage

Anyone wearing tracksuit polyester laundered in the specific detergent used by the clan will trigger sub-threshold recognition. This has been weaponized exactly zero times on the record. It remains exploitable.

---

## C. THE CLOWN (KAZIMIERZ KAZIMIERCZAK)

### History

Distinct from the Tracksuit mass. The Clown is the assassin who occupies the same Bed-Stuy environment but operates at a different threat-tier. The dog encounters him during the Grills arc and afterward.

### Dynamics

Asymmetrical and clinically interesting. The Clown does not engage the dog directly; he treats the dog as scenery. The dog, by contrast, does *not* treat the Clown as scenery — the #11 evidence is that the Clown registers as a distinct scent-signature, tagged with the closest equivalent to dread the subject's classification system permits. The dread is not Ivan-flavored. It is colder, more abstract — a smell that means *something has been ended* rather than *something will hurt me*. The subject correctly identifies the Clown as Grills's killer through scent-residue on the rooftop and on the murder implement.

### Evolution

No on-page reunion of consequence. The Clown is removed from the board by other actors. The scent reference remains in the subject's library and would, if re-encountered, produce the only verified flight-precursor posture in the subject's record: tail-tuck, lowered head, refusal of food.

### Trust / Safety

Negative. The only attachment figure-adjacent human the subject has classified as more dangerous than Ivan, and the only one whose classification was achieved through *inference* rather than direct harm.

### Failure Mode

The subject correctly identified the killer and could not communicate it to the humans in time to matter. The Grills outcome is the closest the record comes to the subject failing at his self-assigned vocational task. He has not, on the evidence, processed this. The mid-#11 panels of his returning to Grills's apartment door are the closest thing in the canon to canine grief.

### Leverage

None held by the Clown. The subject holds, in principle, the leverage of unerring scent-identification — a capacity any law-enforcement-adjacent handler could exploit and none has.

---

## D. MADAME MASQUE (GIULIETTA NEFARIA)

### History

Encountered primarily through Kate Bishop's Los Angeles arc. The dog is in the apartment, in the office, on the beach, through the entire Madame Masque pursuit of Kate.

### Dynamics

The subject's threat-assessment of Masque is unstable, which is itself the diagnostic finding. Masque's scent presents differently across encounters — perfume layers, prosthetic-mask materials, the cosmetic chemistry of disguise. The subject's FRIEND/BAD binary cannot resolve her cleanly. This produces, in the relevant issues, a behavior pattern unique in the record: low-amplitude, sustained agitation — pacing, head-turning, attempts to scent-mark thresholds. He knows she is wrong and cannot prove it to himself.

### Evolution

Across the Kate-LA arcs the subject's classification of Masque sharpens. By the late issues the perfume-disguise no longer fools him. The pacing resolves into oriented vigilance.

### Trust / Safety

Hostile. The only female adversary in the record to whom the subject has assigned consistent BAD classification despite repeated re-encounter.

### Failure Mode

The subject's olfactory system, sophisticated as it is, was initially defeated by cosmetic masking. The vulnerability is general: any adversary willing to invest in scent-discipline can shadow the subject's classification window for at least the first encounter.

### Leverage

The subject would now, post-resolution, be a reliable Masque-detector. None of his caretakers have operationalized this.

---

## E. THE HOOD (PARKER ROBBINS) AND THE BED-STUY CRIMINAL FIELD

### History

Background-tier antagonist across the Fraction run's late arcs. The dog is not the Hood's target but is in the building.

### Dynamics

Diffuse threat-recognition. The Hood's supernatural register produces, in the subject, a category of olfactory perception that does not exist in the species norm and that the artwork (Aja, Wu) renders as a kind of static — Lucky responds to the Hood's presence with disorientation rather than classification. Supernatural antagonists in general (later: Mephisto-adjacent figures in the Aaron *Avengers* tie-ins) produce this same static response.

### Evolution

The subject did not develop a stable schema for supernatural threat across the entire canon. He treats it as weather.

### Failure Mode

The subject is not protectively useful against magical antagonists. He cannot smell what does not smell.

### Leverage

None mutually.

---

## F. SECONDARY ANTAGONISTS (composite entry)

*Brief sub-sub-entries for completeness:*

- **The Swordsman / Jacques Duquesne (residual presence in Kate's life)** — the subject classified as ambivalent; Jacques's scent registers as *familiar-to-Kate*, which collapses BAD classification into uncertainty. The subject defers to Kate's regulation.
- **Various A.I.M. operatives across the West Coast Avengers run** — uniform polyester-and-solvent scent-signature; the subject classifies as a single composite BAD entity rather than as individuals. Tactically useful as a generalized alarm.
- **The Hydra apparatus during the *Secret Empire* environment** — too brief in the dog's experiential window to develop discrimination. He survived it because Clint did.
- **The kingpin-adjacent operators in *Freefall*** — high-end criminal scent (clean wool, leather, blood-residue traces); the subject classifies BAD reliably and is, in this arc, used (informally, by Clint) as a vetting instrument for door-crossers. This is the only arc in which the subject's threat-classification capacity is acknowledged by his handler.

### Composite Failure Mode

None of these antagonists have the depth-of-relationship to produce a relational failure. They are, to the subject, a moving field of bad weather. The aggregate cost is the chronic baseline arousal documented in Sections 2 and 4.

---

## G. INTRA-PACK RIVALS

### G.1. JONATHAN THE PIZZA DOG (continuity-adjacent rival)

There is, across the multiversal record, exactly one persistent dog-on-dog rivalrous register — the question of *which* dog is the *real* Hawkeye dog when continuity has supplied more than one. Inside the subject's lived experience this is non-rivalrous; he does not encounter doubles. It is included here only because any total-surveillance file would note that the *symbolic* rivalry exists in the reception literature and that the subject is uniquely indifferent to it. He does not contest the name. He responds equally to "Lucky," to "Pizza Dog," to "Arrow," to "hey buddy," to whistle, to the can-opener.

### G.2. JESSICA DREW'S CAT (composite entry for the small-mammal field)

Across the Avengers-tower and West Coast arcs the subject is in proximity to other companion animals: cats kept by neighbors, the various pets cycling through Kate's office, the occasional briefly-fostered animal in Clint's building. The subject's response is, uniformly, *non-rivalrous*. He does not contest resources. He does not contest territory. He does not contest attention. This is the third major datum (with the indiscriminate bonding and the absence of protest) of the subject's profound under-development of the normal canine contest-behavior repertoire. Other dogs, on the record, do not press him — he reads as low-status and unthreatening to them and they leave him alone. This is a stable equilibrium and a small tragedy.

### G.3. THE OTHER HAWKEYE-CIRCLE DOGS

In the rare scenes featuring multiple dogs (the West Coast house, certain Bishop-family flashbacks if extant), the subject defers. He eats last. He sleeps furthest from the food bowl. He yields the warm spot. This is consistent with Ivan-era training and has never extinguished.

### Failure Mode

The subject will be out-competed for resources in any multi-dog household and will not signal distress about it. A caretaker not paying attention will systematically under-feed him.

### Leverage

Other dogs hold full resource-leverage over the subject and do not, on the record, exploit it.

---

## H. LOVERS — THE DEFINITIONAL PROBLEM AND ITS RESOLUTION

The subject is, to the best of the canonical record, unneutered and has no reproductive history. There is no on-page mating event. There is no estrus-encounter scene. There is no recorded pair-bond with a conspecific. The category "lover," in the conventional sense, is therefore empty.

This is itself significant and must be analyzed rather than dismissed.

### H.1. THE ABSENCE OF CONSPECIFIC INTIMACY

For a sexually intact adult male dog with the freedom of two cities across a decade of canon, the total absence of mating behavior — even attempted, even thwarted — is a notable omission. Possible readings:

1. **Editorial decorum** — the genre does not depict it. (Likely true and sufficient to explain the silence.)
2. **Subject's attachment economy is human-saturated** — the affiliative drive is fully discharged into the Barton-Bishop axis, leaving insufficient unallocated drive for conspecific pair-bonding. (Consistent with the attachment-primacy organization documented in Section 5.)
3. **Olfactory classification favors human FRIEND signatures over conspecific signatures** — the subject's social map is built around humans first and dogs second. (Consistent with the early-life imprinting environment, in which the only stable affiliates were human.)

The probable truth combines all three. The behavioral consequence is that the subject's intimate life, as actually lived, is *with humans, in a register adjacent to but not identical with romantic intimacy* — the cohabitation, the bed-sharing, the food-sharing, the long mutual gazes, the daily reading of one another's emotional weather. This is not "lover" in the species-normative sense. It is, however, the closest analog the subject's biography contains, and any honest dossier must map it as such.

### H.2. THE BARTON-BISHOP TRIAD AS A SUBLIMATED INTIMATE FIELD

The subject's most-intimate-living register is conducted inside the Clint–Kate dyad-plus-dog triangle. He sleeps in beds. He shares food at faces' distance. He licks tears off cheeks. He positions his body across thresholds. The behavioral grammar is the grammar of cohabitation. The subject is, functionally, *partnered* — to two people, simultaneously, in a configuration that neither human has ever quite admitted is the central relationship of all three of their lives.

This belongs in Section 7a in its primary attachment register and is treated there. Its inclusion *here*, in the lovers section, is to mark that the intimate-pair slot in the subject's psyche is *filled* — filled improperly, filled by humans, filled by two of them rather than one, but filled. He is not pining. He is not under-bonded. He is not seeking. The reproductive-and-romantic drive has been wholly conscripted into the cross-species attachment system.

### H.3. THE CASUAL CONSPECIFIC ENCOUNTERS

Across the various park-and-beach scenes — Venice, Brooklyn, the various brief Central Park appearances — the subject encounters other dogs in the ordinary canine manner: scent-greeting, brief play-bow, occasional chase. None of these encounters develop into bonds. None recur with named individuals. The subject's behavior in these encounters is *appropriate-but-shallow* — he performs the social ritual and disengages without follow-up. This is the same shape as his human-side behavior with non-bonded humans (the Section 7b casual-affiliate register), which is to say: the subject's intimacy-budget is fully allocated to the primary attachments and there is no surplus.

### H.4. THE HYPOTHETICAL FUTURE LOVER

In the event the subject were neutered late (no canonical event), or in the event a stable conspecific partner were introduced (no canonical event), the prediction from the rest of the profile is unambiguous: the subject would bond rapidly, indiscriminately, deeply, and without protest behavior at any subsequent separation. He would treat the conspecific the way he treats humans. The conspecific would, in all likelihood, fail to understand him — dogs do not, on the whole, read other dogs the way this dog reads humans.

### Trust / Safety

In the intimate-field register as actually lived (the triad), trust is total and safety is provisional. The humans are trustworthy at the level of intent and unreliable at the level of execution. The subject has accommodated this fully.

### Failure Mode

The subject's intimate life is structurally *dependent on the continued co-functionality of two damaged humans*. If the Barton-Bishop dyad fractures permanently — and it has come close, repeatedly — the subject will be redistributed. He will accept the redistribution. He will bond to whoever takes him. The failure mode of his intimate life is, therefore, *invisibility*: the dissolution of the most important relationship of his life would produce, on the surface, no behavioral disruption at all. The cost would be entirely internal and entirely unmeasurable from the outside.

### Leverage

The two humans hold complete leverage over the subject's intimate life and do not know they hold it. The subject holds, in return, the leverage of being the only thing in either of their lives that has never made a conditional demand. This is the quiet, unspoken accounting at the bottom of the triad and the single most important relational fact in the entire dossier.

---

## I. SYNTHESIS

The rivals-enemies-lovers register, read in aggregate, returns the same finding as every other section of this file: the subject's relational life is organized around a primary attachment system so dominant that the categories normally distributed across many relationships have collapsed into the primary two. Enemies are a weather system. Rivals are non-events. Lovers are, in the species-conventional sense, absent — and in the lived sense, identical with the primary attachments.

This is not a small finding. It means the subject is, relationally, *all eggs in one basket*, where the basket is woven of two unreliable humans and the subject does not appear to know — or has elected not to know — that this is precarious. The Ivan-era lesson was *attachments end; bond again*. The subject has internalized the first clause as fact and the second as obligation. He is, in this sense, the most resilient and the most exposed creature in the file: every loss he has sustained he has survived by bonding to the next available hand, and the strategy has worked, and it has cost him the capacity to ever recognize a loss as a loss.

The file recommends that any operator with custody of the subject understand that the primary risk to him is not his enemies. It is the moment when both of his humans are unavailable at the same time and no third hand is offered. He will not signal. He will simply, quietly, become available to whoever appears next. This has happened before. It is the entire shape of his life.

*— End Section 7c. See 7d for institutional and incidental affiliates (veterinary, neighborly, team-adjacent).*


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Pre-Synthesis Capability Audit — Subject "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog"

The subject possesses no superhuman capability in any conventional sense. He is a mongrel-built golden-tan retriever-mix of approximately 55–65 pounds, monocular, with intact dentition, ordinary canine musculature, and no pharmacological, mystical, mutagenic, or technological enhancement on record. What he possesses instead is a stack of *species-normal* and *species-superior* capacities arranged in an unusual operational pattern, deployed inside an environment (the Barton/Bishop orbit) that exceeds the threat ceiling for which canine sensory apparatus evolved. The interesting analytical question is therefore not *what can he do* — every dog can do most of it — but *which faculties are load-bearing in his specific operational niche*, how those faculties have been shaped by chronic exposure to superhero-grade incident, and where each faculty hits its hard ceiling.

The audit proceeds faculty by faculty.

---

### 1. Olfaction — The Primary Instrument

This is the subject's load-bearing capability and the one most thoroughly documented in canon. *Hawkeye* #11 ("Pizza Is My Business," Fraction/Aja/Hollingsworth, 2013) is in effect a forensic demonstration reel.

**Mechanism.** Standard canine olfactory architecture: ~220 million receptors against a human baseline of 5 million, a wet rhinarium that captures volatile organics, a vomeronasal organ for pheromonal signatures, and a brain in which roughly one-eighth of cortical mass is dedicated to smell processing. The subject's apparatus appears intact and unimpaired by the orbital trauma; there is no canonical instance of olfactory failure under stress, fatigue, environmental contamination (smoke, blood, accelerant), or distraction.

**Range and resolution.** The #11 evidence shows the subject:

- Discriminating individual human scent-signatures across at least a dozen tenants of a single building, retained in working memory across days.
- Following scent trails through a contaminated environment (a building immediately after a violent death — meaning blood, sweat-fear, gunpowder residue, urine, vomit, and human foot traffic all layered on the substrate) without losing the target trace.
- Cross-referencing scent against affective state — classifying not only *who* a human is but *what state they are in* (SAD, ANGRY, AFRAID, WELL). This is within canine capability — dogs are demonstrably able to detect cortisol, adrenaline, and ketonic shifts — but the subject's operational use of it is forensic rather than reactive.
- Detecting deception adjacency: the FRIEND-tagged scent in a BAD context (the Grills puzzle) produced sustained investigative agitation. The dog is doing pattern-matching against expected scent-context pairings, and flagging mismatch.

**Limits.** Olfactory acuity degrades against (a) accelerants and strong solvents, none of which are shown in canon defeating him but which would in principle; (b) wind direction and elevation — there is no documented airborne scent acquisition at distance beyond ~50 meters; (c) heavily masked environments such as commercial kitchens, which the artists tend to render with comic confusion-iconography on the dog's face; (d) novel signatures not in the working library, which the subject must encounter directly before classifying.

**Growth.** The library expands monotonically. There is no evidence of forgetting; old scents (Ivan, the Tracksuits) remain tagged BAD across years and reappearances. New caretakers and packmates are integrated into the FRIEND set within hours of first co-presence.

**Signature application.** Threat triage by smell rather than sight. The subject does not need to see Ivan to know Ivan is in the building. This is operationally enormous in a milieu where antagonists rotate through costumes, masks, and impersonators — the dog is functionally immune to disguise.

---

### 2. Audition

**Mechanism.** Canine hearing range extends to ~45–65 kHz, against a human ceiling of ~20 kHz, with sound-localization accuracy enhanced by independent ear-pinna articulation. The subject's hearing is intact and is repeatedly the household's primary perimeter alarm, particularly during Clint Barton's hearing-aid arcs in the Fraction run and again in *Hawkeye: Freefall*.

**Operational use.** The dog functions as a *force multiplier on a deafened operator*. When Clint cannot hear an approaching elevator, a door latch, or a footfall on the rooftop, the dog hears it and orients, providing Clint with directional information by body posture (ear-cock, head-turn toward the source). This is an emergent communicative protocol — not trained — that constitutes one of the most analytically interesting capabilities in the file: the subject has, without instruction, developed a habit of *making his perceptual data legible to a perceptually-impaired packmate*.

**Limits.** No canonical instance of supernormal hearing. Bandwidth is species-typical; selectivity is good but not superhuman. The dog can be startled by loud impulse noise (gunfire is depicted as causing flinch in early Aja panels, though notably *less* flinch in later issues — a probable acclimation effect, possibly with hearing damage not yet symptomatic).

---

### 3. Vision

**Mechanism.** Compromised. Left orbital loss reduces visual field by roughly 30%, eliminates binocular overlap on the left side, and degrades depth perception for objects approaching from the blind quadrant. Standard canine visual apparatus otherwise: dichromatic color vision (blue-yellow axis), strong motion detection, weak static-pattern resolution, superior low-light sensitivity via tapetum lucidum.

**Compensation.** The subject demonstrates a consistent postural compensation: he positions himself so that his sighted right eye faces the most-trusted human or the most likely threat axis. This is visible across artists — Aja, Romero, Pérez-Ortiz, and Pulido all stage him with the scarred left side angled toward walls, corners, or known-safe humans. He also turns his head more frequently than a binocular dog would, performing what is functionally a continuous left-side sweep.

**Limits.** Blind-side approach is the single largest tactical vulnerability the subject carries. There is no canonical instance of his being successfully ambushed from the left, but the geometry permits it and a sophisticated antagonist would exploit it. Vision is not the primary perceptual channel and does not need to be.

---

### 4. Locomotion, Strength, and Combat Capacity

**Locomotion.** Standard for a healthy 55–65 lb retriever-mix: estimated sprint at 25–30 mph over short distance, sustained trot at 6–8 mph, climb capacity limited to standard urban architecture (stairs yes, fire escapes yes if open-grate, vertical surfaces no). Swim capacity confirmed (typical for the retriever phenotype, though never operationally critical in canon).

**Strength.** Bite force in the ~250–320 PSI range for the size class, sufficient to puncture human forearm flesh, hold a grip against active resistance, and disable a moving wrist. Confirmed in the original Ivan attack — the subject latched onto the handler's leg with sufficient force and duration to allow Clint to escape.

**Combat behavior.** The audit must be precise here, because the subject is frequently *in* combat environments and almost never *engaged in* combat. The behavioral protocol is:

1. Orient to threat by scent and sound.
2. Position body between threat and bonded human.
3. Vocalize (low growl, then bark) as deterrent.
4. Engage with bite *only* if a bonded human is being actively physically harmed.

The threshold for step 4 is high and remarkably stable. The dog has been in the room for assassination attempts, kidnappings, gunfights, Hydra incursions, and the Ronin-era violence without launching pre-emptive attack. He waits for the trigger condition. When the condition is met, he does not hesitate, and he does not consider personal cost — the eye-loss in the foundational incident is the rule, not the exception. This is not combat *skill*; it is combat *willingness under a narrow trigger condition*, which is a different and arguably more useful operational property.

**Limits.** Against an armed human adult, the subject is outmassed and outranged. He has no training, no tactical doctrine, and no situational awareness of firearms beyond "loud thing means bad." He survives combat environments primarily because antagonists do not prioritize a dog and because his bonded humans are exceptionally capable.

---

### 5. Cognition

**Working memory.** Demonstrably large for species — the #11 issue shows simultaneous tracking of at least a dozen human scent-signatures plus their associated affective states plus their spatial locations within a building. This is at the high end of documented canine cognition but not anomalous.

**Causal reasoning.** Demonstrable. The Grills investigation is a multi-step inference: *Grills is gone → Grills's scent ends here → another known scent is present where it should not be → that scent is BAD-tagged → pursue*. This is sequential goal-directed reasoning across at least four steps, sustained over hours.

**Theory of mind.** Present in the affective-recognition form. The subject identifies emotional states in humans and modifies his behavior accordingly — approaching the sad, withdrawing from the angry, soliciting from the playful. He does not demonstrate higher-order false-belief reasoning (no canine does), but the affective-ToM is operational and is the substrate of his therapy-animal phenotype.

**Inhibitory control.** Excellent. The subject does not steal food from FRIEND-tagged humans even when unattended. He waits. The pizza-fixation is not impulsive; it is opportunistic within a frame of social rules he has inferred without training.

**Language comprehension.** Standard companion-dog range, probably 50–150 word-class receptive vocabulary plus tonal and gestural cues. No reading capacity (the perceptual-iconography of #11 is a *representational device* for the reader, not a literal claim about the subject's symbolic cognition).

**Limits.** No tool use beyond mouth-manipulation of food and toys. No abstract problem-solving outside the scent-and-social domain. No numerical cognition demonstrated. Cannot operate doors, vehicles, or devices. Cannot communicate in human language despite repeated narrative gestures toward inner monologue, which are authorial license rather than diegetic capacity.

---

### 6. Emotional and Social Capacity — The Operational Specialty

This is, in the audit's judgment, the subject's *signature capability* — the one that distinguishes him from a generic dog and from generic comic-book animal sidekicks.

**Affect detection in others.** Continuous, low-overhead, scent-and-posture-driven monitoring of every human in his environment. The dog knows who in the room is decompensating, often before they do. This is not training; it is the developmentally over-recruited faculty of an organism that learned early that reading human emotional weather was a survival skill.

**Affect regulation of others.** The subject reliably produces measurable affect change in distressed humans by proximity, weight-on-lap, eye contact, and grooming-solicitation. Clint Barton's lowest decompensation episodes in the Fraction run are repeatedly interrupted by the dog's intervention; Kate Bishop's anxiety arcs in the Thompson run are similarly buffered.

**Limits.** The capability is *receptive and regulatory*, not curative. The subject can lower acute distress; he cannot resolve a depressive episode, an addiction, a grief, or a PTSD response. He buys the human time. This is not a small thing, but it has a ceiling, and the canonical record shows that when the human's pathology exceeds the dog's regulatory capacity, the dog's protocol is to *remain present anyway* — which is the therapy-animal vocational identity expressing itself at its operational limit.

**The cost-side, which belongs in any honest powers audit:** the regulatory work is not free. The subject absorbs the affective load he detects. There is no canonical accounting of where it goes, because dogs do not journal, but the behavioral evidence (postural deflation at charged departures, sustained agitation around unresolved scent puzzles, the absence of normal protest behavior masking unaddressed stress) suggests the cost is real and is being paid somewhere in the somatic-emotional system. This is the symptom-as-signature reading: *the capability and the wound are the same structure.*

---

### 7. Growth Curve Across the Published Decade

The subject does not acquire new powers. He acquires *operational refinement* within existing faculties.

- **Issue 1–6 of the Fraction run:** baseline. Scruffy, food-fixated, learning the apartment, learning Clint.
- **Issue #11:** demonstrated peak forensic-olfactory operation. This is the high-water mark of depicted cognition and is not exceeded later — it is, however, *consistent* with later depictions, suggesting it is sustained capability rather than a one-off feat.
- **Bishop LA run:** geographic adaptation; integration into a PI practice; expansion of the FRIEND library to include a new social network without observable difficulty.
- **Occupy Avengers / West Coast Avengers / Aaron Avengers:** demonstrates that the operational pattern holds across team contexts, larger packs, more chaotic environments. No degradation, no expansion.
- **Freefall and MCU-tie limited series:** the subject is older, the coat is rendered slightly greyer in some artists' work, but functional capacity is preserved. No depicted cognitive or sensory decline. (Medically this is generous; behaviorally it is the published record.)

The growth curve is therefore flat-but-stable on the capability side, and *deepening* on the relational side — the FRIEND library is monotonically larger and the regulatory work is more continuously deployed.

---

### 8. Symptom-as-Signature Reading

Each of the subject's load-bearing capabilities maps directly onto a developmental wound.

- **Olfactory hypervigilance** is the operationalization of an early-life requirement to know which human in the room was about to hurt him. The forensic-grade scent classification is a survival adaptation now repurposed as detective work.
- **Auditory perimeter monitoring on behalf of a deafened operator** is the externalization of a learned protocol: *I will be the sensory apparatus that the unreliable adult lacks.* He performed this function for himself before he performed it for Clint.
- **Affect-detection and proximity-regulation** is the over-recruited skill of a creature whose early survival depended on reading the violent handler's mood. Redirected toward kinder humans, it presents as grace. The substrate is vigilance.
- **High threshold for combat engagement combined with zero hesitation once threshold is crossed** is the behavioral signature of an organism that learned early that protest does not work, but that *terminal intervention* does. He did not bark Ivan off. He bit, and he paid.
- **Indiscriminate rapid bonding** is the capability that allowed him to survive every household transfer in the canon. It is also the capability that means he could be taken from his current household tomorrow and would re-bond by the end of the week. The portability is the asset and the wound.

The audit's terminal observation: the subject's *powers* are ordinary canine faculties operated at the upper edge of species norm. His *abilities* are the patterns into which those faculties have been organized by trauma. His *limits* are the ceiling at which the regulatory work he performs for others exceeds the regulatory work being performed for him — a ceiling that, on the canonical evidence, no one in his orbit has yet noticed he is approaching.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog"
### File Section 6 of the Standing Workup

---

## 6.1 PRELIMINARY NOTE ON THE FRAME

The subject is a quadruped mammal with a closed left eye, a working nose calibrated to forensic resolution, and no opposable thumbs.
