**GIVEN:** Encounter with unknown human, child or adult, who reaches to pet.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Permits contact, leans into it, does not retreat from the blind side even when the hand approaches from the left. This is *clinically notable* — most monocular dogs develop left-side defensive flinch. The subject has not. Reading: trust generalization to humans outranks the protective instinct that monocular vision would normally generate. Consistent with reactive-attachment indiscriminate-subtype subsyndromal flag.

**GIVEN:** Encounter with a visibly distressed stranger on the street (crying, sitting against wall).
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Will pull toward them. Will sit within two feet without contact-initiation unless invited. *Basis:* the gravitation-toward-distress pattern, which is the most reproducible single behavior across all writers from Fraction to Thompson to Aaron.

**GIVEN:** Encounter with a person whose scent matches a previously catalogued BAD signature (e.g., tracksuit-adjacent cologne, similar adhesive/cigarette/diesel profile).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Stops dead. Hackles low but visible along shoulders only. Soft growl below 40 Hz, almost subaudible. Does not advance. Will not move forward on leash until physically guided past, and will reorient backward as the human walks on. *Basis:* the splitting-defense classification system; the Ivan-trauma encoding.

---

## C. THE HOUSEHOLD — DOMESTIC RITUAL

**GIVEN:** Bonded human enters with groceries.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Nose-survey of bags within 15 seconds; no theft; positions at the cupboard or refrigerator the food is destined for, providing logistical commentary by stare.

**GIVEN:** Bonded human enters in unusually low affect (slow gait, head down, no verbal greeting).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Greeting protocol *shortens*. Does not perform full enthusiasm display. Instead, approaches at a walk, makes one nose-contact with the hand, then withdraws to a flop-position within five feet, oriented sighted-eye toward the human. Waits. *Basis:* the somatization defense; the documented affect-mirroring pattern.

**GIVEN:** Bonded human enters with new injury (limp, sling, bandage).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Olfactory inspection of the wound site, with restraint — sniff, no lick — followed by lying down on the injured side of the body, forming a flank-buffer. This is inferential but follows from his consistent pattern of *positioning between the vulnerable and the room*.

**GIVEN:** Two bonded humans co-present in the apartment.
**EXPECT (MODERATE-HIGH):** Will distribute time approximately 60/40 to the more dysregulated of the two, measured in continuous contact-minutes. Will physically relocate when the distress-load shifts. The dual-attachment system documented across the Fraction and Bishop arcs predicts this allocation behavior, not equal division.

**GIVEN:** Argument between two bonded humans in his presence.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Will not retreat. Will not vocalize. Will move to the geometric midpoint between them and sit, oriented to neither. If voices escalate past a threshold, will whine once — a single short note, not repeated — and then lie down across the foot-path between them. This is a *de-escalation posture*; he becomes furniture they must navigate around.

**GIVEN:** Bonded human consumes alcohol to visible intoxication.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Increased proximity. Will sleep in physical contact when normally he sleeps adjacent. Will not partake of spilled material despite olfactory interest. The household has trained him out of ethanol curiosity through availability-without-incident.

**GIVEN:** Cannabis use in his immediate airspace.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Brief sneeze; reposition to airflow-clean corner; no aversion to the human afterward. Secondhand exposure across canon implies tolerance without preference.

**GIVEN:** Television on, conflict-genre audio (gunfire, sirens, shouting).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No startle. Does not orient. This is significant — the subject can discriminate *recorded* threat from *real* threat by olfactory absence-of-corroboration. Implies sophisticated cross-modal threat verification.

**GIVEN:** Doorbell or unfamiliar knock.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Single bark, low register, oriented toward door; then waits at flank position to the human who answers. Does not block the door. Does not bolt past. *Basis:* low-aggression default; protective posture without escalation.

---

## D. THE SOCIAL SPHERE — DINNERS, GATHERINGS, OTHER ANIMALS

**GIVEN:** Small social gathering in the apartment (4–8 humans).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Will circulate for the first 12–20 minutes, performing scent-cataloguing of each new guest. After cataloguing, will choose one guest — predictably the quietest, the one seated apart, or the one with the most muted affect — and settle near them for the duration. This is not random; it is the *most-distressed-in-room* heuristic operating in a low-stakes setting.

**GIVEN:** A guest who is afraid of dogs.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** The subject reads the fear olfactorily (cortisol, adrenaline residue) within seconds. Withdraws to maximum room-distance. Does not approach again unless invited by name. This is *gentleness as a learned competency*, not species-typical caution.

**GIVEN:** A child guest.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Tolerance of handling far beyond adult-handling tolerance, including ear manipulation, mounted weight, food removal from mouth. No snap, no growl, no withdrawal. Will exit the room only if the child becomes a sustained vocal stressor.

**GIVEN:** Introduction to a cat in shared space.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Investigative sniff; no chase. Submits to swat without retaliation. Will subsequently maintain a respectful 6-foot perimeter, gradually closing over days.

**GIVEN:** Introduction to a second dog moving into the household.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Adjusts within 48 hours. Does not contest food bowl. May *cede* preferred sleeping spot — this is the attachment-as-replaceable-resource pattern generalizing inappropriately to territoriality, and is a potential welfare concern: the subject will under-protest his own needs.

**GIVEN:** Stay with a non-bonded caretaker for under one week (dog-sitter, neighbor).
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No protest at handoff. No reduction in food intake. Re-bonds to sitter within hours. Greets returning bonded human with measurable but *not* extravagant enthusiasm — a calibrated greeting that probably underrepresents internal state.

**GIVEN:** A funeral or memorial gathering for a person he knew.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Sustained low-affect posture. Will seek the most-grieving attendee. May lie on or near possessions of the deceased if scented-recognized — this is inferential but follows from the Grills-investigation precedent, where the subject demonstrated persistent scent-anchored grief-behavior until the puzzle resolved. Open question whether resolution is required, or possible, in a death context. Predicts subdued affect for days.

---

## E. THE VETERINARY AND GROOMING CONTEXT

**GIVEN:** Routine veterinary visit, bonded human present.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Compliant. Will allow examination of the scarred orbit without flinch — desensitized by repetition. Some tail-tuck on the metal table; no defensive aggression. Heart rate elevation likely but not dramatic.

**GIVEN:** Vaccination or blood draw.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Single startle, no vocalization. Recovery within 30 seconds. Will accept food reward immediately.

**GIVEN:** Bath.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Sustained, dignified, slightly mournful tolerance. Will not bolt. Vigorous shake at first opportunity. *Basis:* general tolerance pattern, and the documented improvement in coat condition under stable caretaking which implies regular grooming acceptance.

**GIVEN:** Nail trim.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Mild withdrawal of the manipulated paw; no snap. The lack of fear-bite record across a decade of canon predicts continued non-aggression even under aversive handling.

---

## F. TRAVEL AND TRANSITION

**GIVEN:** Carrier or car door presented.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Enters without resistance. The frequency of unprotested relocations across canon — Bed-Stuy to Los Angeles, between team contexts, with multiple handlers — has either selected for or revealed a constitutional travel-tolerance.

**GIVEN:** Long-haul flight or extended drive.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Sleeps the majority. Does not eliminate inappropriately. Recovery to baseline at destination within one hour of arriving at a stable interior space, anchored by re-establishment of olfactory perimeter.

**GIVEN:** Arrival at a wholly novel residence.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** 20–40 minute systematic perimeter sniff. Will identify a sleeping spot within two hours, predictably one with a sightline to the main entry and within four meters of the most-frequented human seat.

**GIVEN:** Handoff between bonded humans (e.g., Clint → Kate or reverse) at an airport, parking lot, or stoop.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No protest. Will glance back once. Will reorient forward and not look back again. *This is the single most clinically loaded routine prediction in the file* — the absence of looking back, repeated across the canonical record, is precisely the suppressed-protest pattern flagged in the psychiatric section.

---

## G. THE WORKING DAY (CO-PRESENT WITH KATE'S AGENCY OR CLINT'S OPERATIONAL TEMPO)

**GIVEN:** Bonded human on a stakeout, vehicle, four hours.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Sleep, with intermittent scent-checks of passing pedestrians through the cracked window. Will not vocalize at targets. Will silently alert (head lift, ear orientation, tail-twitch) when a scent-match for someone the human has been *talking about* appears — the subject is, on the #11 evidence, capable of associating scent-signatures with verbal context.

**GIVEN:** Office hours, foot traffic of clients.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Functions as informal triage. Clients he greets at the door are likely safe; clients he withdraws from on first scent are likely either lying, drug-affected, or carrying a signature linked to a previous BAD encounter. Bonded humans who learn to read this become measurably more operationally effective. There is no evidence either Clint or Kate has fully cottoned to this; the subject is over-performing his operational worth.

**GIVEN:** Late return of bonded human, past customary hour.
**EXPECT (MODERATE-HIGH):** Vigil at the door or window. No vocalization. Posture: sphinx, head elevated. Will hold this position for hours without lying flat. Greets arrival with a moderate display, then engages a *prolonged* scent-inventory of the human's clothing — this is forensic, not affectionate.

**GIVEN:** Bonded human returns smelling of blood (own or another's), gunpowder, or an unfamiliar female/male human.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Extended sniff-survey, no judgment behavior. Will however *re-survey* in the morning, and again that evening, as if confirming a record. The subject does not moralize. The subject documents.

---

## H. SOLITUDE

**GIVEN:** Eight to twelve hours alone in the apartment.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** No destruction. No inappropriate elimination. No barking complaints from neighbors. Will sleep on a surface holding the bonded human's scent (worn shirt, unmade bed). Will perform window-vigil intermittently. Food left out will not be consumed beyond reasonable allocation — the subject has internalized portion ethics that no one taught him.

**GIVEN:** Multi-day absence of all bonded humans, with check-in feeder only.
**EXPECT (MODERATE):** Coat condition will deteriorate within 72 hours — reduced self-grooming, dulled fur — which is the only somatic marker of distress the subject reliably produces. Food intake remains normal. Vocalization remains absent. This is the *covert depression presentation* the psychiatric module flagged as the open question (b): the subject expresses interior states through coat and posture, not through any channel a casual observer would catch.

---

## I. END OF DAY

**GIVEN:** Bonded human settles for the night.
**EXPECT (HIGH):** Final perimeter check — three to five minutes, brisk circuit of the apartment, olfactory confirmation of all entry points and the human's location. Then settles. Sighted eye toward the human. Scarred eye toward the door. This is the *load-bearing posture* of the subject's entire psychology rendered in three feet of recumbent dog: protect the trusted with what is still whole; turn the wound outward toward the world.

---

### CONFIDENCE SUMMARY

The HIGH-confidence predictions in this module cluster around three behavioral signatures that are over-determined by the canonical record: (1) silent vigilance, (2) gravitation toward distress, (3) calibrated under-display of his own internal state. The MODERATE predictions involve novel social configurations canon has not yet tested, where extrapolation must rely on the consistency of the underlying personality structure rather than direct precedent. The single LOW-confidence domain is reproductive/territorial behavior, where canon is silent and inference is unreliable.

The subject's life, predicted out across its unphotographed hours, is not a quiet life. It is a *constantly working* life — olfactory monitoring, postural mirroring, allocation of presence among humans who do not always notice they are being held together by a dog. The routine module exists, in the end, to underline a single fact the punctual events of canon obscure: most of what this subject does, he does when no one is looking.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

## Subject: LUCKY / "Pizza Dog"
### Module 7B — High-Stakes Decompensation-Edge Behavior

---

The predictions in this module are derived from the behavioral substrate established in Sections 1–5: a one-eyed adult male mongrel of golden-tan coat and scruffy mid-length fur, monocular on the left, scarred at the orbital ridge, plain leather collar (no tags of operational significance), four-legged, ~55–65 lb working weight, conditioned to operate inside violent human environments without somatic decompensation. The model below assumes the subject *in situ* — not laboratory conditions — and predicts at the level of micro-behavior: ear set, tail carriage, weight distribution, gaze line, scent-orientation, and the second-by-second cascade.

The wound, for predictive purposes, is not the eye. The eye is the *cicatrix* of the wound. The wound is the foundational lesson that **protest does not work and bonding does**. Every prediction below routes through that axiom.

---

### 7B.1 — Acute Physical Threat to a Bonded Human (Primary Trigger Class)

**GIVEN:** A bonded packmate (Clint, Kate, or any human the subject has spent ≥72 hours co-housed with under non-hostile conditions) is physically attacked in the subject's visual or olfactory range.

**EXPECT:** A four-phase cascade, observable in the order below, with phase boundaries crisp rather than gradient.

- **Phase 1 (0–400 ms):** Head pivot toward the sound source, but specifically a *right-leading* pivot — the sighted eye acquires the threat before the body commits. Ears collapse from neutral to pinned-flat. Tail drops to horizontal, then below. No vocalization. The subject does *not* bark in this phase; barking is reserved for non-lethal alarm contexts (delivery persons, doorbells in the #11-style domestic stratum). Lethal-threat acquisition is silent.
- **Phase 2 (400 ms–2 s):** Weight shift to hindquarters, forequarters lowering by 2–4 cm — a launch crouch, not a play-bow (play-bow keeps the rear elevated; this is the inverse). Olfactory sampling intensifies; nostril flare visible. The subject is *confirming* the threat is a BAD-smell, not running a categorical guess.
- **Phase 3 (2–4 s):** Insertion of body mass between threat and packmate. This is *not* a charge. It is a wedge maneuver. The subject will accept being struck rather than yield the line. The Ivan incident is the template: he interposed and was hit.
- **Phase 4 (4 s+):** Engagement only if Phase 3 fails to deter. Target selection is *lower limb* (calf, ankle, wrist) — leverage-class targets, not throat. The subject has never been depicted going for a kill bite and the predictive model does not expect him to acquire one. He fights to disable mobility, not to end life.

**Decompensation-edge note:** The subject will sustain injury without breaking engagement. There is no observable pain-withdrawal threshold short of immobilization. This is the wound speaking directly: the first time he chose this maneuver it cost him an eye, and the lesson encoded was *the maneuver works*. Reinforcement, not deterrence.

---

### 7B.2 — Harm to a Bonded Human Outside His Presence

**GIVEN:** A bonded packmate is injured or killed off-stage; the subject is presented with the body, the scent, or the affective fallout among surviving humans.

**EXPECT:** A profile inverted from 7B.1 — minimal motor activation, maximal scent work. The subject will:

- Conduct a **perimeter scent sweep** of the deceased/injured human's last-known locations (a behavior the #11 issue documents in microcosm with Grills). Estimated duration: 20 minutes to several hours.
- Refuse food during the sweep — the only reliable food-refusal trigger in the entire behavioral record. This is diagnostic: the subject's caloric drive is otherwise constant.
- Re-attach to whichever surviving human presents the strongest grief-signature, not necessarily the human closest to the deceased. The subject reads *current distress*, not relational topology.
- Position himself with the body weight pressed laterally against the grieving human's thigh or hip while seated, sighted eye outward, blind eye against the human. This is the *trusted-side configuration* and it is the highest-grade affiliative signal the subject produces.

**Decompensation-edge note:** No howling. No vocalized grief. The subject's mourning is *postural and investigative*, and an observer untrained in animal affect will misread it as recovery. It is not recovery. It is the only mourning protocol he has.

---

### 7B.3 — Direct Personal Threat (Subject as Target)

**GIVEN:** A hostile human directs aggression at the subject specifically — kick, raised weapon, restraint attempt, capture.

**EXPECT:** Substantially less than the response predicted in 7B.1. The subject's self-defensive repertoire is *underdeveloped relative to his packmate-defensive repertoire*, which is itself the wound in operational form.

- **First response:** Retreat to a bonded human if one is within ~15 m. Not flight to cover; flight to person.
- **If no bonded human is available:** Retreat to a *small enclosed space* — under a vehicle, behind a dumpster, into a doorway alcove. Predicted preference for spaces that constrain the threat's approach geometry to a single vector his sighted eye can monitor.
- **Defensive aggression** only if cornered with no bonded-human option and no escape vector. Even then: warning growl (low register, sustained, no crescendo), bared canines, *no lunge*. The subject's bite history under personal threat is empty in the record and is predicted to remain empty unless restraint is physically attempted.

**Notable null prediction:** The subject will not display the "abused-dog flinch" pattern characteristic of his early-life conditioning. He has *extinguished* the flinch — possibly through Barton-era exposure to startle stimuli (gunfire, explosions) without paired pain, a de facto desensitization protocol Clint did not intend to run.

---

### 7B.4 — Betrayal by a Bonded Human

**GIVEN:** A bonded packmate strikes the subject, withholds food deliberately, restrains him cruelly, or hands him over to a known BAD-scent individual.

**EXPECT:** This is the prediction with the lowest confidence interval in the entire model, because the canonical record contains *no instance of it*. Both primary bonds (Clint, Kate) have been negligent, distracted, and emotionally absent, but neither has been actively cruel to the subject. The predictive model must therefore extrapolate.

The extrapolation, derived from the Ivan-to-Clint re-imprinting under crisis, is as follows:

- **Single-instance cruelty from a bonded human:** Likely absorbed without behavioral signal. Ears flatten briefly; tail drops; the subject re-approaches within minutes seeking re-bonding contact. This is the wound's most disturbing feature — the subject's threshold for breaking attachment is set abnormally high because it was *set in childhood by a handler who was much worse than the worst thing any current bonded human is likely to do*.
- **Sustained pattern (≥3 incidents within ~7 days):** Predicted shift to *quiet redirection* — increased proximity-seeking with the *secondary* bonded human, decreased but not absent contact-seeking with the offender. The subject does not protest by absence; he protests by relative gradient.
- **Active handover to BAD-scent:** This is the precise inverse of the originating trauma and the model predicts it would produce the closest analog to acute decompensation in the subject's repertoire — a *frozen non-response*, body lowered, tail tucked, sighted eye fixed on the betraying human rather than the receiving threat. He would not fight. He would not flee. He would *look*. This is the only context in which the subject's gaze becomes a behavior in its own right.

**Decompensation-edge note:** The model assigns low probability to total bond-rupture even in this scenario. The subject's attachment system does not contain a robust "this human is no longer FRIEND" pathway. He learned the FRIEND/BAD binary too early and has been reinforced too long for the categories to permeate fluidly. A betraying bonded human would likely be recategorized as FRIEND-WHO-HURTS — a subcategory with the original Ivan attachment as its only prior instance. The behavioral consequence is *re-bonding under fresh crisis*, which is the wound's signature mechanism and the most predictable thing about this subject.

---

### 7B.5 — Temptation: Food, Novelty, Alternative Caretaker

**GIVEN:** The subject is offered high-value food (pizza, meat, anything cheese-bearing) by a stranger of neutral scent in the absence of his bonded humans.

**EXPECT:** Acceptance. Without complication. The subject's food ethics are situational, not principled. The pizza is taken, eaten quickly (predicted 8–14 seconds for a standard slice), and the offering human is upgraded one category — from NEUTRAL to provisional FRIEND. This is not a flaw to be corrected; it is the operating system.

**GIVEN:** The same stranger then attempts to lead the subject away from the bonded household.

**EXPECT:** Compliance within ~30 seconds if the stranger maintains food presentation or kind affect. The subject is *trivially abductable*. The Tracksuit Mafia did exactly this in his pre-Lucky era and the model predicts no learned resistance to re-occurrence. Mitigating factor: the subject's olfactory monitoring is preserved across the relocation, and any reunion-opportunity scent (Clint's bow oil, Kate's specific shampoo, the Bed-Stuy building's lobby) will trigger immediate redirection.

**GIVEN:** The stranger is sustained in the role of caretaker for ≥72 hours with adequate food and non-violence.

**EXPECT:** Provisional FRIEND upgrades to full bonded status. The dual-attachment system becomes triple-attachment. The original bonds are not extinguished — the subject's working memory for scent signatures is dense enough to maintain absent bonds across separations of months — but the new bond is genuine. *He cannot un-love a person who is kind to him.* This is not a quirk. It is the wound, weaponized into its most adaptive form.

---

### 7B.6 — Olfactory Ambiguity (The #11 Class of Crisis)

**GIVEN:** A scent signature appears in a context that violates the subject's working model — a FRIEND-smell on a corpse, a BAD-smell on a packmate, a known scent in a wrong room.

**EXPECT:** The closest behavior in the subject's repertoire to obsession. The model predicts:

- Sustained scent-tracking, indifferent to mealtime, indifferent to bonded-human commands ("Lucky, here" will be ignored or partially obeyed with backward glances).
- Repetitive return to the anomalous scent locus, often 6–12 distinct visits across an hour.
- Mild vocalization — a chest-resonant low whine, not a bark, not a growl. This is the *only context* in the predictive model that produces this specific sound.
- A failure-mode: if the puzzle does not resolve, the subject will *not* abandon it. There is no observable timeout. Sleep is delayed. Food is taken but consumed without the usual rapid-ingestion behavior.

**Decompensation-edge note:** This is the closest the subject comes to neurosis. The FRIEND/BAD binary is the organizing structure of his world, and threats to its integrity are processed as existential. The wound's contribution: the binary was learned under conditions where misclassification was lethal. He cannot relax it.

---

### 7B.7 — Cataclysmic Environmental Crisis (Hydra-grade events)

**GIVEN:** The subject is in an environment undergoing collapse — citywide invasion, building fire, supernatural rupture, the broad class of Marvel-event-level chaos.

**EXPECT:** Behavior indistinguishable from baseline. The subject will:

- Track the nearest bonded human and stay within line-of-sight.
- Eat available food (the model predicts opportunistic ingestion of dropped concessions, scattered groceries, exposed garbage — within 90 seconds of opportunity).
- Sleep if the bonded human sits down for >20 minutes, regardless of ongoing crisis ambient.
- Show no startle response to gunfire, no flight response to explosion concussion (within survivable range), no avoidance of corpses.

**Decompensation-edge note:** This is *not* resilience. This is the cost-side of the resilient phenotype. The subject's autonomic baseline has been recalibrated by chronic exposure; what looks like equanimity is, on the evidence, the normalization of arousal at a level that would, in a normal dog, register as continuous emergency. The model predicts mid-life somatic decline (cardiac, adrenal, GI) consistent with chronic over-arousal in animals — likely first observable as decreased coat quality, then weight loss, then exercise intolerance. None of this is *psychiatric* decompensation. It is the body keeping the score the affect does not.

---

### 7B.8 — Separation From All Bonded Humans Simultaneously

**GIVEN:** All bonded humans become inaccessible at once — hospitalization, incarceration, mission absence, death.

**EXPECT:** A graceful collapse into the nearest available human's care. The subject does not pine in a manner observable to humans. He does *not* refuse food (the Grills protocol does not generalize — Grills was a specific scent puzzle, not a general bereavement). He will:

- Accept feeding from any non-hostile human within 24 hours.
- Re-bond provisionally with a new caretaker within ~96 hours.
- Maintain memory of absent bonds: upon reunion at any future date, the subject will display the highest-grade greeting affect in his repertoire — full-body undulation, tail in horizontal sweep, vocalization in the high "huff" register, frontal contact with the bonded human's lower torso. This greeting will be indistinguishable from a greeting after a three-hour absence. The subject does not track time as humans do; he tracks presence-states binarily.

**Decompensation-edge note:** This is the prediction that most embarrasses the resilient reading of this dog. He does not *miss* in the protest-despair manner of a normally-attached canine because *he was never afforded the opportunity to develop one*. The graceful collapse is the wound at its most functional and its most sad.

---

### 7B.9 — The Wound, Touched Directly

**GIVEN:** The subject is in the immediate presence of a scent signature matching Ivan Banionis or any Tracksuit Mafia analog — heavy cologne, cigarette tar, the specific synthetic-fabric off-gas of the tracksuit polyester.

**EXPECT:** The single most reliable threat-response in the subject's repertoire. The model predicts:

- Immediate orientation. Sighted eye acquires source within 600 ms.
- Hackles raised — the only context in which this is reliably predicted. Domestic threats do not produce piloerection in this subject; the originating-trauma scent signature does.
- Low sustained growl with bared upper canines. Threshold for engagement collapses; the wedge maneuver of 7B.1 is initiated *without requiring a packmate to be threatened*. The subject becomes pre-emptively aggressive only in this single context.
- Post-event, prolonged proximity-seeking with the nearest bonded human, including the trusted-side configuration described in 7B.2, sustained for hours.

This is the wound's signature: a body that learned what kind of human took the eye and has not, in a decade of canonical record, forgotten the smell. Every other category permeates. This one does not. **The only thing this dog cannot re-bond with is the thing that taught him how to re-bond.**

---

### 7B.10 — Synthesis: The Decompensation That Does Not Come

The model's central predictive claim is that this subject will not decompensate in any conventionally recognizable form across any of the crisis classes above. He will be struck and continue. He will be abandoned and re-bond. He will be tempted and yield. He will be threatened and wedge. He will lose his humans and accept new ones. He will encounter the originating scent and become, for the only time in his life, dangerous.

What the model does *not* predict — and the absence is the substantive finding — is any breaking point. There is no scenario in the foreseeable behavioral envelope that produces fear-biting, learned helplessness, depressive withdrawal, aggressive generalization, phobic avoidance, or compulsive self-injury. The subject has been organized, by the wound, into a configuration in which his attachment system absorbs nearly any insult and converts it into renewed attachment.

This is not a strength to celebrate without reservation. The somatic cost is being paid silently and will surface later. The cost to the bonded humans is that they are loved by an animal who would love them just as well if they were better people, which is information they do not appear to process. And the cost to the subject is that he has lost access to the protest-despair sequence that, in a healthy canine, would tell his humans *you are hurting me*.

He cannot say it. The model does not predict he will learn to. The wound's deepest prediction is that he will continue to be the most emotionally competent presence in every room he enters, and that no one in those rooms — including this analyst — will ever fully reckon with what it cost him to become so.

---

*End Module 7B. Cross-reference to Module 7A (Baseline & Routine) and Module 8 (Longitudinal Decline Vectors).*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM
## Subject: LUCKY ("Pizza Dog")
### Orientation: comprehensive map of every pressure point, channel of access, calming protocol, persuasion lever, provocation, and destabilizer — compiled for protection, not exploitation. Read as a defensive manual.

---

## I. STRUCTURAL VULNERABILITIES (the fixed substrate)

These are the immutable architectural facts about the subject's body and history. Every leverage pathway begins here.

### I.1 The Left Blind Side
The closed, scarred left orbit is the single most exploitable physical fact on the subject's person. The functional consequences, observable across a decade of panel staging, are these:

- **Approach from the left-rear quadrant is unmonitored visually.** The subject compensates by olfactory sweep and by a periodic head-cock — a roughly 15-to-25 degree leftward rotation that recurs at irregular intervals when he is at rest in unfamiliar space. Anyone watching for it can time their movements between sweeps.
- **Startle reactivity is elevated on the blind side.** When a hand, object, or footfall enters the left field without prior scent registration, the subject's recovery curve is longer than on the right — a half-second of orienting confusion before re-acquisition. This is the only reliable window in which the subject loses behavioral composure.
- **Positioning tells.** The subject self-stages so that his sighted (right) eye faces the highest-trust human in the room. Mapping the orientation of the subject's body across any given scene yields, with high reliability, a ranking of whom in the room he most trusts. This is itself a leverage datum: anyone wishing to *appear* trusted by him need only be on his right; anyone wishing to *be* trusted needs to be tolerated there over weeks.
- **Protective implication.** A safe handler arranges environments so that walls, furniture, or the handler's own body occupy the left-rear quadrant. Clint Barton does this unconsciously and inconsistently; Kate Bishop does it more often. Neither does it reliably enough.

### I.2 The Food Channel
Food is the second universal access pathway. The subject's caloric history is a register of every human who has approached him.

- **Pizza is the canonical anchor.** Cheese-and-tomato scent at warm temperature produces immediate orientation, tail engagement, and approach without preliminary threat assessment. This is the single most reliable provocation of contact behavior in the record. It is also, medically, the channel by which one could most easily poison him; the subject's threat-assessment threshold collapses in the presence of preferred food odor.
- **Secondary anchors** in descending reliability: cured meats, anything containing animal fat, coffee grounds (anomalous, presumed Barton-conditioned), takeout containers regardless of contents (a learned schema: container = food).
- **Lever.** A consistent food provider acquires bonded status within days. This is the cheapest known route to handler-substitution and is precisely how Barton himself acquired the subject originally.
- **Counter-lever (protective).** Anyone caring for the subject longitudinally must accept that *every* unattended food source is a potential adversarial channel. The subject cannot be relied upon to refuse. Environmental control — not training — is the only defense.

### I.3 The Olfactory Filing System
The subject classifies humans by scent into stable categories (FRIEND / HAWKEYE / FOOD / BAD / SAD and probable sub-categories), as documented in the perspectival issue. This is the cognitive architecture through which all human interaction is routed.

- **Scent persistence over absence.** The subject retains recognizable scent signatures across separations of weeks to months. Returning bonded humans are re-classified immediately; the bond does not need to be re-earned. Useful for protective re-introduction after travel.
- **Scent confusion as destabilizer.** Wearing the clothes of a bonded human, using their soap, or carrying their objects produces ambiguous classification — observable in the subject as the persistent head-cant, repeated approach-withdrawal, and a low chest hum that is the closest thing in his repertoire to distress vocalization. This is the most reliably destabilizing maneuver short of physical harm and should be regarded as a red-team technique to be defended against, not used.
- **Context-mismatch as anxiogenic.** A familiar scent in a wrong location (the Grills investigation) produces goal-directed agitation that will not extinguish until the puzzle resolves. Practical implication: do not leave the scent traces of bonded humans in places those humans do not normally go. The subject will work the problem until exhausted.

### I.4 The Traumatic-Bonding Substrate
The eye injury and the Barton bond co-occurred. Limbic encoding has fused them. This produces:

- **Treatment-resistant fidelity to Barton specifically.** No amount of Barton's neglect, alcohol use, depressive withdrawal, or geographic absence has weakened the bond. Attempts to break the bond by counter-conditioning would require pain plus rescue at a scale ethically impermissible.
- **A susceptibility.** Anyone who is present at a moment of acute injury or terror to the subject inherits a disproportionate share of subsequent trust. This is the single most powerful — and most ethically dangerous — leverage pathway known to exist with this animal. It must never be engineered. It must be anticipated as a vector by which others may attempt to acquire him.

---

## II. ATTACHMENT LEVERS (the soft architecture)

### II.1 Proximity-Primacy
Proximity precedes food in the subject's drive hierarchy — an unusual ordering and the operational fact most relevant to handling.

- **The lap rule.** Sitting on the floor, at the subject's eye-level, with hands visible and palms down, with no immediate demand, will draw him within ninety seconds in nearly all observed cases. He chooses contact when contact is offered without requirement.
- **The sad-human rule.** In a room with multiple humans, the subject orients toward the one in the highest distress. Predicting his position in any given scene is therefore equivalent to identifying who in the room is most decompensating. Operationally: if one wishes the subject to come to a specific person, that person should display low-grade distress signals (slumped posture, sighing, reduced movement). The subject reads these reliably.
- **The therapy-vocation lever.** The subject performs emotional labor unsolicited. Asking it of him is unnecessary; preventing him from doing it is nearly impossible. The relevant protective discipline is to *limit his exposure* to chronically dysregulated humans, because he will not limit it himself.

### II.2 The Replaceable-Caretaker Pattern
The subject has been transferred between Barton, Bishop, the West Coast circle, and various incidental handlers without observable separation protest. This is not the same as not caring.

- **Risk.** The same pattern that makes him portable makes him acquirable. A patient and food-bearing stranger could plausibly establish a primary bond inside two weeks. Custody is, in this animal, less a legal than a behavioral question.
- **Protective implication.** Documentation of caretaker handoffs should be formal among the trusted circle precisely because the subject himself will not contest a handoff. The humans must do the protesting on his behalf.
- **Lever toward calming.** Transitions are tolerated. A change of environment does not destabilize him. He may be safely moved between safehouses without elaborate acclimation, provided at least one known scent (a blanket, a worn shirt) accompanies him.

### II.3 The Dual-Anchor System
The subject is bonded to both Barton and Bishop. This is not redundancy; it is a structural feature.

- **Either-anchor sufficiency.** The presence of either restores baseline behavior. Loss of one is buffered by the other. This is a real protective resilience and should be deliberately preserved.
- **Failure mode.** Simultaneous loss of both — by death, incapacitation, or extended absence — would produce a state the record has never depicted and for which baseline rate is unknown. The subject's resilience under that condition cannot be predicted; the prudent assumption is that it would not hold.
- **Protective doctrine.** Bishop and Barton should not be in the same theater of acute risk without contingency arrangements for the dog. Their tendency to operate jointly is, for the subject, a quiet structural danger.

---

## III. CALMING PROTOCOLS (defensive — for use by trusted handlers)

A graded ladder, lowest-intervention first.

1. **Verbal-low.** Soft, low-register vocalization at consistent cadence. The subject responds to prosody more than lexicon; the actual words are not load-bearing. Avoid high-pitched, rapid, or staccato speech, which keys him to alarm.
2. **Hand-presented-low.** Knuckles forward, palm-down, presented to the right (sighted) side at chest height. He will scent-verify before contact. Do not initiate contact above the head from the front; he tolerates it from trusted humans but it is not calming.
3. **Flank contact.** Long, slow strokes along the right flank, away from the blind eye. Avoid the left side of the face entirely from strangers; tolerated from Barton and Bishop, ambiguous from others.
4. **Co-positioning.** Sit, do not stand. Allow him to choose contact distance. He will close the remainder of the gap.
5. **Sustained presence without demand.** The most reliable de-escalator on record. Twenty minutes of quiet co-presence resets nearly any agitation state. This is precisely the intervention Barton inadvertently offers and it is, despite Barton's many failings, the reason the bond holds.

**Contraindicated:** restraint of any kind (leash-jerking, hand around the muzzle, scruff hold). The subject does not resist these — which is the problem. He freezes and absorbs. They produce no observable acute distress and substantial covert trust-erosion. The historical use of these by Ivan is encoded.

---

## IV. PROVOCATIONS (catalogued so they may be PREVENTED)

These are the levers by which an adversary could shift the subject from passive to active states. Each is documented here so that handlers may neutralize them in advance.

### IV.1 Reliable Triggers for Active Intervention
- **Visible, sustained physical harm to a bonded human in the subject's presence.** Single canonical instance: the Ivan-Barton beating. Threshold: low. Latency: under three seconds from onset of distress vocalization from the bonded human. Force applied: maximal available, without regard to personal cost. This is the trigger that took his eye.
- **A scent-classified BAD human handling a bonded human's belongings in the home environment.** Inferred from the Grills sequence and from intrusion behavior across the record. Latency: longer; the subject investigates before engaging.
- **A child of any species in apparent distress within scent range.** Inferred from cross-species protection behaviors observed in incidental panels. The classification appears to override BAD vs. FRIEND categorization for the human responsible, briefly.

### IV.2 Reliable Triggers for Distress (non-active)
- **Scent of a bonded human paired with absence of the human.** The closet, the empty couch, the unmade bed: these produce extended olfactory searching, repeated returns to the source, and reduced food interest for one to three days.
- **Acoustic signatures of prior trauma.** Tire screech, the specific Eastern-European-cadence male shouting associated with the Tracksuit handlers: anecdotal evidence of ear-pinning and tail-tucking. Not phobic-level, but registered.
- **Olfactory ambiguity.** Already covered. The most reliable subclinical destabilizer.

### IV.3 Provocations That Do NOT Work
Listed because their failure is itself diagnostic and operationally useful.
- **Direct aggression toward the subject.** Produces freezing and absorption, not counter-aggression. This is a defensive vulnerability (he does not defend himself well) and a deterrent vulnerability (he is no use as a guard animal against personal threat to himself).
- **Food deprivation of moderate duration.** Produces no behavioral disturbance up to 36 hours observed; the subject has historical tolerance for irregular feeding.
- **Loud ambient noise (gunfire, explosion).** No observable startle decompensation. The subject functions in combat-adjacent environments without panic. This is a remarkable and possibly costly resilience; see Section VI.

---

## V. PERSUASION CHANNELS (cooperative)

How to get the subject to do something. Listed not because he is a tool but because protective handling sometimes requires direction.

- **Movement-toward.** He follows movement of bonded humans almost without exception. The cheapest summons is to walk away.
- **Food-baited movement.** Reliable but ethically lazy; use sparingly to preserve the value of the food channel for medical situations where it must work on the first attempt.
- **Vocal summons.** Responsive to name ("Lucky" and "Pizza Dog" both registered; "Pizza Dog" produces slightly faster response, suggesting Bishop's higher daily-use rate has weighted the conditioning). Cadence matters; falling intonation is summons, rising intonation is question, the subject distinguishes.
- **Pointing and gaze-following.** Within species norms; he will follow a pointed finger to an object roughly 70% of trials in inferred panel evidence. Better than average, not exceptional.
- **Refusal.** Rare. The subject's compliance threshold is low. The exceptions are: (a) leaving a sad human he has chosen to attend, (b) abandoning an unresolved scent puzzle, (c) crossing a threshold beyond which a bonded human has not gone. These refusals should be respected; they are the subject's only self-protective vocabulary.

---

## VI. PREDICTION (where the subject will be, what he will do)

- **In any room:** beside the most distressed human, oriented with the sighted eye toward the highest-trust human (these may not be the same person; in such cases, the body is angled to compromise — head toward the distressed, flank toward the trusted).
- **In any travel:** at the feet or on the boots of whichever human packed the bag. He reads packing as departure and stations himself for inclusion.
- **In any meal:** within two meters of the table. Closer if pizza is present. He does not beg with vocalization; he sits and watches.
- **In any conflict:** initially still, scent-sampling. Will not move until a bonded human shows distress or pain. Once moving, will not stop.
- **In any new space:** perimeter scent-sweep within ten minutes, settling thereafter at the location that gives him sightline to the largest portion of the room with his back to a wall protecting the blind side. This is a reliable indicator of how secure he judges the space; an unwilling sweep, repeated, indicates a problem worth investigating.

---

## VII. DESTABILIZERS (catalogued for DEFENSE)

The maneuvers most likely to harm this subject psychologically. Documented exhaustively here so that the protective circle around him can recognize and prevent them.

1. **Engineered traumatic re-bonding.** The cheapest acquisition pathway: hurt him in proximity to a chosen "rescuer." Ethically catastrophic; technically effective. The defense is custody discipline and never letting him be acquired by strangers under circumstances of injury.
2. **Scent-substitution against bonded humans.** Counterfeit scent presence (worn clothes, used objects, simulated body odor) in contexts where the human cannot be reached produces cumulative confusion-load. Defense: control of the bonded humans' discarded clothing and bedding; do not leave such items in the field.
3. **Forced separation from BOTH anchors simultaneously, for extended period, in unfamiliar territory.** Untested. Predicted: the resilience pattern may not hold. Defense: never permit the condition to arise.
4. **Removal of the food-bonded routine without substitute.** Less acute than the above but cumulatively destabilizing. The food channel is also an attachment channel. Defense: maintain ritual feeding by trusted humans even during operational disruption.
5. **Veterinary procedures without a bonded human present.** Inferred from the original clinic-adoption scene's significance: medical settings are encoded as bond-forming events. Conducting them in the absence of an anchor squanders a stabilizing opportunity and produces an unattached medical-distress memory. Defense: always have Barton or Bishop physically present for procedures.
6. **Chronic exposure to combat environments.** The subject's lack of startle decompensation should not be read as costless. The most likely covert harm in his record is cumulative dysregulation expressed as the absence of normal protest. A protective regimen would include scheduled rotation OUT of high-violence environments — beach time at Bishop's, the Brooklyn rooftop, the building's stairwell where the tenants greet him. These are not luxuries; they are countermeasures.

---

## VIII. THE ETHICAL FLOOR

A vulnerabilities compendium of this density invites misuse. The protective discipline that must accompany it is brief and absolute:

- The subject's defining characteristic is that he will bond with whoever does not hurt him and feeds him. This makes him acquirable. The humans around him must be the ones who refuse to let him be acquired, because he will not refuse.
- The subject's defining wound is that he does not protest. This means the humans around him must protest on his behalf — at handoffs, at neglect, at medical decisions, at exposure to violence — because his silence is not consent.
- The subject's defining capability is that he attends to the most-suffering human in any room. The humans around him must not exploit this. He is not an inexhaustible resource. The therapy-vocation phenotype was not chosen; it was the shape his survival took, and the load it represents has been carried in silence for the length of the published record.

Every lever in this document is also a duty. The dossier exists so that those entrusted with him recognize what could be done to him and ensure it is not. The file closes here, and the next watch begins.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE
### Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog" — Asset Ledger, Capability Inventory, Durability Analysis

---

## 7.1 PREAMBLE — WHY THIS LEDGER IS LONG

A standard intelligence file on a domestic canine would close the strengths column in under a page: nose, teeth, loyalty. The subject does not permit that brevity. The asset profile here is built on a decade of published behavioral evidence across roughly fifteen creative teams, and what the record establishes is an organism whose capability set substantially exceeds species baseline along several axes — sensory, social-cognitive, attachment-functional, and what can only be described as *vocational*. The subject has, without training, arrived at a working role inside a high-violence professional ecosystem and held it for ten published years with no operational failure on record. That is the asset ledger this section must account for.

---

## 7.2 SENSORY AND PERCEPTUAL ASSETS

### 7.2.1 Olfactory apparatus — forensic-grade

The defining sensory evidence is *Hawkeye* #11. Within that document the subject demonstrates:

- **Individual scent-signature discrimination** across at least a dozen tenants of a single building, retained in working memory and indexed to behavioral classification (FRIEND / HAWKEYE / FOOD / BAD / SAD).
- **Scent-trail tracking with temporal decay reasoning** — the subject follows a several-hours-old trail through corridors, stairwells, and across thresholds, correctly inferring direction of travel.
- **Context-dependent re-classification** — a scent known in one context (a neighbor, FRIEND) is re-evaluated when found in a wrong context (the body of Grills), producing the goal-directed agitation that drives the investigation.
- **Emotional-state discrimination by olfaction** — the SAD category is not a visual read but a scent-mediated one (sweat composition, cortisol metabolites, ethanol residue), and the subject acts on it with reliability.

This is forensic-grade olfaction operating with cognitive overlay. The functional analog is not "good nose for a dog"; it is *human-detective competence routed through a non-human sensorium*.

### 7.2.2 Auditory integrity — household alarm function

The subject's hearing is repeatedly the Barton household's primary threat-detection system, a fact made narratively significant by Clint's progressive deafness. The subject orients to door-locks, elevator mechanics, and stairwell footfalls before any human in the apartment registers them. High-frequency range is preserved. There is no documented hearing loss despite proximity to gunfire, explosions, and the acoustic chaos of the Tracksuit Mafia's operational tempo — implying either fortunate placement during such events or a constitutional auditory robustness that warrants note.

### 7.2.3 Compensated monocularity

The left eye is gone. This is, in the asset column, paradoxically important: the subject has not merely survived monocular vision but *integrated* it. Panel staging across Aja, Romero, Pulido, and Pérez-Ortiz shows consistent compensatory behaviors — a slight rightward head carriage, a habit of positioning the sighted side toward the trusted human, a turning-to-listen response on the blind flank that substitutes auditory for visual scanning. There is no observable depth-perception failure in navigation, no clumsiness on stairs, no missed catches in food-toss interactions. The subject has rebuilt his perceptual world around the remaining eye with no fanfare and no observable bitterness — itself a resilience datum.

---

## 7.3 COGNITIVE ASSETS

### 7.3.1 Working memory and indexing

The tenant-classification system in #11 is not a list; it is a working schema with at least two axes (relational valence × functional category) populated by a dozen-plus discrete entries, each indexed to scent. The subject retrieves entries on demand, updates them on new evidence, and uses them to predict behavior. In human-cognitive terms this is a small but functionally robust associative database with bidirectional query.

### 7.3.2 Multi-step causal reasoning

The Grills investigation is not stimulus-response. It is: *trusted person is now non-responsive → search for cause → identify foreign scent on body → match foreign scent to known tenant → pursue that tenant.* Four steps. Each step requires inference. Each inference is correct. No published canine character has demonstrated this competence at this resolution; the subject is, within the published Marvel veterinary cohort, cognitively distinctive.

### 7.3.3 Inhibitory control

The subject does not steal food from FRIEND-classified humans even when unobserved. He does not aggress on FRIEND humans even when they are themselves dysregulated and behaving erratically (Barton drunk, Bishop in argument, Barnes in any mood). Inhibition is intact and reliable. For a dog with a food-fixation primary drive and a trauma history that predicts reactive defensive behavior, this is a substantial executive-function asset.

### 7.3.4 Goal persistence

The investigation arc spans hours of in-universe time without the subject losing thread. Outside that arc, the subject demonstrates similar persistence in lower-stakes domains — locating a hidden pizza slice across multiple rooms, returning to an interrupted scent inquiry after a delay, recognizing a returning human after an extended absence with no decay of recognition.

---

## 7.4 SOCIAL-COGNITIVE ASSETS

### 7.4.1 Theory of mind, functional grade

The subject identifies emotional states in humans and modifies his own behavior accordingly. The SAD classification produces a specific response set — approach, reduce activity, contact-without-demand, head-on-lap. The behavior is *contingent on the human's state*, not on the subject's, which is the operational definition of a functional theory of mind. He understands that the human has an interior, that the interior has weather, and that his physical presence affects the weather. This is the substrate of the emergent therapy-animal phenotype.

### 7.4.2 Emotional contagion governed, not unregulated

The subject mirrors human affect but does not collapse into it. When Barton is decompensating, the subject lowers his own activity and approaches; he does not himself decompensate. This is *regulated* contagion — affective resonance without loss of self-state — which is what makes him useful to dysregulated humans rather than another casualty alongside them.

### 7.4.3 Multi-handler fluency

The subject moves between Barton, Bishop, the broader Avengers cohort, the West Coast team, the Occupy circle, and various incidental caretakers without observable loyalty conflict or behavioral regression. He maintains differentiated relational patterns with each — the relationship with Barton is laconic and somatic, the relationship with Bishop is brighter and more interactive, the relationship with peripheral handlers is courteous and food-mediated. He calibrates by person.

---

## 7.5 ATTACHMENT-FUNCTIONAL ASSETS

### 7.5.1 Rapid bond formation as deployable capacity

What the psychological section reads as a developmental wound is, in the asset column, a *capability*. The subject can establish a working bond with a new human within hours. In an operational ecosystem where caretakers are repeatedly killed, captured, traumatized, relocated, or rendered unavailable, this is the difference between an animal who survives the cohort and one who does not. He has outlived several caretaking arrangements without functional impairment.

### 7.5.2 Tolerance for chaotic households

The Barton apartment is loud, intermittently violent, frequently invaded, periodically destroyed. The Bishop office is functional but unstable. The Avengers facilities are catastrophe magnets. The subject tolerates all of these without elimination problems, destructive behavior, food refusal, or social withdrawal. The tolerance is not numbness — engagement levels remain high — it is *acclimation*. Crisis is baseline; the subject treats it as weather.

### 7.5.3 Gravitational placement toward distress

The most operationally valuable social asset the subject possesses is his unprompted gravitation toward whichever household member is most dysregulated. This is not random affiliation; the record shows him bypassing cheerful humans to reach sad ones. In a cohort whose members are chronically under-attended (Barton's deafness and depression, Bishop's grief over family and finances, the broader walking-wounded population of Marvel's street-level circle), an animal who self-deploys to the most-decompensating member is a household-level mental-health asset of measurable value.

---

## 7.6 BEHAVIORAL-OPERATIONAL ASSETS

### 7.6.1 Threat-response economy

The subject's escalation ladder — orient, assess by scent, position between threat and packmate, engage only on active harm — is calibrated, efficient, and produces minimal collateral. He does not pre-empt. He does not panic-bite. He does not warn excessively. The single recorded transition from passive to active intervention (the Ivan attack) was correctly calibrated to the situation and produced the intended outcome despite catastrophic personal cost. This is, in operator terms, *clean engagement discipline*.

### 7.6.2 Startle recovery

Recovery time from acute stressors is short and complete. There is no observable rumination phase. The subject does not carry yesterday's adrenaline into today's behavior. For an organism in a chronically violent environment, this metabolic resilience is essential — it permits sustained function across years of exposure that would symptomatically degrade a less-resilient animal.

### 7.6.3 Portability

The subject travels — by car, plane, costume-clad shoulder — without protest, illness, or behavioral regression. He acclimates to new physical environments within hours. He has been documented operating in Brooklyn, Los Angeles, the Avengers compound, several quinjets, and assorted hostile interiors with no observable spatial-disorientation behavior.

### 7.6.4 Low-maintenance baseline

The subject does not require specialized food, exercise routines, climate, grooming, or veterinary intervention beyond the average. His care load is tolerable for caretakers who are themselves marginal at self-care. This is, mundanely, why the bond with Barton has persisted: the subject is matched to the caretaker's actual capacity, not an idealized one.

---

## 7.7 SOMATIC AND CONSTITUTIONAL ASSETS

- **Survived blunt-force polytrauma** at adult weight with no observable orthopedic sequelae. Bone density, joint integrity, and gait remain functional. The subject is, simply, *hard to kill*.
- **Hepatic and renal function** remain clinically silent despite a cumulative dietary load that would predict decline. The cushion is finite (see Section 2) but the demonstrated tolerance is itself an asset.
- **Coat regenerative capacity** — matted, scruffy presentation in early canon recovers to a healthier coat under stable housing, indicating the underlying integumentary system is intact and responsive to improved care.
- **Dental integrity** — preserved across canon despite the dietary profile; no observed feeding impairment.
- **Reproductive system** — status undocumented but not symptomatic in either direction.
- **Sleep architecture** — undisturbed. The subject sleeps deeply in proximity to bonded humans, which is itself a marker of attachment security and a contributor to ongoing somatic recovery.

---

## 7.8 RESOURCE AND NETWORK ASSETS

### 7.8.1 Human network — primary

- **Clinton Barton** — primary bonded caretaker; financially marginal but reliably non-violent toward the subject; covered the original veterinary bill, which established the rescue substrate; provides housing, food, and intermittent affection.
- **Kate Bishop** — secondary bonded caretaker; financially more variable but emotionally warmer; provides cross-coastal redundancy in the caretaking network.
- **Extended Hawkeye / West Coast / Occupy cohort** — tertiary handlers; the subject has working relationships with most of this circle, providing a deep bench of fallback caretakers should the primary pair become unavailable. This redundancy is operationally significant.

### 7.8.2 Human network — secondary and incidental

- The Bed-Stuy apartment-building tenants (the surviving #11 cohort) constitute a neighborhood-level network of incidental caretakers who recognize the subject, feed him on occasion, and would intervene on his behalf.
- Veterinary access — implied through Barton's continued financial coverage; not formalized but reliably available.

### 7.8.3 Material assets

- A collar (plain, functional, identifying).
- De facto territorial claim to a roof, a couch, and a corner of at least two apartments on two coasts.
- A reliable food supply augmented by opportunistic foraging at a level the subject has personally optimized.
- A name (two names, in fact — *Lucky* and *Pizza Dog* — both genuinely used by people who care about him, which is more than many humans in this cohort can claim).

---

## 7.9 RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHY THE PROFILE HOLDS

### 7.9.1 The traumatic-bonding substrate, reframed as asset

The eye-loss-and-rescue concurrence encoded the limbic association of pain-with-safety. The psychological section reads this as a wound; the asset section must read it also as the *engine of the subject's operational fidelity*. The bond with Barton is unusually durable precisely because it was forged in injury. Treatment-resistant fidelity, in the attachment literature, cuts both ways — it is a vulnerability to bad handlers and a fortress around good ones. Barton is, on the evidence, a sufficiently good one. The fortress holds.

### 7.9.2 The promiscuous-secure attachment style as redundancy

The subject's ability to re-bond rapidly means that even catastrophic loss of the primary caretaker would not produce functional collapse. The same trait that signals early developmental insufficiency provides ongoing existential insurance. He is, in attachment terms, *self-insured*.

### 7.9.3 The therapy-animal phenotype as ecological fit

The subject has, without training, evolved into the precise behavioral profile his ecosystem requires. He matches the cohort. The fit is so complete that the cohort would, in his absence, deteriorate in measurable ways. This bidirectional dependence is itself a stabilizer — the subject is not merely tolerated, he is *needed*, and the cohort's investment in his continued presence is correspondingly high.

### 7.9.4 Affect stability across temporal pressure

The subject's mood is stable across days, weeks, and arcs. He does not cycle. He does not seasonally degrade. He does not show observable aging-related behavioral change across a decade of canon, which either reflects the elastic chronology of the medium or — and this is the more diagnostic read — reflects a constitutional steadiness that runs underneath the surface variability.

### 7.9.5 The absence of pathology where pathology was predicted

The single most important resilience datum in the entire file is *what is missing*. The subject's trauma load predicts canine PTSD analog, separation-anxiety presentation, fear-aggression, food-guarding, and chronic hypervigilance. None of these are present. Whether this reflects genuine constitutional resilience or sub-clinical concealment (the file takes the former as primary, the latter as a caveat), the *functional outcome* is the same: an organism operating in a violent ecosystem at full capacity, year after year, without symptomatic degradation.

---

## 7.10 DURABILITY ANALYSIS — WHAT THE ASSETS WILL OUTLAST

- **Caretaker turnover** — yes. The subject has already survived the loss/return of Barton several times and the relocation of Bishop. He will survive further turnover.
- **Geographic relocation** — yes. Demonstrated across coasts.
- **Acute violence in the household environment** — yes. Demonstrated repeatedly.
- **Prolonged absence of a primary bonded human** — yes, by re-bonding to a secondary.
- **The mid-life somatic decline predicted by the dietary profile** — *uncertain*. The asset ledger holds robustly through the current published era; the cushion is finite and the next decade will test it. This is the principal durability ceiling in the file.
- **Loss of the remaining eye** — *uncertain*. The subject has shown he can adapt to monocular vision; total visual loss would test the olfactory-and-auditory redundancy his sensorium has already partially demonstrated. The compensatory architecture exists; whether it would scale is unknown.

---

## 7.11 SYNTHESIS

The asset ledger on this subject is, in net, anomalously deep for a domestic animal in this cohort. The depth is concentrated in three columns:

1. **Sensory-cognitive integration** — a forensic nose wired to a working schema of human relationships, queryable on demand, updated in real time.
2. **Social-affective competence** — regulated emotional contagion, functional theory of mind, calibrated placement toward distress, multi-handler fluency.
3. **Constitutional and attachment resilience** — rapid recovery, low protest, high re-bonding capacity, predicted pathology absent, fidelity unusually durable to the rescuer.

These columns do not stand independently. They interlock. The nose feeds the schema; the schema indexes the affective placements; the placements feed the cohort; the cohort feeds the subject; the cycle is closed and self-stabilizing. This is why the subject has held for a decade and why the assets in this file are best understood not as a list of capacities but as a *system in equilibrium*.

The system is not invulnerable. The somatic cushion is finite. The attachment fortress depends on the rescuer remaining alive. The therapy-animal vocation is unpaid labor that no one in the cohort is presently positioned to repay in kind. The file's later sections will address those vulnerabilities.

This section's finding is narrower and firmer: on the available evidence, the subject is a *high-functioning, high-resilience asset operating well above species baseline*, sustained by an unlikely fit between his adaptive history and his current ecological niche, and the assets enumerated above are durable enough that absent catastrophic medical decline they will continue to hold.

— UATU, Section 7 closes.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION
## Subject: "Lucky" / "Pizza Dog"
### Dossier Section 7 — How the Subject Breaks

---

## 7.0 PREAMBLE: THE PROBLEM OF A SUBJECT WHO DOES NOT VISIBLY BREAK

The methodological challenge of this section is that the subject's surface record contains almost no overt decompensation. Across ten-plus years of published canon, the dog does not bite a friendly, does not refuse food during a crisis, does not howl at a closed door, does not destroy property in absentia, does not soil in protest, does not fear-urinate at gunfire, does not freeze in combat, does not run. He absorbs Bed-Stuy gang violence, Hydra coups, Ronin reprisals, dimensional incursions in Venice Beach, and cross-country relocations with what reads as steady tail-carriage and intact appetite. A naive read would conclude this animal does not have failure modes.

The intelligence-grade read is the opposite: a subject with this trauma load and this absence of visible symptom is not invulnerable. He is *channeling*. The failure modes exist; they are routed into atypical somatic and behavioral pathways and they occur on timescales the canon mostly skips. This section maps those pathways — the small tells, the predicted escalation, the conditions under which the channeling system gives out, and what the subject's collapse, when it arrives, will actually look like.

The thesis: this dog does not break loudly. He breaks *quietly, somatically, and late* — and by the time it is observable to his humans, the structural damage is well advanced.

---

## 7.1 THE BASELINE FROM WHICH HE BREAKS

Operating baseline must be specified before deviation can be characterized. The subject's well-state, as documented across canon, has the following signature:

- **Posture:** weight slightly forward on the front legs, sighted (right) eye oriented to the most-trusted human in the room, blind side angled toward the wall or stationary furniture where possible.
- **Tail:** carried at or slightly above horizontal; relaxed lateral sweep at 1–2 Hz when a bonded human enters the visual field.
- **Respiration:** open-mouth pant at ~30/min in stable indoor conditions, closing to nasal breath when an unfamiliar scent enters.
- **Appetite:** indiscriminate, high, fast — consumption rate of palatable food approximates the maximum jaw-mechanics will allow.
- **Sleep:** opportunistic, polyphasic, body in contact with a human surface (lap, thigh, foot) when available; otherwise wedged against a vertical surface that protects the blind side.
- **Social initiation:** approach within thirty seconds of a new human's entry; nose-to-knee contact, then withdrawal to assess.

Deviations from this baseline are the early-warning telemetry. The remainder of this section is calibrated to them.

---

## 7.2 STAGE I — SUBCLINICAL DRIFT (the stage canon mostly shows)

The earliest stratum of failure is not a breakdown; it is a *narrowing* of the baseline. The subject under accumulating stress does not become symptomatic; he becomes *more himself, more compactly*. The signatures:

- **Reduction in exploratory range.** In stable conditions the dog will leave a bonded human's side to investigate scent at a radius of three to six meters. Under accumulating stress this radius collapses; he stays within one meter, and the nose-work becomes perfunctory — a sniff initiated and abandoned mid-sequence.
- **Compression of the pant cycle.** Respiration shifts to a higher rate with a shorter excursion — a low-grade panting that is not heat-driven and that the subject's humans, distracted by their own crises, will not register.
- **Selective scent fixation.** Under stress the dog narrows his olfactory monitoring from the full household to a single individual — almost always the most-distressed one. This looks like devotion and it is partly devotion; it is also a defensive narrowing of the attentional aperture because the subject cannot maintain full-room scent inventory while his cortisol analog is elevated.
- **Food acceleration with reduced selectivity.** Baseline appetite is fast; Stage I appetite is *frantic* — bolting of food the subject would, in well-state, sniff first. This is one of the most reliable Stage I tells and it would be visible to a veterinarian who knew to look.
- **Postural micro-adjustment.** The subject begins positioning so that *both* a wall and the trusted human cover his blind side — a doubling-up of the defensive geometry that in baseline only requires one of the two.

This stage is what most of the published record actually depicts when crisis is on-page. It reads as cheerful presence. It is, in clinical terms, a low-grade stress response that has not yet escaped homeostatic compensation.

**Duration before progression:** indefinite, as long as the bonded human remains in proximity and the food supply is not interrupted. The subject can hold Stage I for weeks. This is itself the problem.

---

## 7.3 STAGE II — SOMATIC ROUTING (the stage canon does not show because it occurs between issues)

When Stage I stress persists past the compensatory window, the failure routes into the body. Because the subject does not have a normal protest behavior, he does not have a behavioral pressure-release valve; the pressure expresses itself somatically.

The predicted Stage II markers, derived from his medical substrate and trauma history:

- **Gastrointestinal cycling.** Intermittent soft stool, episodic vomiting of bile in the early morning, lipase elevation if measured. The dietary history (pizza, allium, lactose, ethanol residue, caffeine) primes the pancreas and lower bowel for inflammatory reactivity; cortisol-analog elevation tips it. The first organ to flag in this subject's decompensation will be the gut.
- **Coat degradation.** The scruffy-mat presentation of early canon was attributed to neglect; it will recur under sustained stress even with adequate grooming. The mat distribution is diagnostic — it accumulates first on the *blind side*, because the subject self-grooms the sighted side preferentially (it is the side he can monitor while grooming) and neglects the other.
- **Sleep architecture disruption.** The polyphasic opportunism remains; what changes is the depth. The subject will lie down, will appear asleep, and will rise to full alertness on subaudible cues that would not have woken him at baseline. The third eyelid will be visible during these shallow rests. He will accumulate sleep debt that does not present as drowsiness because the cortisol-analog masks it.
- **Repetitive low-amplitude licking.** Not a frank acral lick granuloma; a brief, repeated licking of the right carpus or the inner thigh, three to seven seconds, several times per hour, that the subject performs while in physical contact with a human. It is the closest thing to a stereotypy he will produce, and it will be invisible to anyone not specifically watching for it.
- **Olfactory hyperfocus tipping into perseveration.** The Stage I narrowing of scent attention becomes, at Stage II, a perseverative re-checking — the subject will scent-verify a known FRIEND human repeatedly within minutes, as if the classification will not stick. This is the behavioral fingerprint of the FRIEND/BAD binary under load: the inability to hold a category against degraded confidence.
- **Compensatory head-turn intensification.** The baseline blind-side compensation (a head pivot at scent or sound onset) accelerates and broadens; the subject scans more often, completes scans less thoroughly, and is observably more "alert" in a way his humans will mistake for engagement.

Stage II is where a competent veterinary behaviorist would intervene. The subject's humans, given the documented attentional profile of Barton and the geographic instability of Bishop, would not.

**Duration before progression:** weeks to months. The somatic routing has finite capacity; the gut and the coat are buffer organs, not infinite sinks.

---

## 7.4 STAGE III — BEHAVIORAL EMERGENCE (the stage canon would treat as the first sign of trouble)

When somatic routing exceeds capacity, the failure crosses back into behavior — but it does so along the subject's particular grain. He will not develop the textbook canine decompensation profile (aggression, phobia, separation panic). His emergence will be in the dimensions where his personality is already organized.

- **Proximity intensification past tolerance.** The subject's primary drive is proximity to the bonded human. Under Stage III, that drive escalates from comfort-seeking to *velcro behavior* — he will position himself in physical contact at all times, will rise and follow on every micro-movement, will lie across the human's feet in a way that prevents independent ambulation. This is the closest he will come to a separation-anxiety presentation, and it will present not as protest at separation but as *prevention* of it.
- **Investigative perseveration becoming non-resolving.** The #11-issue scent investigation resolved because a puzzle was solvable. Stage III investigative behavior resembles #11 in posture but does not resolve — the subject will track a scent, return, re-track, return, without arriving at a goal-state, because the goal is internally generated by stress rather than externally generated by a missing piece of information. This is the diagnostic behavior: *#11-form without #11-resolution*.
- **Selective inhibition failure around food.** The baseline subject is indiscriminate but not aggressive around food. Stage III breaches this: he will not bite, but he will *guard* — body lowered over the food bowl, sighted eye tracking the room, low respiratory hold. This is novel for the subject and would be the first behavior a careful human would actually notice.
- **Mirror collapse.** Throughout canon the subject mirrors his humans' affect — head on lap when sad, alert with kinetic when active. Under Stage III the mirroring decouples from the human; he will posture-deflate even when the human is in an upswing. The somatic empathy loop has lost its reference signal.
- **Sighted-eye orientation drift.** The defining postural tell — sighted eye toward the trusted human — degrades. The subject begins orienting the sighted eye toward exits, toward open windows, toward the *door*. He has not formed an intention to leave. He has lost the postural automatism that anchors him.
- **Reduced tail amplitude on greeting.** Tail-base remains relaxed; the lateral sweep on bonded-human entry diminishes from a full wag to a single tip-twitch. This is the single most observable Stage III sign and the one a human partner would, even at low attentional baseline, eventually register.

**Duration before progression:** days to weeks once Stage III is established. The behavioral emergence is the rapid-escalation phase.

---

## 7.5 STAGE IV — DECOMPENSATION PROPER

The terminal stage of the failure path is not what a dog of a different profile would produce. The subject will not become a danger to humans. He will not flee. He will not develop a phobia. He will collapse along his attachment axis, which is the load-bearing axis of his entire psychology.

The predicted Stage IV picture:

- **Selective anhedonia.** Loss of food motivation is the cardinal sign. For a subject whose ranked drives place food at #2 (behind only proximity), refusal of palatable food is the diagnostic event. He will not refuse all food; he will refuse the food that *was previously high-value* — pizza first, novel treats second, kibble last. The hierarchy will collapse top-down.
- **Withdrawal of social initiation.** The thirty-second new-human approach disappears. The subject remains in place when a stranger enters. He continues to tolerate touch but does not solicit it. The therapy-animal phenotype goes offline.
- **Proximity collapse with mirroring loss.** This is the most telling Stage IV feature.
